# Parity matrix

Java file → ported/partial/not-needed/deferred. Populated per PR from Phase 1.
Pinned Lucene version: **10.5.0** (matches OpenSearch `gradle/libs.versions.toml`).

## lucene-util

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `util/BitUtil.zigZagEncode/Decode` | `lucene-util/src/zigzag.rs` | ported, fixture-verified |
| `Long.toString/parseLong(_, 36)` (generation ↔ base-36 filename suffix) | `lucene-util/src/base36.rs` | ported, round-trip tested |
| `util/FixedBitSet` (dense bitset: get/set/clear/cardinality) | `lucene-util/src/fixed_bit_set.rs` | ported (the subset `.liv` reading needs); no `SparseFixedBitSet` (in-memory-only optimization, not a format difference) |

## lucene-analysis

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `analysis/Analyzer`/`Tokenizer`/`TokenFilter` pipeline shape | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{Token, tokenize, LowerCaseFilter, StopFilter, Analyzer}` | **ported, scoped down.** `Token { term, start_offset, end_offset, position_increment }` is a plain struct standing in for real Lucene's `CharTermAttribute`/`OffsetAttribute`/`PositionIncrementAttribute` trio (no `AttributeSource` reflection machinery). `tokenize()` is a simplified word-boundary tokenizer — split on non-alphanumeric boundaries, keep alphanumeric runs as terms, char offsets — mirroring the *core algorithm* of real `StandardTokenizer`/`WhitespaceTokenizer`, **not** a port of full UAX#29 Unicode Text Segmentation (combining marks, locale word-breaking, complex scripts are out of scope). Note: despite the doc comment calling these "character offsets," `tokenize()` actually emits UTF-8 **byte** offsets (via `char_indices()`); harmless while every fixture/test string was ASCII (byte and char offsets coincide there), but task #64's fixture needed an explicit char-to-byte reconciliation once non-ASCII text was involved — see that row below. `LowerCaseFilter` and `StopFilter` are both ported in full, including `StopFilter`'s position-increment-preservation rule: a removed stopword's own increment is carried onto the next surviving token rather than dropped, so position gaps across query slop (`PhraseQuery`/`SpanNear`) survive stopword removal. `Analyzer::standard(stopwords)` composes tokenizer + lowercase + optional stopwords, standing in for `StandardAnalyzer`. **Deferred**: any `TokenFilter` besides `AsciiFoldingFilter`/`PorterStemFilter`/`SynonymFilter` (see the rows below), plus per-field analyzer configuration. This crate is a standalone, dependency-free crate below both `lucene-index` and `lucene-search` in the workspace graph; `lucene-search/src/query_parser.rs` (task #62) and `lucene-index/src/indexing_chain.rs::invert_documents` (task #63, in-memory-only builder, see that row in the `lucene-index` section) are now its two real consumers; term-vector fixtures still take already-tokenized terms directly. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-analysis/tests/analysis_fixtures.rs` runs real `StandardAnalyzer` with a real stopword set (`fixtures/src/GenAnalysis.java`) over six cases — a stopword mid-sentence, at the very start, at the very end, three consecutive stopwords, an all-stopwords string (empty output), and a mixed-case/punctuation sentence exercising tokenizing, lowercasing, and stopword removal together ("The" is itself a stopword once lowercased) — and asserts this port's `Analyzer` produces byte-identical (term, position_increment, start_offset, end_offset) sequences; all six passed on the first real-Lucene run. |
| `analysis/miscellaneous/ASCIIFoldingFilter` | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{AsciiFoldingFilter, Analyzer::with_ascii_folding}` | **ported (task #64), scoped to a documented character subset, not the full real table.** A fourth `lucene-analysis` filter (alongside `tokenize`/`LowerCaseFilter`/`StopFilter` from task #61), folding each token's `term` to its closest plain-ASCII form. **Covered, itemized**: the full Latin-1 Supplement letter block (U+00C0-U+00DE uppercase / U+00E0-U+00FE lowercase, i.e. À-Þ/à-þ, skipping the `×`/`÷` math symbols at U+00D7/U+00F7), plus a documented Latin Extended-A subset: Polish (Ą/ą, Ć/ć, Ę/ę, Ł/ł, Ń/ń, Ś/ś, Ź/ź, Ż/ż) and Czech/Slovak/Baltic caron forms (Š/š, Č/č, Ž/ž, Ď/ď, Ť/ť, Ň/ň). `Æ`/`æ` and `Œ`/`œ` fold to **two** ASCII characters (`AE`/`ae`, `OE`/`oe` respectively — real Lucene's actual multi-char folding), and `ß` folds to `ss` (real Lucene's actual special case, not "b"/"beta") — both verified against real `ASCIIFoldingFilter` output, not assumed. **Deferred, real follow-on work**: the rest of real Lucene's table (remaining Latin Extended-A/B, Latin Extended Additional such as precomposed Vietnamese, and non-Latin-script folding e.g. fullwidth Latin forms) — a character outside this table passes through **unchanged**, never dropped, never a panic. **Offsets are never adjusted for folding-driven length changes**: folding `æther` → `aether` grows the term from 5 to 6 characters, but `start_offset`/`end_offset` still denote the *original* source text span, matching real Lucene's `ASCIIFoldingFilter`, which never touches `OffsetAttribute`. **Filter-ordering decision**: `Analyzer::with_ascii_folding()` inserts folding *before* lowercasing (tokenize → fold → lowercase → stopwords) — an uppercase accented letter (`É`) folds straight to its ASCII form (`E`) and is lowercased in the same subsequent pass as every other token, and stopword matching (last in the chain) always sees the fully folded-and-lowercased form. Folding is **off by default**: `Analyzer::standard(stopwords)` is unchanged, so `query_parser.rs` (task #62) and `indexing_chain.rs` (task #63) keep their exact prior behavior — callers opt in via the additive `.with_ascii_folding()` builder method. **Verified against real Lucene**: `fixtures/src/GenAnalysis.java` gained two new cases via a hand-built `Analyzer` subclass wiring real `StandardTokenizer` + `ASCIIFoldingFilter` — `fold_only` (fold with no lowercasing, over "café naïve Müller cœur straße") and `fold_then_lower` (the same plus real `LowerCaseFilter`, over "Café Naïve ÉCOLE") — and `crates/lucene-analysis/tests/analysis_fixtures.rs` asserts this port's `AsciiFoldingFilter`/`Analyzer::with_ascii_folding()` produce the same (term, position_increment, offset-span) sequences, both passing on the first real-Lucene run. **Offset-unit reconciliation, done explicitly in the test** (`char_offsets_to_byte_offsets`): real Lucene reports `char`/UTF-16-code-unit offsets, while this crate's `tokenize()` emits UTF-8 byte offsets (see the row above); the test converts real Lucene's char offsets to byte offsets via the fixture's own text before comparing — the same kind of documented byte-vs-codepoint scope call `fuzzy.rs`/`wildcard.rs` already make elsewhere in this port, not a bug introduced here. Unit tests cover: each Latin-1 spot-check (café/naïve/Müller/ñ), the eszett special case, a ligature growing the term's character count while offsets stay put, a plain-ASCII token passing through untouched, mixed diacritic+ASCII in one token, a non-table character (Cyrillic) passing through unchanged, the composed fold-then-lowercase order, and the unchanged no-folding default. Coverage: `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs` 100% lines. |
| `analysis/en/PorterStemFilter` | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{PorterStemFilter, Analyzer::with_stemming}` | **ported in full (task #65) -- all five steps of the classic 1980 Porter algorithm, not a subset.** A fifth `lucene-analysis` filter (alongside `tokenize`/`LowerCaseFilter`/`StopFilter`/`AsciiFoldingFilter`), stemming each token's `term` per Martin Porter's original suffix-stripping algorithm. **Steps ported, itemized**: step 1a (`-sses`->`-ss`, `-ies`->`-i`, `-ss`->`-ss` no-op, else trailing `-s`-> delete); step 1b (`-eed`->`-ee` if `m(stem) > 0`; `-ed`/`-ing` deleted only if the stem contains a vowel, followed by `-at`/`-bl`/`-iz`-append, double-consonant-not-l/s/z-drop, or `m==1`-and-CVC-append cleanup); step 1c (trailing `-y`->`-i` if the stem contains a vowel); step 2, `m(stem) > 0` (the full 20-entry suffix-family table, `-ational`->`-ate` through `-biliti`->`-ble`, tried longest/most-specific-suffix-first exactly as the original paper orders them); step 3, `m(stem) > 0` (`-icate`->`-ic`, `-ative`-> delete, `-alize`->`-al`, `-iciti`->`-ic`, `-ical`->`-ic`, `-ful`/`-ness`-> delete); step 4, `m(stem) > 1` (removes `-al`/`-ance`/`-ence`/`-er`/`-ic`/`-able`/`-ible`/`-ant`/`-ement`/`-ment`/`-ent`/`-ion` (only if the stem ends in `s`/`t`)/`-ou`/`-ism`/`-ate`/`-iti`/`-ous`/`-ive`/`-ize`); step 5a (trailing `-e` deleted if `m(stem) > 1`, or if `m(stem) == 1` and the stem is not CVC); step 5b (a trailing double `-ll` collapses to a single `-l` if `m(word) > 1`). Nothing is deferred within the algorithm itself -- this is the complete classic port. **Domain of definition, explicit**: the algorithm (and real Lucene's own port of it) is defined only over lowercase ASCII alphabetic words; a term with any non-ASCII-alphabetic character or uppercase letter passes through **unchanged**, never a panic -- a non-issue in the normal chain since this filter runs after `LowerCaseFilter`. **Filter-ordering decision**: `Analyzer::with_stemming()` inserts stemming *last* (tokenize -> fold -> lowercase -> stopwords -> stem), matching real Lucene's `EnglishAnalyzer` (its stop set holds unstemmed words like `"the"`, so stopword matching must see pre-stem terms). Off by default -- existing callers unaffected; opt in via the additive `.with_stemming()` builder method. **Verification**: direct unit tests against known Porter-algorithm input/output pairs, not a new Java fixture -- this is a purely algorithmic, non-file-format task (no on-disk bytes to decode), and the test vocabulary is drawn from the algorithm's own canonical worked examples (Porter's 1980 paper's step 2-4 illustration list, e.g. `"relational"`->`"relat"`, `"operator"`->`"oper"`, `"triplicate"`->`"triplic"`), independently traced step-by-step against this implementation rather than guessed. Unit tests cover: step 1a plurals (caresses/ponies/cats/caress), step 1b's `m`/vowel guards including words that must **not** stem (feed/bled/sing all fail their respective conditions and stay unchanged; agreed->agre, plastered->plaster, motoring->motor do stem), the full step 2/3/4 suffix-family table (47 canonical pairs), step 5's final-e/double-l edge cases (`rate` keeps its `e` since `m==1` and it is CVC; `roll` keeps one `l` since `m==1` not `>1`), offsets/position-increment left untouched, non-lowercase-ASCII pass-through (uppercase, accented, empty, digit-only terms), and the composed `Analyzer::with_stemming()` running after `StopFilter`. Coverage: `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs` 99.11% lines. |
| `analysis/synonym/SynonymFilter`/`SynonymGraphFilter` | `lucene-analysis/src/lib.rs::{SynonymFilter, Analyzer::with_synonyms, Analyzer::with_bidirectional_synonyms}` | **ported (task #66), scoped to single-word-to-single-word synonyms only -- not the full `SynonymGraphFilter`.** A fifth `lucene-analysis` filter (alongside `tokenize`/`LowerCaseFilter`/`StopFilter`/`AsciiFoldingFilter`/`PorterStemFilter`), taking a caller-supplied `HashMap<String, Vec<String>>` and, for each token whose term is a map key, injecting one additional token per configured replacement immediately after the original. **Explicit scope boundary**: real `SynonymGraphFilter` also handles multi-word synonym *phrases* (`"New York"` <-> `"NYC"`) via a graph token stream -- legitimately out-of-scope machinery here; this filter only maps one term to one or more single-word replacement terms. **Positional semantics (the core real-Lucene rule mirrored)**: an injected synonym gets `position_increment == 0` and the exact same `start_offset`/`end_offset` as the original -- it occupies the *same position*, an alternative reading of the same span, not a new one, so `PhraseQuery`/`SpanNear` built against either term still aligns with surrounding words. This is the first token in the crate with `position_increment == 0` (every prior token, including `StopFilter`'s carried-over increments, has been `>= 1`). **Bidirectionality is NOT automatic by default**, matching real Lucene's `SynonymMap`: configuring `"quick" -> ["fast"]` does not also expand `"fast"` to `"quick"` through the original `SynonymFilter::apply`/`Analyzer::with_synonyms` entry points -- unchanged and unaffected by the addition below. **Bidirectional expansion (follow-up task, "SynonymFilter bidirectional expansion")**: a second, purely additive opt-in entry point, `SynonymFilter::apply_bidirectional`/`Analyzer::with_bidirectional_synonyms`, mirrors real Lucene's `SynonymMap.Builder(true)` bidirectional construction mode at this filter's same single-word-to-single-word scope: given the same `HashMap<String, Vec<String>>` config, a `key -> [values]` mapping also expands each `value -> key` -- configuring only `"cat" -> ["feline"]` is enough for analyzing `"feline"` to inject `"cat"` too, without the caller configuring both directions. A private helper, `build_bidirectional_map`, builds the combined forward+reverse map once per `apply_bidirectional` call (not re-derived per token) and dedupes so a term already configured in both directions (e.g. `"cat" -> ["feline"]` and `"feline" -> ["cat"]` both present) is never injected twice. **What this does NOT replicate**: transitive closure (if `"cat" -> ["feline"]` and `"feline" -> ["kitty"]` are both configured, this does not infer `"cat" -> ["kitty"]` -- only the direct reverse of each configured pair is added), multi-word synonym phrases, weighted/scored synonyms, and real Lucene's `includeOrig` flag -- the same carve-outs the unidirectional case already states. **Filter-ordering decision**: `Analyzer::with_synonyms()`/`with_bidirectional_synonyms()` both insert synonym expansion *last* (tokenize -> fold -> lowercase -> stopwords -> stem -> synonyms) -- real Lucene's convention is that synonym expansion runs over already-normalized terms, so the caller's map keys are expected to already be lowercased/stemmed; and running after `StopFilter` means a term that is itself a stopword (and thus removed) never gets its synonym expanded, since expanding a term about to be dropped would produce an orphaned synonym token with no corresponding original. Both entry points off by default -- existing callers unaffected; opt in via `.with_synonyms(map)` (unidirectional) or `.with_bidirectional_synonyms(map)` (bidirectional). **Verification approach**: no new Java fixture -- the `position_increment == 0` injection is new Rust-level control flow over an already cross-engine-verified position system (`StopFilter`'s increment mechanics were differentially verified in task #61), not new byte-format decoding, so unit tests are the appropriate tool. Unit tests cover: one configured synonym produces two tokens (original at its own increment, synonym at increment 0); multiple synonyms produce the original plus all of them, all at increment 0; a token with no configured synonym passes through unchanged; synonym expansion is confirmed NOT automatically bidirectional through the original `apply`; injected-token offsets match the original's exactly; composed with `StopFilter` (a stopword's own synonym is never expanded since the stopword is removed first, and a surviving term's synonym is correctly carried through with the right accumulated `position_increment`); composed with `PorterStemFilter` (the synonym map's key matches the *stemmed* form, proving synonyms see post-stemming terms); a forward-only-configured term expanding both ways under `apply_bidirectional`; both-directions-configured producing no duplicate injection; and bidirectional mode composed with both `StopFilter` and `PorterStemFilter`, mirroring the unidirectional composition tests. `cargo test -p lucene-analysis`: 44 lib tests pass (up from 37). Coverage: new code (`apply_bidirectional`, `build_bidirectional_map`, `with_bidirectional_synonyms`) fully exercised by the new tests. |

| `store/DataInput.readString` | `lucene-store/src/data_input.rs::read_string` | ported |
| `codecs/CodecUtil` (header/index-header/footer, CRC-32) | `lucene-store/src/codec_util.rs` | ported, fixture-verified (incl. corrupted-checksum case) |
| `codecs/CodecUtil.retrieveChecksum` (structural-only footer check, no full-file CRC) | `lucene-store/src/codec_util.rs::retrieve_checksum` | ported, unit-tested |
| `store/Directory`, `FSDirectory` (listing + whole-file read) | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::{Directory, FsDirectory}` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified |
| `store/MMapDirectory` | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::MmapDirectory` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified; this crate's only `unsafe` |
| `index/SegmentInfos.getLastCommitGeneration`, `generationFromSegmentsFileName`, `IndexFileNames.fileNameFromGeneration` | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::{last_commit_generation, generation_from_segments_file_name, segments_file_name, read_latest_commit}` | ported, fixture-verified end-to-end (open dir → find latest commit → parse `segments_N`) |
| `store/IndexInput.slice(sliceDescription, offset, length)` / `.clone()` | `lucene-store/src/data_input.rs::SliceInput::slice_input`, `Clone for SliceInput` | **ported.** `slice_input` returns a new `SliceInput` over `[offset, offset+length)` of the parent's own addressing, cursor reset to 0, independent of the parent's and any sibling's file pointer; `Clone` (already derived) gives the same independent-pointer duplicate Java's `clone()` does, since `SliceInput` is just `(&[u8], usize)`. Slicing a slice is supported (offsets are always relative to the callee). `Directory::open` still returns a whole-file buffer rather than lazily paging a real file — that's unchanged and remains fine for this port's read-into-memory/mmap model, since `slice_input` works over either backend's bytes once opened. `crates/lucene-codecs/src/compound_format.rs::open_input` was refactored to return a `SliceInput` via this primitive instead of a hand-rolled `data.get(range)` slice, since it's the same offset/length-into-a-shared-buffer shape and the real caller (segment merging, reading one source segment's sub-range out of a shared `.cfs`) needs an independent cursor, not just a raw byte range. Unit-tested (bounds, zero-length, slice-of-a-slice, interleaved-reads independence) plus a real-on-disk-file test in `directory.rs` |
| `store/DataOutput` (vint/vlong/zlong/string/fixed-width encode) | `lucene-store/src/data_output.rs` | **write path started.** Ported as an in-memory-buffer-only sink (`VecDataOutput`, plus a direct `impl DataOutput for Vec<u8>`); every codec writer built on this (stored fields, field infos, `.si`) still returns an owned `Vec<u8>` rather than targeting `IndexOutput` directly (see the row below for why that's an intentional, low-risk choice, not a gap). Unit-tested by round-tripping every primitive through `DataInput`'s decoders |
| `codecs/CodecUtil.writeHeader/writeIndexHeader/writeFooter` (encode side) | `lucene-store/src/codec_util.rs::{write_header, write_index_header, write_footer}` | ported, unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own `check_header`/`check_index_header`/`check_footer` |
| `store/IndexOutput`/`OutputStreamIndexOutput` (sequential write to a real on-disk file) | `lucene-store/src/index_output.rs::{IndexOutput, FsIndexOutput}` | **ported.** `FsIndexOutput` wraps a real `std::fs::File` (buffered via `BufWriter`), implements `DataOutput` directly, and tracks `getFilePointer()`/`getChecksum()` (running CRC32) like Java's `OutputStreamIndexOutput`. `DataOutput`'s methods stay infallible by signature (matching `VecDataOutput`, which can never fail — making the trait fallible would ripple through every already-committed codec writer for no benefit there): a real file I/O error is latched as a **sticky error** on first failure, every subsequent write becomes a no-op, and the latched error surfaces from `close()`. `close()` flushes to the OS but deliberately does **not** fsync -- durability is `Directory::sync`'s job (next row), matching Java's actual contract that `close()` alone doesn't guarantee durability. The three existing write-path example binaries (`write_stored_fields_fixture`, `write_field_infos_fixture`, `write_segment_info_fixture`) now route their encoded bytes through this real `Directory`/`IndexOutput` instead of `std::fs::write`, and re-running each of their Java verifiers (`VerifyStoredFields`/`VerifyFieldInfos`/`VerifySegmentInfo`) against the resulting files still passes -- proving the primitive produces real, Java-`FSDirectory`-openable files, without needing new Java scaffolding for this slice |
| `store/Directory.createOutput`/`Directory.sync` (real on-disk write + fsync-before-durable contract) | `lucene-store/src/directory.rs::Directory::{create_output, sync}` (shared impl in `index_output.rs`) | **ported** for both `FsDirectory` and `MmapDirectory` (write doesn't need mmap, so both backends share the same real-file logic). `create_output` creates/truncates a file and returns an `FsIndexOutput`; `sync` fsyncs every named file's contents plus, best-effort, the containing directory entry -- mirrors `IndexWriter`'s real requirement to fsync a new segment's files before a `segments_N` commit references them. Unit-tested by round-tripping bytes written through `create_output` back through the existing read-side `Directory::open` (both backends), plus error paths (missing directory, missing file to sync, a write that fails partway through). **Deliberately out of scope for this slice**: `segments_N`/`SegmentInfos.write` (the commit file itself — generation numbers, checksum-of-checksums, atomic rename/publish) is a separate, larger piece with its own commit-lifecycle correctness risks, tracked in its own row below; so is `NativeFSLockFactory` (write-lock acquisition, not needed until concurrent-writer support matters) |

## lucene-codecs

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90LiveDocsFormat` (`.liv` read) | `lucene-codecs/src/live_docs.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter deletion (2 of 5 docs deleted by term, `NoMergePolicy` to keep the segment intact) |
| — `SparseFixedBitSet`/`SparseLiveDocs` in-memory choice | — | not applicable to this port: the on-disk bytes are identical dense bits regardless of Java's in-memory representation choice |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90LiveDocsFormat.writeLiveDocs` | `lucene-codecs/src/live_docs.rs::write` | **write path ported, and genuinely complete for this format** -- unlike every other write-side row in this table, there is no scoped-down subset left to defer. The format itself has no sparse/compressed on-disk variant to omit: `.liv` is always one dense bit array regardless of deletion rate (`SparseFixedBitSet`/`IndexedDISI`-style sparse encodings are Java's in-memory-only choice for `readLiveDocs`, made after the same dense bytes are read off disk -- see the row above), so there's no equivalent of doc-values' "dense only, sparse deferred" or points' "single-leaf only, multi-leaf deferred" caveat here. Real Lucene's `writeBits` copies the input `Bits` in 1024-bit batches via `Bits#applyMask` purely as a performance trick over the generic `Bits` interface; since this port's input is always an already-word-addressable `FixedBitSet`, writing `live_docs.words()` directly produces byte-identical output without needing to replicate that batching. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own reader (`parse`): all-live/no-deletions, some-deleted, a doc count not a multiple of 64 (130 docs, exercising the bitset's partial last-word case), the del-count-mismatch rejection path, and a wrong-segment-id rejection. **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_live_docs_fixture.rs` writes three `.liv` files (`_0`: 5 docs, no deletions; `_1`: 5 docs, 2 deleted; `_2`: 130 docs, 2 deleted including the last doc in the final partial word) and `fixtures/src/VerifyLiveDocs.java` opens each directly through `Lucene90LiveDocsFormat.readLiveDocs` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`SegmentCommitInfo`, no `.si`/`segments_N`/`.fnm` writer needed -- deletions aren't per-field, so unlike every other codec write-side fixture here this one needs no `FieldInfos` at all) and confirms every doc's live/deleted state matches the manifest via real `Bits#get(int)` -- all three segments passed on the first real-Lucene run |
| `codecs/lucene94/Lucene94FieldInfosFormat` (`.fnm` read, incl. `FieldInfo.checkConsistency`) | `lucene-codecs/src/field_infos.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter (7 field shapes + a soft-deletes field introduced by a later DV-update generation) |
| `codecs/lucene94/Lucene94FieldInfosFormat.write` | `lucene-codecs/src/field_infos.rs::write` | **write path ported.** Always emits the current format version (`FORMAT_DOCVALUE_SKIPPER`); does not re-validate `FieldInfo.checkConsistency` on the way in (callers are trusted, matching the parser's own stance), it's exercised via own-reader round-trip unit tests instead. **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_field_infos_fixture.rs` writes an `.fnm` file (8 field shapes: plain indexed, term vectors + payloads + an attribute, numeric doc values with a skip index and a gen, sorted doc values, a point field, a KNN vector field, a soft-deletes field, a parent field) and `fixtures/src/VerifyFieldInfos.java` opens it directly through `Lucene94FieldInfosFormat.read` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`, no `.si` writer needed) and confirms every field's properties match the manifest — passed on the first real-Lucene run |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90NormsFormat` (`.nvm`/`.nvd` read: empty/dense/sparse) | `lucene-codecs/src/norms.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against real per-doc norm values from Lucene's own `NormsProducer`, including a real sparse field (some docs missing it entirely) |
| `codecs/lucene90/IndexedDISI` (sparse doc-id-set: SPARSE/DENSE/ALL blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/indexed_disi.rs` | ported as a **one-shot decode to `Vec<i32>`**, not Java's lazy seekable iterator — see the module doc for why (this port isn't in the hot-path-perf phase yet); jump table and DENSE rank bytes are parsed past but never used, since a full sequential decode doesn't need to skip ahead |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90DocValuesFormat`/`Lucene90DocValuesProducer` (`.dvm`/`.dvd` read, **all five doc-values types**) | `lucene-codecs/src/doc_values.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter: numeric plain-varying dense, numeric GCD-compressed dense, numeric sparse (`IndexedDISI`), binary fixed-length dense, binary variable-length dense (`DirectMonotonicReader`), binary variable-length sparse (`IndexedDISI` + `DirectMonotonicReader`), a SORTED field with repeated values (ordinal reuse + terms dictionary), a SORTED_NUMERIC field with 0-3 values/doc, and a SORTED_SET field with 0-2 values/doc sharing a terms dictionary (both exercising the sparse-via-`IndexedDISI` and multi-value-via-`DirectMonotonicReader`-address-range paths together); per-field doc-values skip indexes are out of scope (`Error::UnsupportedSkipIndex`), as is the varying-bits-per-value block split (`Error::UnsupportedVaryingBpvBlocks`) — see the module doc |
| `util/packed/DirectReader`/`DirectWriter` (bit-packed integer array read + write) | `lucene-codecs/src/direct_reader.rs` | **both directions ported**, as **one generic bit-position formula** each (`get`/`encode`), not Java's thirteen width-specialized `DirectPackedReaderN`/encode-path classes — those exist for JIT monomorphism, a concern this port doesn't have yet. `encode`'s output round-trips through `get` for every `DirectWriter`-supported width (unit-tested); `padding_bytes_needed`/`unsigned_bits_required` (`DirectWriter.paddingBytesNeeded`/`unsignedBitsRequired`) are also ported, needed for wire-compatible writer output even though this port's own bounds-checked `get` never needs the padding itself |
| `util/packed/DirectMonotonicReader`/`DirectMonotonicWriter` (monotonic sequence read/write, blocks of min/avg/bit-packed-delta) | `lucene-codecs/src/direct_monotonic.rs` | **both directions ported.** Read side used by BINARY doc values' variable-length address blocks, SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED_SET's multi-value address ranges, and (structurally, values discarded) by the terms dictionary. Write side (`write`) returns owned `(meta_bytes, data_bytes)` rather than streaming to an `IndexOutput` (no on-disk `IndexOutput` yet); round-trip-tested through the read side for linear, irregular, single-value, and empty sequences, plus one hand-verified case matching Java's exact `flush()` arithmetic |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90DocValuesProducer.TermsDict` (ordinal → term bytes, 64-term LZ4-compressed blocks + prefix compression) | `lucene-codecs/src/terms_dict.rs` | ported as a **decode-once full materialization** (`decode_all_terms` returns every term up front), not Java's lazy seekable `TermsEnum` — the block-address array and reverse index exist purely to support random seeking without a full scan, which a one-shot decode doesn't need; both are parsed structurally (to keep the `.dvm` cursor aligned) but their values are discarded, same trade-off as `IndexedDISI` and stored fields. Noted in passing during the doc-values write-side slice: this file's `cargo llvm-cov` **region** coverage sits at 92.15% (below this project's 95% bar), though its **line** coverage (96.27%, the metric the pre-commit gate actually enforces via `--fail-under-lines`) clears it — pre-existing, not introduced by that slice; worth closing the region gap in a future pass but not gating anything today. |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90NormsConsumer` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/norms.rs::write_single_dense_field` | **write path started -- scoped to exactly one shape: a single norms field, DENSE (every doc `0..maxDoc` has a value, no `IndexedDISI` sparse structure), at most 1 byte per doc** -- the `numDocsWithValue == maxDoc` branch of `addNormsField` feeding `numBytesPerValue`'s `0` (all values equal, `min >= max`, Java's constant-value encoding) and `1` (`Byte.MIN_VALUE..=Byte.MAX_VALUE`) cases only; a range needing 2/4/8 bytes returns `WriteError::RangeTooWide` rather than silently truncating. Returns `(meta_bytes, data_bytes)` — norms have no third (`.dvs`-style) file, unlike doc values. **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing**: sparse fields (`IndexedDISI.writeBitSet`, the `numDocsWithValue != maxDoc` branch), 2/4/8-byte-per-doc widths, and multiple fields in one `.nvm`/`.nvd` pair — all separate future slices. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own existing reader (`parse_meta`/`norm_value`/`check_data_header_footer`): varying signed-byte values, an all-equal-values (constant-encoding) set, the non-dense-input rejection path (`WriteError::NotDense`), and the range-too-wide rejection path (`WriteError::RangeTooWide`). **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_norms_fixture.rs` writes two segments and `fixtures/src/VerifyNorms.java` opens each directly through `Lucene90NormsFormat.normsProducer` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, no `.si`/`.fnm` writer needed), confirming every doc's value matches the manifest via real `NumericDocValues.nextDoc`/`longValue` iteration: `_0` (varying small signed values, the real `bytesPerNorm == 1` path) and `_1` (all-equal values, the `bytesPerNorm == 0` constant path, added from the start per the doc-values write-side review's finding rather than shipping it unverified against real Lucene) — both passed on the first real-Lucene run |
| `codecs/lucene90/IndexedDISI.writeBitSet` (sparse norms/doc-values write side) | — | deferred to Phase 5 (write path), needed once sparse norms/doc-values write support is scoped |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90DocValuesConsumer` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/doc_values.rs::{write_single_dense_numeric_field, write_single_dense_binary_field, write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field, write_single_dense_sorted_field, write_single_dense_sorted_set_field}` | **write path covers four of the five doc-values kinds now (task #77 added BINARY and SORTED_NUMERIC to task #11's original NUMERIC-only write side, task #99 added SORTED, this task adds SORTED_SET) -- all four share the same scope: DENSE only** (every doc `0..maxDoc`/every doc for SORTED_NUMERIC has at least one value, no `IndexedDISI` sparse structure), **plain delta-compressed, no table compression, no varying-bits-per-value blocks.** `write_single_dense_numeric_field`: `bitsPerValue = DirectWriter.unsignedBitsRequired(max - min)`, `gcd` always `1`, the `min >= max` (all-equal) case handled as `bitsPerValue = 0` constant encoding, matching Java. `write_single_dense_binary_field`: fixed-length (`ordinal * length` indexing) and variable-length (a `direct_monotonic::write`-backed end-offset array, `block_shift = 0`, same simplicity-over-ratio choice `term_vectors.rs`/`stored_fields.rs`'s own monotonic writers already made) — an empty-length value is a present value, not "no value". `write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field`: flattens every doc's values into one shared array (reusing the NUMERIC-entry encoder verbatim via the newly-extracted `write_dense_numeric_entry_body` helper) plus a per-doc address range, **except** when every doc has exactly one value, where it must (not may) omit the address array entirely to match what `read_sorted_numeric_entry` infers from `num_docs_with_field == numeric.num_values` — that equality isn't a stored flag, so writing addresses when it holds would desync the two sides. All three functions return `(meta_bytes, data_bytes, skip_index_bytes)`, same shape, and always emit a valid (if empty) `.dvs` skip-index file. **SORTED now has a write side too (this task)**: `write_single_dense_sorted_field` builds the sorted, deduplicated distinct-value dictionary from the field's raw per-doc bytes (`Vec<Vec<u8>>` in, `sort_unstable`+`dedup`), maps each doc to its term's ordinal (written as a plain dense NUMERIC entry via the same `write_dense_numeric_entry_body` the other three functions share — matches real Lucene's `doAddSortedField`, which always wraps a `SortedDocValues` as a singleton `SortedNumericDocValues` and so never needs an address array), then writes the dictionary itself via a new `write_terms_dict` helper — a from-scratch port of `Lucene90DocValuesConsumer.addTermsDict`/`writeTermsIndex` (64-term LZ4-compressed prefix-compressed blocks, a `DirectMonotonicWriter`-backed block-address array, and the coarser every-1024th-ordinal reverse index with `StringHelper.sortKeyLength`-style disambiguating prefixes) that real Lucene shares byte-for-byte between `addSortedField` and `addSortedSetField`, so it's already positioned to serve a future SORTED_SET writer unchanged. `write_terms_dict` uses `lz4::compress` (no preset-dictionary variant, unlike real Lucene's `compressWithDictionary`) on each block's prefix-compressed body alone rather than the first term acting as a preset dictionary — still format-compatible, since the decompressor only ever *permits* back-references into the dictionary region, never requires them, and the dictionary bytes are already present verbatim right before the compressed body starts (see `write_terms_dict`'s own doc comment). Both writer's `DirectMonotonicWriter` block shift is fixed at `0` (real Lucene always uses `16`), the same simplicity-over-compression-ratio choice `write_single_dense_binary_field`'s address array already made — the format stores `block_shift` per-field, so any value round-trips correctly through this port's own reader. **SORTED_SET now has a write side too (this task)**: `write_single_dense_sorted_set_field` builds the dictionary from every value of every doc (not one value per doc, since a doc can carry more than one), sorted and deduped the same way `write_single_dense_sorted_field` does, then writes each doc's ordinals following `write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field`'s exact collapse rule: when every doc ends up with exactly one distinct value it writes a plain `SortedEntry` (`multiValued = 0` flag byte, per-doc ordinal via `write_dense_numeric_entry_body`, no address array), otherwise a true multi-valued form (`multiValued = 1`, flattened ordinals plus a `direct_monotonic`-backed address-range array), matching what `read_sorted_set_entry` actually checks (the `multiValued` flag byte, not a count equality like SORTED_NUMERIC's read side uses). The dictionary itself goes through the same `write_terms_dict` helper, unchanged. Docs with zero values are rejected with `WriteError::EmptyMultiValuedDoc`, same contract as SORTED_NUMERIC. **Explicitly still deferred for the three kinds that do have a write side** (see the module's own doc comments): sparse fields (`IndexedDISI`-backed docs-with-value), GCD compression, table compression (`uniqueValues`-driven ordinal remapping), the varying-bits-per-value block split (`doBlocks`), per-field doc-values skip indexes (`writeSkipIndex`/`.dvs` content), and multiple fields in one `.dvm`/`.dvd`/`.dvs` triple. **Now wired into `IndexWriter::commit()` for all five DocValuesTypes -- NUMERIC, BINARY, SORTED, SORTED_NUMERIC, and SORTED_SET** (SORTED wiring added by task #99, SORTED_SET wiring by the following task, BINARY/SORTED_NUMERIC wiring added by this task): `IndexWriter::set_doc_values_field(Some(field_name))` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) opts a writer into calling `write_single_dense_numeric_field`/`write_single_dense_binary_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_set_field` (dispatched on `DocValuesFieldConfig::doc_values_type`, cached at `set_doc_values_field` time) for exactly one field of every segment `commit()` flushes. NUMERIC sources per-doc `i64` values from `FieldValue::Int`/`FieldValue::Long`; BINARY sources per-doc raw bytes from `FieldValue::String` (UTF-8 bytes) or `FieldValue::Binary`, one value per doc, via the new `build_binary_doc_values_output` (same accepted-value shape as SORTED, but no terms dictionary/dedup/ordinals -- BINARY stores every doc's bytes verbatim); SORTED sources per-doc raw bytes the same way via `build_sorted_doc_values_output`; SORTED_NUMERIC sources per doc *every* `StoredField` entry carrying that field's number as `FieldValue::Int`/`FieldValue::Long` (a doc opts into multiple values by repeating the field), via the new `build_sorted_numeric_doc_values_output`; SORTED_SET sources per doc *every* `StoredField` entry carrying that field's number as raw bytes (same repeated-field convention, real Lucene's own `SortedSetDocValuesField`/`SortedNumericDocValuesField` convention), via `build_sorted_set_doc_values_output`. All five are dense-only: every pending doc must carry at least one value for the field or the whole `commit()` fails atomically with `Error::MissingDenseDocValue`; a wrong-typed value fails it with `Error::NonNumericDocValue` (NUMERIC/SORTED_NUMERIC) or `Error::NonBinaryDocValue` (BINARY/SORTED/SORTED_SET) — same "atomic, not best-effort" contract `set_postings_field`/`set_term_vector_field` don't have (there is no sparse/missing-value doc-values shape to fall back to). **This task is IndexWriter wiring only, not new codec logic**: `write_single_dense_binary_field`/`write_single_dense_sorted_numeric_field` themselves (the on-disk byte encoding) were already implemented and already had real-Lucene fixture verification from an earlier task (see the `write_doc_values_fixture.rs`/`VerifyDocValues.java` paragraph below, segments `_3`-`_6`) -- this task only adds the `IndexWriter::set_doc_values_field`/`build_doc_values_output` call sites and `IndexWriter`-level tests (add_document/commit/read-back through the existing reader) for those two already-verified write functions; no new real-Lucene fixture was added by this task. **Merge-policy interaction, applied proactively from the postings/term-vector features' own review findings**: `execute_merge`/`merge_stored_only_segments` have no `.dvd`/`.dvm`/`.dvs` awareness either, so `segment_stats()` also excludes any segment whose `.si` lists a `.dvd` file from `find_merges`' candidate pool, covered by `segments_with_doc_values_are_never_automatically_merged_away`. **Postings + term vectors + doc values together, tested and found to work correctly**: all three setters can be configured at once (to different fields in the same commit) -- each builds its own in-memory output before `dir` is touched, and each `.si`-patching helper reads back whatever the others have already written rather than clobbering it, so a segment ends up with all ten files correctly listed; covered by `postings_term_vectors_and_doc_values_configured_together_all_write_correctly`. Required end-to-end proof: `commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_numeric_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_binary_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_sorted_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_sorted_numeric_values_for_multiple_docs`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_writes_readable_sorted_set_values_for_multiple_docs` (`lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) add documents via `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` and read the written `.dvm`/`.dvd` back via the existing unmodified `lucene_codecs::doc_values::{parse_meta, numeric_value, binary_value, sorted_ord, sorted_numeric_values}`/`terms_dict::decode_all_terms`, asserting the exact per-document values (SORTED/SORTED_SET: resolved ordinal(s) -> term bytes) come back; `commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_non_binary_sorted_value`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_non_binary_binary_value` cover `Error::NonBinaryDocValue`, and `commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_non_numeric_sorted_numeric_value`/`commit_with_doc_values_field_rejects_doc_with_no_sorted_numeric_values` cover `Error::NonNumericDocValue`/`Error::MissingDenseDocValue` for the SORTED_NUMERIC wiring added by this task. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own existing, unmodified reader (`parse_meta`/`numeric_value`/`binary_value`/`sorted_numeric_values`/`sorted_ord`/`terms_dict::decode_all_terms`/`check_data_header_footer`): NUMERIC -- a mixed-magnitude value set, an all-equal-values (constant-encoding) set, negative/large values, and the non-dense-input rejection path (`WriteError::NotDense`); BINARY -- fixed-length, variable-length (including an empty-string value), and the non-dense-input rejection path; SORTED_NUMERIC -- varying per-doc value counts (1-3 values/doc), the all-single-valued collapse case (confirms no address array gets written), the all-same-value case (confirms the flattened array still gets constant-value encoding), and the empty-per-doc-value rejection path (`WriteError::EmptyMultiValuedDoc`); SORTED (task #99) -- a small dictionary with repeated values (confirms dedup + ordinal reuse), an all-docs-share-one-value set (confirms constant-ordinal encoding), an empty-`Vec<u8>` value (a present, distinct value, not "no value"), a 300-distinct-term dictionary reversed into descending input order (exercises 4 full + 1 partial 64-term LZ4 block; only the first, `ord == 0` reverse-index sample fires at this size), a separate 2200-distinct-term dictionary that crosses two 1024-ordinal reverse-index sample boundaries (exercising both the `sampled_previous` capture and a non-first sample's `common_prefix_len` computation, which the 300-term case doesn't reach), and the non-dense-input rejection path; SORTED_SET (this task) -- a small dictionary shared across docs with varying, overlapping value sets, an all-docs-single-value set (confirms the collapse to a plain `SortedEntry` with no address array), varying per-doc value counts (1-3 values/doc), intra-doc duplicate raw values collapsing to one ordinal reference per doc, a 2200-distinct-term dictionary reversed into descending input order that crosses many 64-term LZ4 blocks and two non-trivial 1024-ordinal reverse-index sample boundaries (matching SORTED's own large-dictionary term count -- a smaller count such as 2000 only reaches the first non-trivial sample, never the second), the empty-per-doc-value rejection path (`WriteError::EmptyMultiValuedDoc`), and the non-dense-input rejection path. **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction, all five DocValuesTypes now (task #11 covered NUMERIC only; this task extends to BINARY/SORTED_NUMERIC/SORTED/SORTED_SET)**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_doc_values_fixture.rs` writes **ten** segments and `fixtures/src/VerifyDocValues.java` opens each directly through `Lucene90DocValuesFormat.fieldsProducer` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, no `.si`/`.fnm` writer needed), dispatching per segment on a `<segment>.type` manifest key to the matching production-facing read API -- `NumericDocValues`, `BinaryDocValues`, `SortedNumericDocValues`, `SortedDocValues`, or `SortedSetDocValues` -- and confirming every doc's value(s) match the manifest: `_0`/`_1`/`_2` are the original NUMERIC segments (mixed values, the min-shift-drop regression case, and the all-equal constant-encoding case); `_3`/`_4` are BINARY (fixed-length direct addressing, and variable-length including an empty value via the `DirectMonotonicReader` address block); `_5`/`_6` are SORTED_NUMERIC (every doc exactly one value, the address-array-collapse case, and 1-3 values/doc forcing the real address-range array); `_7` is SORTED (repeated terms over a 3-term dictionary, exercising both the ordinal decode and the terms-dict decode); `_8`/`_9` are SORTED_SET (every doc one distinct value, the `multiValued = false` collapse case, and 1-2 distinct values/doc sharing a dictionary including a doc whose raw values dedup to one ordinal). All ten passed on the first real-Lucene run. **Scope note**: `_7`'s SORTED and `_8`/`_9`'s SORTED_SET dictionaries are deliberately small (3 terms), so this real-Lucene verification exercises `write_terms_dict`'s single-64-term-block path only -- it does **not** reach the multi-LZ4-block / multi-1024-ordinal-reverse-index-sample paths a large dictionary forces (those remain covered only by the 2200-term unit tests against this port's own reader, described above; no fixture has yet forced real Lucene to open a multi-block dictionary this port wrote). |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90CompoundFormat`/`Lucene90CompoundReader` (`.cfs`/`.cfe` read) | `lucene-codecs/src/compound_format.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real `useCompoundFile=true` IndexWriter segment (12 packed sub-files); preserves Java's exact-version cross-check between `.cfs`/`.cfe` and the total-length-vs-entries-table sanity check |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90CompoundFormat.write` | `lucene-codecs/src/compound_format.rs::write` | **write path ported**, given already-written sub-files as `(stripped_id, complete_bytes)` pairs -- each sub-file must already be a complete standalone codec file (its own `IndexHeader` sharing the segment's id, a body, and its own `Footer`), exactly what this port's other write-side modules (`field_infos::write`, `stored_fields::write_best_speed`, etc.) already produce, so no new file-on-disk plumbing was needed to compose them. Verified precisely against Java rather than assumed simple: `Lucene90CompoundFormat.writeCompoundFile` isn't a bare concatenation -- it (1) packs sub-files smallest-first (`Comparator.comparingLong(length)`), (2) pads each sub-file's start offset up to a 64-byte boundary, and (3) "verifies and copies" each sub-file's header (checking the object id matches) then re-derives its footer from the *verified* checksum rather than copying the footer bytes outright -- but since that checksum is definitionally the value already stored in the sub-file's own footer, the net result is byte-identical to a verified verbatim copy, which is what this port does (validate header id + footer checksum, then copy the whole sub-file). No per-sub-file checksumming beyond that verification step; the `.cfs` file's own footer covers the whole packed blob via a single CRC, same as every other framed format in this port. Unit-tested by round-tripping through this port's own existing reader (`parse_entries`/`check_data_header_footer`/`open_input`) with three differently-sized/differently-codec-named sub-files, confirming ascending-size ordering, 64-byte-aligned offsets, and byte-for-byte sub-file recovery, plus rejection of a wrong segment id, a bad magic number, and a corrupt footer checksum. **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_compound_format_fixture.rs` packs a `.fnm` (`field_infos::write`) and a `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` triple (`stored_fields::write_best_speed`) -- four distinct sub-files -- into a `_0.cfs`/`_0.cfe` pair, and `fixtures/src/VerifyCompoundFormat.java` opens it through real `Lucene90CompoundFormat.getCompoundReader` with a hand-built `SegmentInfo`, confirms the sub-file list and lengths, then re-decodes the `.fnm` through real `Lucene94FieldInfosFormat` and the `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` triple through real `Lucene90StoredFieldsFormat` -- both read *through* the compound reader, not the raw sub-file bytes directly, so a byte-offset bug would fail this check even if the entries table alone looked correct. Passed on the first real-Lucene run. **Wired into the write path (task #38):** `lucene-index/src/segment_writer.rs::flush_stored_only_segment` now actually calls this `write` function when its caller passes `use_compound_file: true`, packing a flushed segment's `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm` into `<name>.cfs`/`.cfe` and setting `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file` accordingly, instead of leaving this codec's write half unreferenced by any writer. See that row below for the wiring's own tests. |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90StoredFieldsFormat`/`Lucene90CompressingStoredFieldsReader`/`FieldsIndexReader` (`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` read, **both `Mode.BEST_SPEED` and `Mode.BEST_COMPRESSION`**) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter for both modes: BEST_SPEED (6 docs, one field of each of the 6 stored-field types, varying lengths so the chunk uses the bulk multi-doc framing) and BEST_COMPRESSION (same shape, forced via `Lucene104Codec.Mode.BEST_COMPRESSION`, with a long repeated-text field so the DEFLATE dictionary + multi-sub-block path is actually exercised); the mode is detected from the `.fdt` data codec name itself (`...FastData` vs `...HighData`), and `chunk_size` is read from `.fdm` rather than hardcoded, since BEST_COMPRESSION's is ~480KB vs BEST_SPEED's ~80KB |
| `util/compress/LZ4.decompress`/`LZ4.compressWithDictionary` | `lucene-codecs/src/lz4.rs` | decompress ported (read-only, as before) **and a real compressor is now ported** (`lz4::compress`): a scoped-down port of `compressWithDictionary` with a zero-length dictionary only (preset-dictionary compression is a separate, larger piece -- cross-block dictionary reuse -- and remains unported; `decompress`'s dictionary *read* support is unaffected) and always using the simpler `FastCompressionHashTable` match-finding strategy (a single last-occurrence-per-hash table with a fixed hash-table size) rather than `HighCompressionHashTable`'s hash-chain "try a better match" search (`compressHC`, unported) -- every match this compressor emits is a real, verified back-reference within `MAX_DISTANCE`, just not necessarily the longest one available at each position the way Lucene's own search would find. Verified both by round-trip through this port's own `decompress` (empty input, single byte, below-match-threshold-length, highly repetitive input, pseudo-random incompressible input, matches at the very start/end, and long input forcing the extended-length continuation encoding) and cross-engine (see the `stored_fields.rs::write_best_speed` row below) |
| `codecs/lucene90/LZ4WithPresetDictCompressionMode` (dictionary + fixed-size sub-blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::decompress_unit` | ported as an eager full decode (no partial/lazy read path — this port hands back a materialized `Document`, not a streaming reader); every unit's *compressed*-length vint (the dictionary's, then each block's) is batched up front in this format, before any of the actual compressed bytes -- they exist in Java only to support seeking without decompressing everything before it, so they're read here to keep the cursor aligned and discarded |
| `codecs/lucene90/DeflateWithPresetDictCompressionMode` (raw DEFLATE, dictionary + fixed-size sub-blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/deflate.rs` | decode ported as an eager full decode, same shape as the LZ4 sibling but a real semantic difference caught by a real fixture: DEFLATE isn't self-terminating from an output-length count alone, and (unlike LZ4) each unit's compressed-length vint sits **immediately before its own compressed bytes**, not batched up front -- getting this backwards (by over-generalizing from the LZ4 format) produced a `MalformedVarint` against real Lucene bytes, caught and fixed before commit. Built on `miniz_oxide::inflate::core`'s low-level API (raw deflate, no zlib header/Adler-32) rather than its `decompress_to_vec` convenience wrappers, which don't support a preset dictionary; the preset-dictionary trick is the same one `lz4::decompress` uses -- pre-write the dictionary bytes into the output buffer before `d_off` and let back-references look behind it. **A real DEFLATE compressor is now ported too** (`deflate::compress`): unlike LZ4 (no compress-capable crate was already a dependency, so this port hand-wrote a real greedy-match encoder), `miniz_oxide` -- already a dependency for the decode side -- exposes `miniz_oxide::deflate::compress_to_vec`, a real, already-vetted raw-DEFLATE encoder (no zlib wrapper to strip; that's the sibling `compress_to_vec_zlib`), so this port reuses it directly at level 6 rather than hand-writing Huffman+LZ77 from scratch -- only a *correctly decodable* stream is required, not byte-identical output to Java's own `Deflater`. Fixed a real latent bug while wiring this up: `decompress`'s `decompressed_len == 0` fast path returned without consuming `compressed_len` bytes from the shared reader, silently desyncing every subsequent unit in a chunk whenever a dictionary (or sub-block) happens to be zero-length but still has nonzero *compressed* bytes on the wire (a real DEFLATE stream, even of empty content, still emits a final-block marker) -- caught by `write_best_compression`'s own round-trip tests, not a real-Lucene fixture, but the same bug could in principle have hit a real BEST_COMPRESSION file whose dictionary happens to size out to 0 bytes |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/StoredFieldsInts` (bulk per-doc field-count/length arrays) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::read_bulk_ints`/`write_bulk_ints` | **both directions ported**, `Mode.BEST_SPEED` only for the write side so far. Read: exact on-disk transposed-block layout preserved (values decode identically to Java's SIMD-shaped bulk reader), decoded via a plain per-value loop rather than replicating the bulk/SIMD machinery itself. Write: **scalar-tail encoding only** (correct for `values.len() < 128`; the 128-value transposed-block path Java's bulk writer produces for larger chunks isn't implemented yet, so `write_best_speed` asserts chunks stay under that) |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/Lucene90CompressingStoredFieldsWriter` (write side), `Mode.BEST_SPEED` (LZ4) only | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::write_best_speed` | **write path started — first slice of Phase 5, since updated with a real compressor.** Every doc still goes into one single, un-sliced, zero-dictionary chunk (no dictionary/sub-block splitting, no multi-chunk-by-size flush heuristics -- that part of the real writer's behavior remains out of scope) but the chunk's payload is now compressed with **real LZ4 back-reference matching** (`crate::lz4::compress`, see that row above) rather than the original `encode_literal_lz4` literal-only stub -- the empty zero-length dictionary unit that precedes it is still emitted via `encode_literal_lz4` since a real compressor over zero bytes degenerates to the same single token. Numeric field encodes (`write_zint`/`write_zfloat_full`/`write_tlong_full`/`write_zdouble_full`) still always emit the full/worst-case encoding rather than Java's shortest-of-several choice (still correct, just not size-optimal). **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction** (the reverse of this repo's usual differential-testing pattern): `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_stored_fields_fixture.rs` writes a `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` triple -- now including a field whose value is a phrase repeated 50 times, specifically to prove genuine compression (the resulting `.fdt` is ~222 bytes for a doc set whose one repeated field alone is 2250 bytes, well under a literal-wrapped size) -- and `fixtures/src/VerifyStoredFields.java` opens it directly through `Lucene90StoredFieldsFormat.fieldsReader` (with a hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, so this slice doesn't also need `.si`/`.fnm` writers) and confirms every document's fields, including the repeated-phrase one, match byte-for-byte -- passed on the first real-Lucene run after the compressor was wired in |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/Lucene90CompressingStoredFieldsWriter` (write side), `Mode.BEST_COMPRESSION` (DEFLATE) | `lucene-codecs/src/stored_fields.rs::write_best_compression` | **write path ported**, sharing `write_best_speed`'s single-chunk/`docs.len() < 128` scope and `.fdx`/`.fdm` assembly (factored into a shared `write_index_and_meta` helper -- both modes produce an identical index/meta shape, differing only in the recorded `chunkSize`), but with its own `.fdt` payload framing since the two modes' compression-unit shapes genuinely differ (BEST_SPEED: one zero-dictionary LZ4 unit; BEST_COMPRESSION: a dictionary prefix plus several fixed-size DEFLATE sub-blocks, real Lucene's own `dictLength = len/(NUM_SUB_BLOCKS*DICT_SIZE_FACTOR)`/`blockLength = ceil((len-dictLength)/NUM_SUB_BLOCKS)` sizing formula reused verbatim, `NUM_SUB_BLOCKS=10`/`DICT_SIZE_FACTOR=6`) -- sharing one function across both would have needed a mode-branch threaded through the framing itself, so two functions sharing only the common suffix was the more readable split. Each sub-block (and the dictionary prefix) is compressed independently via `deflate::compress` with no cross-unit back-referencing (`miniz_oxide` has no preset-dictionary compress API) -- still a valid decode per `decompress_unit`'s contract, just a smaller compression ratio than real Lucene's writer, not a correctness gap. **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_stored_fields_fixture.rs` now writes *two* segments, `_0` (BEST_SPEED, unchanged) and `_1` (BEST_COMPRESSION, one field repeating a phrase ~2000 times, ~90KB, forcing a real dictionary plus several sub-blocks rather than one trivial unit), and `fixtures/src/VerifyStoredFields.java` was extended to loop over both segments (a `segments=_0,_1` manifest key, each with its own `<seg>.mode` attribute value) -- both pass against real Lucene on the same run |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90TermVectorsFormat`/`Lucene90CompressingTermVectorsReader` (`.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` read) | `lucene-codecs/src/term_vectors.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter (a repeated-term field with positions/offsets/payloads on some occurrences but not others, a multi-field doc, and a doc with no term vectors at all); positions/offsets reset to a fresh delta chain at each **term's** first occurrence rather than one chain per field (reverse-engineered from the reader's exact loop bounds, not its doc comment — see the module doc); the LZ4 unit's term-suffix and payload bytes are interleaved **per document** (each doc's suffixes then its payloads, not two global regions), a second reverse-engineered detail the first fixture run caught; uses two more bit-packing conventions alongside `direct_reader`: `packed_ints` (generic MSB-first bitstream, for the distinct-field-numbers array) and `block_packed` (64-value blocks built on `packed_ints`, for the field/term bookkeeping arrays) |
| `util/packed/PackedInts.Format.PACKED`/`BulkOperationPacked` (generic MSB-first bit-packed array, arbitrary width) | `lucene-codecs/src/packed_ints.rs` | **both directions ported.** Read as before; `encode` is the exact bitwise inverse of `get`, any width `0..=64` (this convention has no whitelist of supported widths, unlike `direct_reader`) |
| `util/packed/BlockPackedReaderIterator`/`BlockPackedWriter` (64-value self-describing blocks) | `lucene-codecs/src/block_packed.rs` | **both directions ported.** Read as before (a single `decode_all`, not Java's seekable `next`/`skip` iterator). Write (`encode_all`) always emits `minValue = 0` rather than Java's per-block min-value optimization -- correct, just not minimal, same "worst-case width over minimal width" stance as `stored_fields::write_best_speed` -- and picks each block's `bitsPerValue` as the exact width its own max value needs, not rounded to any fixed set |
| `codecs/lucene90/compressing/Lucene90CompressingTermVectorsWriter` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/term_vectors.rs::write_best_speed` | **write path started, scoped down twice over from the real writer.** Single chunk only (`chunk_docs = docs.len()`), same as `stored_fields::write_best_speed`. Feature matrix: **positions only** -- every field passed in must have `has_offsets == false` and `has_payloads == false` (asserted), so offsets/payloads/`charsPerTerm` patching aren't attempted on the write side at all (committing to the full positions+offsets+payloads matrix in one pass risked a half-correct offset-patching interaction; positions alone is fully correct and independently useful, so the rest is left for a follow-up slice). No prefix sharing: every term is written with `prefix_len = 0` (its full text as the "suffix"), unlike a real writer that shares a prefix with the previous term in the field. Every `block_packed`/`direct_reader`/`packed_ints` array uses the exact bit width its own values need (worst case, not minimized across blocks/chunks). LZ4 is the same zero-dictionary, literal-only "compression" as stored fields' write side (`encode_literal_lz4`, a term-vectors-local copy since this format's LZ4 unit has no dict/block-length wrapper to begin with). **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_term_vectors_fixture.rs` writes a `.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` triple (3 docs, a multi-field doc, a doc with no term vectors, repeated terms with multi-occurrence positions) and `fixtures/src/VerifyTermVectors.java` opens it directly through `Lucene90TermVectorsFormat.vectorsReader` (hand-built `SegmentInfo`/`FieldInfos`, no `.si`/`.fnm` writer needed) and confirms every doc's terms/freqs/positions match via real `Terms`/`TermsEnum`/`PostingsEnum` -- passed on the first real-Lucene run. **Two review-pass fixes landed before this slice's commit**, both worth naming durably rather than leaving only in a source comment: (1) `bits_per_field_num` (the bit width `field_nums`/`allFieldNumOffs` are packed at) is floored at 1, never 0 -- a chunk where every field across every doc has `field_number == 0` (an entirely ordinary shape, e.g. any single-field index) previously computed a 0-bit width, which this port's own reader tolerates (an all-zero chunk just decodes as all-zero) but real Lucene's reader does not: it unconditionally indexes `packedBulkOps[bitsPerValue - 1]`, throwing `ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException` on a 0-bit width, independent of Java's `assert` (stripped without `-ea`, the default). The fixture now writes a second segment (`_1`) specifically shaped this way (every field number 0 across two docs) since the primary fixture's mixed field numbers 0/1 never exercised this; both segments pass against real Lucene. (2) the `.tvm` meta stream's `packedIntsVersion` field must be written as `2` (`PackedInts.VERSION_CURRENT`/`VERSION_MONOTONIC_WITHOUT_ZIGZAG`) -- this port's own reader never validates that field (a wrong value round-trips fine through it), but real Lucene's `BlockPackedReaderIterator` does validate it, so this is a genuine cross-engine-only requirement a purely-Rust test suite could never catch. Multi-chunk segments, real LZ4 back-reference compression, and the offsets/payloads slice of the feature matrix remain unimplemented on the write side. **Now wired into `IndexWriter::commit()`** (follow-up task, see PLAN.md): `IndexWriter::set_term_vector_field(Some(field_name))` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) opts a writer into calling this function for exactly one field of every segment `commit()` flushes, sourcing per-document `term -> (freq, positions)` data by regrouping `crate::indexing_chain::invert_documents`'s term-keyed inverted index by doc ID (term vectors need the transpose of what the postings writer wants) -- the same single-chunk/positions-only scope above, unchanged, now reachable from a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` call. Requires `store_term_vectors == true` on the field's `FieldInfo` (checked, `Error::UnsupportedTermVectorField` otherwise). **Still not wired for more than one field per commit**, same "no per-field file-suffix machinery" limitation `set_postings_field` has. **Merge-policy interaction, applied proactively from the postings feature's own review finding**: `execute_merge`/`merge_stored_only_segments` have no `.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` awareness either, so `segment_stats()` also excludes any segment whose `.si` lists a `.tvd` file from `find_merges`' candidate pool, keeping it permanently un-mergeable rather than mergeable-with-silent-data-loss. Covered by `segments_with_term_vectors_are_never_automatically_merged_away`, mirroring the postings version. **Postings + term vectors together, tested and found to work correctly**: `set_postings_field` and `set_term_vector_field` can both be set (to the same field) in one commit -- each builds its own in-memory output before `dir` is touched, and the `.si`-patching helper for each reads back whatever the other has already written rather than clobbering it, so a segment ends up with all seven files correctly listed; covered by `a_field_with_both_postings_and_term_vectors_configured_together_produces_both_correctly` (`lucene-search`) and its `lucene-index`-side unit-test counterpart. Required end-to-end proof: `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_term_vectors_fixtures.rs::documents_added_via_index_writer_have_readable_term_vectors` adds documents via `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` (not a hand-built fixture) and reads them back via the existing unmodified `lucene_search::term_vector_for_doc`, asserting the exact per-document term/freq/position data. |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90PointsFormat`/`Lucene90PointsReader`/`util/bkd/BKDReader` (`.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` read, block KD-tree point values -- `IntPoint`, `LongPoint`, `LatLonPoint`, etc.) | `lucene-codecs/src/points.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real IndexWriter (2000 docs, a `LongPoint` field on two-thirds of them so leaves have non-continuous doc ids, forcing several leaves past the default 512-point-per-leaf threshold); only the current on-disk BKD version (10, vectorized BPV24 + BPV21) is accepted, older versions rejected outright rather than replicated. **Decode-fully, no query pruning yet**: the packed index tree is walked in full left-to-right order to recover every leaf's file pointer rather than replicating Java's bounding-box-pruned seek/skip navigation -- the index's `leftNumBytes` skip-ahead hint is read and discarded, since a full recursive left-then-right traversal naturally consumes exactly that many bytes and needs no seeking at all; every `DocIdsWriter` doc-id encoding real writes can produce is supported (continuous run, bitset, 16/21/24/32-bit delta-packed), but the legacy vint delta encoding is not, since current Lucene never writes it. **`num_index_dims != 1` leaf layout bug fixed (task #22)**: `read_leaf_block`'s per-leaf min/max bounding box (present whenever `numIndexDims > 1`) had been decoded in the wrong position relative to the compressed-dimension marker byte -- it read the box *before* the marker, matching real `BKDReader.visitDocValuesNoCardinality`'s (older, no-longer-written) leaf layout instead of `visitDocValuesWithCardinality`'s (the layout every current-version, `VERSION_LOW_CARDINALITY_LEAVES`-and-up tree actually uses), which reads the marker *first* and only reads the box afterward, and only when the marker isn't `-1`. This went unnoticed for a while since the only test ever exercising it was a hand-built unit test (no real multi-dimension tree had ever been read *or* written by this port), and was only caught once this task's new write side produced a real 2-dimension `.kdd`/`.kdi` pair and `fixtures/src/VerifyPoints.java` tried to open it through real `Lucene90PointsFormat` (`CorruptIndexException: Got compressedDim=127`) -- exactly the kind of bug the differential-testing skill's fixture-first rule exists to catch. Fixed in both `read_leaf_block` (order swapped, box now conditioned on `compressed_dim != -1`) and this port's own `write_leaf` (marker written before the box, matching) |
| `codecs/lucene90/Lucene90PointsWriter`/`util/bkd/BKDWriter` (write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/points.rs::write` | **write path now supports any number of dimensions, any number of leaves** (task #22 extends the prior one-dimension-only, multi-leaf write path to `numDims > 1`, e.g. `LatLonPoint`-shaped 2D fields; `numIndexDims` is always treated as equal to `numDims` -- a field with extra data-only, non-indexed dimensions is not supported). **Split-dimension selection**: at every recursive split, [`widest_dim`] picks the dimension with the widest value range (`max - min`, computed via unsigned big-endian byte subtraction so it works for any `bytesPerDim`, not just ones that fit a native integer) across the current point subset, ties toward the lowest dimension index -- for `numDims == 1` this always picks dimension 0, so the original single-dimension path/behavior is unchanged. This is a real, deliberately-chosen heuristic, not a wild deviation from real `BKDWriter`: real Lucene's own multi-dimension `build()` picks its split dimension by computing each dimension's cardinality/range at the current node too (see `BKDWriter.build`'s `usedBytes`/cardinality-driven choice for leaf-level dimension selection, and its inner-node `splitDim` selection based on recomputed per-dimension bounds) -- this port's version is a simpler, still-real range comparison rather than replicating the exact cardinality-counting algorithm, documented as a deliberate scope reduction. Because a different dimension can be chosen at every recursion level, `compute_leaf_plan` now consumes and re-sorts an owned `Vec` at each split node (`Vec::split_off`) rather than indexing into one shared, globally-presorted array the way the single-dimension predecessor did -- still no per-node `radix select` the way real `BKDRadixSelector` does, a plain `sort_by` per node is enough at this port's sizes. Real Lucene picks the leaf-split shape via `getNumLeftLeafNodes` (fill the deepest full binary-tree level, half its leaves go left, then push any remainder left too) and `mid = numLeftLeafNodes * maxPointsInLeafNode`; this port's `compute_leaf_plan` uses the exact same two formulas (verified against `BKDWriter.getNumLeftLeafNodes`'s source, not approximated), so the resulting tree shape matches real Lucene's for any point count/leaf-size combination. `packIndex`/`recursePackIndex`'s general case (split descriptor + left/right children + `leftNumBytes` skip-ahead) is implemented (`pack_index`), matching real Lucene's node layout exactly, **now including the split *dimension*, not just the split value**: the packed-index code formula `(firstDiffByteDelta * (1 + bytesPerDim) + prefix) * numIndexDims + splitDim` (already documented from task #21) now genuinely varies `splitDim` per node rather than always encoding `0`, and the split-value delta-coding's `lastSplitValues`/`negativeDeltas` state (`last_split_values`/`negative_deltas` in this port) is now **one array slot per index dimension** (real `BKDWriter.recursePackIndex`'s own per-dimension arrays) instead of a single dimension-0-only pair -- only the dimension a given node actually split on has its slot touched/saved/restored around that node's children, every other dimension's slot is inherited unchanged from the parent, exactly like real Lucene's shared per-dimension arrays. Leaf data now carries all dimensions per point (`numDims * bytesPerDim` bytes), and each leaf also writes its own (tighter-than-field) per-dimension min/max bounding box whenever `numIndexDims != 1`, matching what the read side ([`read_leaf_block`]) already unconditionally decoded in that case (see the read-side row above for the ordering bug this surfaced and fixed). Leaf-encoding choices remain freely made (not replicating real `BKDWriter`'s size-driven heuristics): common-prefix length always 0 per dimension, compressed-dimension marker always `-2` with every run forced to length 1, doc ids `CONTINUOUS_IDS` or plain `BPV_32`. Unit-tested: `widest_dim`/`unsigned_byte_sub` in isolation (widest-range selection, tie-breaking, multi-byte borrow), `compute_leaf_plan`'s point-distribution/balance invariants (now leaf-content-based rather than range-based, since dimension changes at each recursion level, and confirmed no longer a globally-presorted single order), two dedicated multi-dimension `pack_index`/split-value-reconstruction tests (a 3-dimension, 7-leaf tree whose split dimensions are confirmed to vary across nodes, decoded by a generalized `reconstruct_split_values` mirror of real `BKDReader.readNodeData`), and full write→read round trips through this module's own reader for a 2D `LatLonPoint`-shaped 100-point/25-leaf tree and a 3D 2-byte-per-dim, non-continuous-doc-id, 8-leaf tree, on top of the pre-existing 1D single/multi-leaf coverage. 99.5%+ line coverage on `points.rs`. **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction**: `crates/lucene-codecs/examples/write_points_fixture.rs` now writes *three* segments -- `_0` (single-leaf, 1D, unchanged), `_1` (multi-leaf, 1D, unchanged, including its pre-existing narrow-bounding-box pruning query), and **`_2` (new: 2-dimension, `LatLonPoint`-shaped, multi-leaf, with the two dimensions deliberately correlated so a real bounding-box query narrow on both axes actually finds leaves fully `CELL_INSIDE_QUERY`, not just `CELL_CROSSES_QUERY`/`CELL_OUTSIDE_QUERY`)** -- and `fixtures/src/VerifyPoints.java`'s new `verifySegment2D`/`verifyPruningQuery2D` open `_2` directly through real `Lucene90PointsFormat.fieldsReader`, confirm every point via a full-decode `CELL_CROSSES_QUERY`-only pass, **and then run a real two-dimension bounding-box query that prunes across *both* dimensions** (asserting at least one `CELL_OUTSIDE_QUERY` and one `CELL_INSIDE_QUERY` cell actually occur, then checking the returned point set against the manifest) -- all three segments and both pruning queries (1D and 2D) passed against real Lucene, proving real `BKDReader`/`IndexTree` accepts this port's multi-dimension packed-index encoding and correctly reconstructs per-dimension split values/dimensions from it, including under real pruning. **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing**: data-only dimensions (`numDims > numIndexDims`), and real query-driven pruning on this port's *own* read side (still decode-fully, see the read-side row) -- multi-dimension write is otherwise no longer a scoped-out gap. |

| `codecs/lucene104/Lucene104PostingsReader`/`Writer`, `PostingsUtil`, `ForUtil`, `PForUtil` (`.doc`/`.pos`/`.pay` files, `PostingsEnum` in `DOCS`/`DOCS_AND_FREQS`/`DOCS_AND_FREQS_AND_POSITIONS`/`DOCS_AND_FREQS_AND_POSITIONS_AND_OFFSETS` mode, incl. payloads) | `lucene-codecs/src/postings.rs` (+ `lucene-codecs/src/for_util.rs`) | **ported: sequential decode (a full forward scan, `nextDoc()`-equivalent -- no skip-ahead/`advance()`) of any `docFreq > 1` up to `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (32 * `ForUtil.BLOCK_SIZE` = 8192), `IndexOptions::Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs`.** Three writer-side shapes now all decode: `docFreq == 1` is pulsed entirely into the term dictionary (`Lucene104PostingsWriter.finishTerm`, no `.doc` bytes at all -- `postings::singleton_postings` reconstructs `(docID, freq)` purely from `TermMetadata::singleton_doc_id` + `totalTermFreq`); `1 < docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE` takes `PostingsUtil.writeVIntBlock` (group-varint doc-delta/freq-bit packing + a plain-vint tail of freq exceptions, no skip data, no impacts), decoded via `DataInput::read_group_vints` (`postings::read_tail_block`); and **`docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`** now decodes one or more full 256-doc blocks (`postings::read_full_block_header` + `postings::decode_full_block_body`) followed by that same tail-block encoding for the `docFreq % BLOCK_SIZE` remainder. Each full block is `ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-bit-packed -- `for_util.rs` is a direct transliteration of `ForUtil.decode1..decode16`/`decodeSlow` (the lane-interleaved-per-byte/halfword SIMD-shaped bit-packing for `bitsPerValue <= 16`, plain 32-bit-wide packing above that) and `PForUtil.decode` (the token byte + up to 7 byte-patched exceptions), independently round-tripped against a hand-written test encoder for every `bits_per_value` in `1..=32` (not just what one fixture term happens to need) -- and the full block's doc-delta section additionally supports the "all-256-consecutive" (`bitsPerValue == 0`) and dense unary bit-set (`bitsPerValue < 0`) encodings the writer picks for storage efficiency (the bit-set path is not a corner case: it's what real Lucene chooses for this port's own dense `big`/"everywhere" fixture term, confirmed by regenerating against the real writer). Also ported (previously skipped by `blocktree.rs`, see that row): the per-term postings-metadata bytes (`Lucene104PostingsReader.decodeTerm`, no-positions subset) -- `postings::decode_term_metadata`, threaded across a `.tim` block's entries exactly like `SegmentTermsEnumFrame` threads `IntBlockTermState`. `blocktree::FieldTerms::postings(term, doc_in)` wires this up end-to-end: `seekExact` -> stats + metadata -> singleton reconstruction or `.doc` decode. **`advance()`: an "advance()-shaped API, not real skip-ahead" shim, landed this slice.** `postings::PostingsCursor` (`next_doc()`/`advance(target)`/`doc_id()`/`freq()`) gives `PostingsEnum`-style interface parity, but it is a binary search over `DocInput::read_postings`'s already-fully-materialized `Postings.docs`/`freqs` `Vec`s -- **not** a lazy on-wire jump using the level-0/level-1 skip pointers (those are still parsed-and-discarded, exactly as before this slice; see the deferred bullet below, unchanged). This was a deliberate scope choice per this slice's own design brief: a real lazy skip-ahead would need a new stateful `DocInput`-like type tracking on-wire position and decoding blocks on demand, which is a materially larger and riskier change than a cursor over data this file already decodes eagerly by design (the same tradeoff every other decoder in this file already made -- `BlockTree`'s `TermsEnum`, `IndexedDISI`, the terms dictionary, `BlockPackedReaderIterator`).
