Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum.advance(target)` output (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java::appendAdvanceManifest`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::{big,body}_field_advance_matches_real_lucene_postings_enum_advance`) for both "big"/"everywhere" (`docFreq == 300`, so some targets cross the full-block/tail-block boundary) and "body"/"cat" (`docFreq == 2`, single tail block), across before-first-doc/exact-match/between-docs/next-doc-after-a-match/last-doc/past-last-doc targets -- matched on the first real-Lucene run, no decode bugs caught (unsurprising, since the shim never touches the wire format at all, only the already-verified decoded `Vec`s). Unit tests (`postings.rs`) additionally cover: advancing to a target at or before the current doc ID (documented no-op, not an error or rewind -- real Lucene's contract technically forbids this, but the shim's binary-search-from-current-position implementation makes a no-op the natural, safe behavior to document rather than leave accidental), advance on empty postings, advance past the last doc (`NO_MORE_DOCS`), and advance immediately followed by `next_doc()` continuing from the landed position. **Deferred** (rejected with `Error::Unsupported`, or in the skip-ahead case simply not implemented as an API): (1) **real lazy skip-ahead** -- the level-0/level-1 skip pointers (`level0NumBytes`/`blockLength`/level-1 header vlongs) are parsed in wire order for correctness but never used to jump forward or to avoid decoding a block; every block between the start and the target is fully decoded by `read_postings`, and `PostingsCursor` only adds a post-hoc binary-search cursor on top of that (see above) -- correct but not fast for a searcher that only wants a subrange (fine for a full-scan/merge consumer, or a conjunction/phrase query over small-enough postings lists that eager decode is cheap); a stateful decode-on-demand `DocInput` that actually jumps past undecoded blocks using the level-0 pointers remains future work; (2) **`docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`** (8192) -- level-1 skip entries start appearing inline in the `.doc` stream every 32 full blocks, not yet parsed; (3) positions/offsets/payloads (`.pos`/`.pay`, `IndexOptions::DocsAndFreqsAndPositions` and up -- `decode_term_metadata` doesn't even parse the `posStartFP`/`payStartFP`/`lastPosBlockOffset` fields those index options add to the wire; being worked on separately, this slice deliberately did not touch `.pos`/`.pay`); (4) impacts/competitive-scoring metadata (`ImpactsEnum`, `CompetitiveImpactAccumulator`, needed for WAND/MAXSCORE in PLAN.md Phase 3) -- full-block impact bytes are parsed-and-discarded (skipped by length), never surfaced; (5) `IndexOptions::DocsAndCustomFreqs` -- rejected outright, real Lucene never writes it for a normal text field. **Positions/offsets/payloads are now ported** (`.pos`/`.pay`, `IndexOptions::DocsAndFreqsAndPositions` and `...AndOffsets`), sequential-only (no skip-ahead, same scope as the `.doc` side): `decode_term_metadata` now parses `posStartFP`/`payStartFP`/`lastPosBlockOffset` (`Lucene104PostingsReader.java:237-250`), `read_full_block` parses (but doesn't act on) the extra level-0 pos/pay skip-pointer fields those index options add to a full doc block's header (`Lucene104PostingsReader.java:754-761`), and the new `PosInput`/`PayInput` + `read_positions` decode every position/offset/payload occurrence for a term as **one flat sequence of `totalTermFreq` occurrences** (not one block per doc -- the writer buffers 256 occurrences at a time across doc boundaries, only resetting the position/offset accumulator per doc, `Lucene104PostingsReader.java:1298-1304`) -- full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` blocks (payload lengths and offset start-deltas/lengths bulk-encoded, payload bytes batched per block) for `totalTermFreq / BLOCK_SIZE` full blocks, then a `refillLastPositionBlock`-style vint tail (payload bytes inlined in `.pos`, lengths only re-written when they change) for the remainder, re-chopped into per-doc groups via `Postings::freqs`. `blocktree::FieldTerms::positions(term, doc_in, pos_in, pay_in)` wires this up end-to-end alongside `postings()`. Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum.nextPosition()`/`startOffset()`/`endOffset()`/`getPayload()` output via a new "pos" field in `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java` (`DOCS_AND_FREQS_AND_POSITIONS_AND_OFFSETS`, a repeated term across two docs with a payload on only one occurrence, exercising the vint tail's payload-length-change bit) -- matched on the first real-Lucene run, no decode bugs caught this time. **Deferred**: the full-`ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-block position path (`totalTermFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`) is only unit-tested (`postings::tests::read_positions_exactly_one_full_block_boundary`), not fixture-verified against real Lucene bytes, since reaching it needs 256+ real token occurrences of one term that this port's small hand-built fixtures don't produce; `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` interacts with positions the same way it does with docs (not supported, same `Error::Unsupported` gate on `read_postings`, which `positions()` also goes through via `postings()`). Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum.nextDoc()`/`freq()` output (not just aggregate `docFreq`/`totalTermFreq` stats) via `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java`'s extended manifest: "body" (`docFreq == 2` for every term, `.doc` group-varint decode), "id" (`docFreq == 1`, singleton path, no `.doc` access at all), and **"big"/"everywhere" (`docFreq == 300`, one full `PForUtil`-bit-set-encoded block + a 44-doc group-varint tail, added specifically to force the multi-block path past real `Lucene104PostingsWriter`/`IndexWriter`)** -- see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`. Hand-built unit tests cover edge cases no small real fixture reaches: `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE` (256, exactly one full block, no tail bytes at all), `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE + 1` (257, one full block + a 1-doc tail), the full-block bit-set (unary) doc-delta decode and its too-few-set-bits corruption check, `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE - 1` (255, the largest size the non-multi-block path supports), all-docs-freq-1 (group-varint bit-packing path with zero trailing freq-exception vints), `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` rejection, and `decode_term_metadata`'s absolute-vs-delta and docStartFP-delta-vs-singleton-zigzag-delta branches. `for_util.rs`'s own unit tests independently round-trip `bits_per_value` `1..=32` (both the lane-interleaved `<=16` paths and the `decodeSlow` `17..=32` path) and the `PForUtil` all-equal/exceptions fast paths, via test-only encoders mirroring `ForUtil.collapse8/16`+`encode`/`PForUtil.encode`. **Post-landing review fixes**: (a) `decode_term_metadata` now correctly zeroes `doc_start_fp`/`pos_start_fp`/`pay_start_fp` before applying deltas when `absolute` is set (`Lucene104PostingsReader.decodeTerm`'s own reset), instead of basing them on whatever `prev` the caller passed in -- invisible today since every current caller passes a fresh `TermMetadata::EMPTY` as `prev` on `absolute`, but load-bearing once multi-block BlockTree threads `prev_meta` across blocks; covered by `decode_term_metadata_absolute_resets_fps_even_with_stale_prev`; (b) `read_positions`'s per-doc re-chop loop now returns `Error::Store(Corrupted(_))` instead of panicking via out-of-bounds indexing when a corrupted `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tmd` makes `freqs` sum to more or less than `total_term_freq` (covered by two new rejects-mismatch tests); (c) closed two coverage gaps the ≥95%-per-file bar didn't catch: the packed (`bitsPerValue > 0`) `.doc` doc-delta branch and the full-`PForUtil`-block position path *with offsets* (as opposed to payloads) were previously exercised by neither the fixture nor a unit test -- both now have dedicated unit tests (`read_full_block_packed_encoding_decodes_bit_packed_deltas`, `read_positions_full_block_with_offsets_no_payloads`), reusing `for_util`'s own test-only bit-packing encoder (later promoted to the production `for_util::for_encode` function, see below, so this cross-module reuse point moved with it) **Real lazy skip-ahead is now ported** (`postings::LazyDocsCursor`, `DocInput::lazy_cursor`, `blocktree::FieldTerms::lazy_postings`): a decode-on-demand `next_doc()`/`advance(target)` iterator that decodes one `.doc` block at a time, replacing the eager whole-term materialization `PostingsCursor` sits on top of (that shim is unchanged and still exists for callers that want the simpler already-decoded path -- see the module doc for which to pick). **The honest boundary of what is actually skipped**: `read_full_block_header` was split out of `read_full_block` (now a thin wrapper over `read_full_block_header` + `decode_full_block_body`) to read a full block's level-0 header (`level0NumBytes`/`docDelta`/`blockLength`/impacts/pos-pay fields) *without* running `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` decode on its body; the header alone gives the block's last doc ID (`prev_doc_id + docDelta`) and its on-wire byte span. When `advance(target)` finds `target > header.last_doc_id`, it `seek()`s straight to the block's end and moves to the next block, skipping the actual bit-unpack entirely -- the expensive part of a block. This works for **every full block a term has, at any `docFreq`, not just `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`**: level-0 skip-past-one-block only requires the term to have at least one full 256-doc block (`docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`), which is unrelated to the level-1 (8192-doc) threshold -- level-1 exists to skip past *32 full blocks at once* without reading their individual level-0 headers, a coarser optimization this port still does not need since it already reads every level-0 header cheaply one at a time. The **tail block** (the `docFreq % BLOCK_SIZE` remainder, or the whole term when `docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE`) carries no skip data on the wire at all -- reaching it always means decoding it in full, lazy cursor or not, matching real `Lucene104PostingsReader.refillRemainder`. `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` is still rejected by `lazy_cursor` with the same `Error::Unsupported` as `read_postings` -- unchanged from before this slice; the lazy cursor does not add level-1 support, it only makes level-0 skip actually *used* instead of parsed-and-discarded. Differential-tested against real `PostingsEnum.advance(target)` output for the same target set as `PostingsCursor` (`crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::{big,body}_field_lazy_advance_matches_real_lucene_postings_enum_advance`) plus a full `next_doc()` walk compared against the eager `read_postings` result byte-for-byte (`big_field_lazy_next_doc_matches_eager_read_postings`) -- all three matched on the first real-Lucene run. A hand-built unit test (`lazy_cursor_advance_skips_corrupted_earlier_block_without_decoding_it`) proves the skip is real, not just correct by coincidence: it builds a first full block whose body is deliberately corrupt (a bit-set with fewer than `BLOCK_SIZE` bits set, which `decode_full_block_body` rejects with a `Corrupted` error) followed by a valid second block, and confirms `advance()` to a target in the second block succeeds (the corrupt first block is never decoded) while `advance()` to a target in the first block surfaces the corruption error (confirming the earlier success wasn't accidental). Other unit tests cover sequential multi-block decode matching `read_postings`, the no-op advance-to-current-or-earlier contract, advance past the last doc, and the `docFreq <= 1` rejection mirroring `read_postings`'s own. **`docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (8192) level-1 skip data is now ported for both paths, closing the last remaining `docFreq` gap** (supersedes the several "rejected with `Error::Unsupported`" / "not yet parsed" mentions of that threshold above, which described the state before this slice). Above `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` the `.doc` stream interleaves a level-1 skip entry (`postings::read_level1_entry`, the vInt span-last-doc delta + vLong `level1DocEndFP` + `indexHasFreq`-gated `readShort` skip1EndFP/numImpactBytes + impacts bytes + pos/pay sub-fields, reverse-engineered from `Lucene104PostingsReader.skipLevel1To`, `Lucene104PostingsReader.java:674-719`) before every span of `LEVEL1_FACTOR` (32) full level-0 blocks, for as long as at least `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` docs remain. `read_postings` (eager) consumes each entry's bytes purely to stay byte-aligned and decodes its 32 blocks like any other; `LazyDocsCursor` (lazy) tracks `level1_last_doc_id`/`level1_doc_end_fp`/`level1_doc_count_upto` and, via the new `skip_level1_to` method (mirroring Java's `skipLevel1To`, wired into `advance` exactly like Java's `moveToNextLevel0Block`/`doAdvanceShallow` call it first), `seek()`s straight to `level1_doc_end_fp` to jump a whole 32-block span whose last doc is behind the target -- never reading even the individual level-0 headers of the skipped span, the coarser counterpart to the level-0 skip-past-one-block above. Positions inherit level-1 support automatically, since `positions()` no longer hits a `docFreq` gate. Fixture-verified against real `PostingsEnum` via a new "l1" field in `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java` ("l1term" in 8250 docs, one level-1 span + a 58-doc remainder): full `nextDoc()`/`freq()` iteration over all 8250 docs for both eager and lazy paths, plus eager and lazy `advance()` at the exact span boundaries (occurrence 8191 = span's last doc, 8192 = first remainder doc reached only by jumping the whole span, `appendLevel1AdvanceManifest`) -- matched on the first real-Lucene run, no decode bugs caught. Hand-built unit tests cover the level-1 entry decode in isolation (all freq/pos/pay sub-fields + the docs-only short form), an eager span+tail decode, a lazy sequential walk matching eager, and a "provably skipped" test corrupting an entire 32-block span to confirm `advance()` past it never touches the corrupt bytes while a control target into the span still surfaces the corruption. **Impacts/competitive-scoring metadata (`ImpactsEnum`/`CompetitiveImpactAccumulator`) are now decoded, for both level-0 (per-block) and level-1 (per-span) impact byte runs** -- this was the last thing on the postings wire that was parsed-and-discarded purely by length rather than decoded. `postings::Impact { freq: i32, norm: i64 }` (a direct port of `Impact`'s two fields) plus `postings::decode_impacts(bytes)` implement `Lucene104PostingsReader.readImpacts`'s decode exactly: a flat sequence of vint `freqDelta`s (each storing `impact.freq - previous.freq - 1`, i.e. `+1` is added back on decode) whose low bit selects between an implicit `normDelta == 0` (the common "norm only increases by 1" case, zero extra bytes) and an explicit zigzag `normDelta` vlong. `read_full_block_header` (level-0) and `read_level1_entry` (level-1) both now decode their impacts byte run into `FullBlockHeader::impacts`/`Level1Entry::impacts` instead of `skip()`-ing past it -- the length-prefix parsing (vint for level-0, `readShort` for level-1) is unchanged, only the payload is now real. **Exposed on both cursors** (impacts are inherently a "what's coming up from here" query that only makes sense against a position, matching real `ImpactsEnum.getImpacts()` -- both `LazyDocsCursor` and `PostingsCursor` have one): `LazyDocsCursor::level0_impacts()`/`level1_impacts()` for the genuinely lazy, decode-on-demand cursor, `PostingsCursor::level0_impacts()`/`level1_impacts()` for the eager, already-materialized one (a lookup into `Postings::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts`, see below): `level0_impacts()` returns the current level-0 block's competitive pairs (empty once positioned in the tail block, which carries no level-0 impacts on the wire at all -- deliberately *not* replicating Java's synthetic "everything is competitive" `(Integer.MAX_VALUE, 1)` sentinel for that state, since this port exposes decoded wire data rather than reconstructing `ImpactsEnum`'s full multi-level fallback semantics) and `level1_impacts()` returns the current level-1 span's merged pairs (empty below `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` docs or past the last span). Differential-tested against real `TermsEnum.impacts(PostingsEnum.FREQS)`/`ImpactsEnum.getImpacts(level)` ground truth (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java::appendImpactsManifest`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::{big,l1}_field_impacts_match_real_lucene_impacts_enum`) for "big"/"everywhere" (level-0 only, three occurrences within its one full block, freq/norm both varying 1..4) and "l1"/"l1term" (level-0 varying across different blocks of the same level-1 span, level-1 merged and identical across all three sampled occurrences since they share one span) -- matched on the first real-Lucene run. Unit tests for `decode_impacts` itself cover: empty input, a single implicit-norm-delta entry, multiple entries mixing implicit and explicit (including a full-width `i64::MAX` norm) deltas via a test-only encoder mirroring `Lucene104PostingsWriter.writeImpacts` exactly, and two truncation/corruption cases (a freqDelta vint missing its continuation byte, an explicit-norm-delta flag with no following zlong). **Impacts are now threaded through the eager path too**: `DocInput::read_postings` captures each level-0 block's and level-1 span's already-decoded impacts (no second decode pass -- it just retains what it was discarding) into `Postings::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts` (`Vec<(last_doc_id_covered, Impacts)>`, ascending/contiguous so a lookup is a single `partition_point` binary search), and `PostingsCursor::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts` look up the entry covering `doc_id()` the same way `LazyDocsCursor::level0_impacts`/`level1_impacts` report the block/span covering its own current position -- same query, same empty-cases contract (tail block, below `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`, no freqs, not yet/no-longer positioned), just against pre-materialized data instead of decode-on-demand state. Verified against the same real-Lucene ground truth as the lazy path (`crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`'s `big_field_impacts_match_real_lucene_impacts_enum`/`l1_field_impacts_match_real_lucene_impacts_enum`, extended to assert `PostingsCursor`'s new accessors too, not just cross-check against `LazyDocsCursor`). **Still deferred**: no `ImpactsSource`/full `ImpactsEnum` trait hierarchy (`numLevels()`, `getDocIdUpTo()`) is implemented for either cursor, only the two concrete accessors this port actually needs. **`for_util.rs` now has real, production (not test-only) encode-side primitives**: `for_util::for_encode` (`ForUtil.encode`, bit-pack 256 already-fit values at a caller-chosen width) and `for_util::pfor_encode` (`PForUtil.encode`, the full histogram-based bit-width search that picks the smallest width keeping at most `MAX_EXCEPTIONS` (7) patched outliers, plus the all-equal vint fast path) -- both are direct ports of the real Java encoders, independently round-tripped in `for_util.rs`'s own tests (exactly-256-entries no-exceptions, all-zero, full-31-bit, few-outliers-with-patched-exceptions, and a direct `pfor_encode`-then-`for_decode` cross-check). **Not yet wired into `postings_writer.rs`**: the writer's `write_single_field`/`write_fields` still reject any term with `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` or `total_term_freq >= BLOCK_SIZE` (`Error::DocFreqTooLarge`/`Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`, see that module's own doc comment) -- calling `for_encode`/`pfor_encode` from the writer to actually emit full 256-entry blocks (matching what `postings.rs`'s reader already fully decodes, see above) additionally needs the writer to build the level-0 skip-list metadata (`level0NumBytes`/`blockLength`/impacts bytes) the reader expects to find alongside each full block, which the writer does not build today. That remaining wiring is out of scope for this slice and tracked here rather than silently left unimplemented. |
| `util/fst/FST` (`FST.Arc`/`BytesReader`/`readArc`/`findTargetArc`/`readMetadata` -- on-heap arc-lookup read side) | `lucene-codecs/src/fst.rs` | **ported, scoped to lookup-only.** Lives in `lucene-codecs`, not `lucene-util` as PLAN.md §1's crate table originally sketched -- FST metadata parsing needs `CodecUtil.checkHeader` (`lucene-store::codec_util`), and per the `architecture` skill's strict downward dependency graph (`util ← store ← codecs`), `lucene-util` cannot depend on `lucene-store`, so a module needing both belongs in `lucene-codecs`. Ported: `Fst::read` (metadata + on-heap body, `OnHeapFSTStore`'s single-`Vec<u8>` case, copying the body into a freshly-allocated `Vec<u8>`) and `Fst::read_borrowed` (identical metadata parsing, but the body is a zero-copy `&'a [u8]` borrowed straight out of the caller's own buffer via `SliceInput::slice`/`seek`, no allocation for the body at all). **What "off-heap" honestly means here**: this port's `Directory` abstraction already has a real zero-copy backend, `lucene_store::directory::MmapDirectory` -- an actual OS `mmap(2)` via `memmap2`, returning `Input::Mapped` which `Deref`s to `&[u8]` without ever materializing an owned `Vec<u8>` copy of the file. `Fst::read_borrowed` is the missing FST-level plumbing that lets an `Fst<'a>` be constructed directly over such a buffer without `Fst::read`'s unconditional extra copy of the body -- for an `Fst` opened over an `MmapDirectory`-backed `Input`, that reproduces real Lucene's `OffHeapFSTStore` cost model: bytes stay in the OS page cache, faulted in lazily as arcs are actually visited, never doubled in the process heap. This module itself performs no `mmap(2)` call -- that already exists in `lucene-store` -- so the precise framing is "a borrowing/zero-copy FST constructor that composes with this port's existing mmap `Directory` backend," not "this file re-implements memory-mapping." `Fst::read` and `Fst::read_borrowed` are proven to agree on every lookup for the same bytes (`crates/lucene-codecs/src/fst.rs::tests::read_borrowed_matches_read_for_same_bytes`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_fixtures.rs::read_borrowed_matches_read_on_real_fixture` against the real Lucene-written fixture), and an end-to-end test opens a real `MmapDirectory`-backed file this way (`read_borrowed_over_a_real_mmap_directory_input`). The reverse `BytesReader` cursor (`ReverseBytesReader`), and `Fst::get` (`Util.get(FST, BytesRef)`-equivalent: walk `findTargetArc` once per key byte, then check `arc.is_final()`). Single output type: `ByteSequenceOutputs` (`Vec<u8>` in Rust) -- the type real Lucene's term index FST actually uses to map term-prefix byte sequences to concatenated block-pointer bytes, confirmed by checking `ByteSequenceOutputs.java` directly rather than assumed. Only `INPUT_TYPE.BYTE1` is accepted by `get` (the term index's label type; `BYTE2`/`BYTE4` are parsed in metadata for completeness but rejected by `get` before any label decoding, since nothing in this port needs them yet). **FST construction (`build_fst`/`write_fst`, same file) is now ported, scoped to a simplified builder, not real `FSTCompiler`.** Real Lucene's `FSTCompiler` is an *incremental*, memory-bounded builder (a stack of `UnCompiledNode`s, a node hash table for suffix sharing/minimization, output pushing down shared prefixes) -- reproducing that algorithm exactly remains deferred, much larger future work. What's ported instead: `build_fst(&[(Vec<u8>, Vec<u8>)])` takes the *entire* sorted key/output sequence in memory, builds an ordinary trie, and serializes it bottom-up directly into the same list-encoded (variable-length arc) node/arc byte format `Fst::read`/`find_target_arc`/`read_arc` (above, unmodified) already parse -- explicit `vlong` targets everywhere (no `BIT_TARGET_NEXT` physical-adjacency compaction), each key's whole output placed on the single arc leading to its accepting node (no output-pushing down shared prefixes), no suffix sharing (two keys sharing a suffix, e.g. `"cat"`/`"bat"` sharing `"at"`, get independent copies of that suffix's nodes rather than one shared node). `write_fst(&Fst)` serializes a built `Fst` back through the exact codec-header + `FSTMetadata.save` layout `Fst::read` parses, for a full round trip through the unmodified reader rather than only the in-memory `Fst` struct. **Verified**: self-round-trip only, not a real-Lucene byte-compatibility cross-check -- `crates/lucene-codecs/src/fst.rs::tests` builds FSTs from a 7-key set matching `fixtures/src/GenFst.java`'s shape (`app`/`apple`/`application`, `banana`/`band`/`bandana`, `z`), a single key, an empty key set, a key set including the empty-string key, a key that's a proper prefix of another (final arc with its own children, not a stop node), a 200-key set forcing multi-byte `vlong` targets, and unsorted/duplicate-key input rejection -- every case opens via the real unmodified `Fst::read` and confirms every present key resolves correctly and every absent key is rejected via `Fst::get`. **Still deferred**: real `FSTCompiler`'s suffix sharing/minimization and output-pushing (affects output compactness, not correctness of this port's own round trip); fixed-length arc nodes (`ARCS_FOR_BINARY_SEARCH`/`ARCS_FOR_DIRECT_ADDRESSING`/`ARCS_FOR_CONTINUOUS` -- rejected outright via `Error::Unsupported` rather than misdecoded, so large/dense FSTs with "enough" arcs per node to trigger these will currently error rather than silently corrupt); other output types (`PositiveIntOutputs`, `PairOutputs`, ...); full ordered enumeration (`BytesRefFSTEnum`/`IntsRefFSTEnum`, needed for prefix/range iteration, not single-key lookup) -- `readFirstTargetArc`/`readNextRealArc` (the enumeration-only siblings of `findTargetArc`) were written, found to be dead code under this slice's `get`-only scope, and removed rather than kept untested. Fixture-verified against a real `FST<BytesRef>` built via real `FSTCompiler` (`allowFixedLengthArcs(false)`, so the fixture itself never emits the array-node encodings this slice doesn't support) with 7 keys sharing prefixes/suffixes (`app`/`apple`/`application`, `banana`/`band`/`bandana`, `z`) plus 8 deliberately-absent lookups (proper prefixes, over-extensions, a disjoint key) -- see `fixtures/src/GenFst.java` and `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/fst_fixtures.rs` |
| `codecs/lucene103/blocktree/Lucene103BlockTreeTermsReader`/`Writer`, `FieldReader`, `SegmentTermsEnum`/`Frame`, `TrieReader`/`TrieBuilder` (`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` term dictionary + term index) | `lucene-codecs/src/blocktree.rs` | **ported, scoped to `seekExact` + `docFreq`/`totalTermFreq`, now covering multi-block fields (multi-child `.tip` tries and floor-split `.tim` blocks), not just single-block ones.** Correction to the row this replaces: the pinned Lucene version (10.5.0, `Lucene104PostingsFormat`) uses `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsReader`/`Writer` (package `lucene103.blocktree`), *not* `Lucene90BlockTreeTermsReader` -- that class lives in `backward-codecs` and is out of scope. This version's `.tip` term index is **not an FST** -- Lucene 10.x replaced it with a purpose-built binary trie (`TrieReader`/`TrieBuilder`); `fst.rs` (scoped to the older format) is not used here. Ported: opening a `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` triple (header/footer/checksum framing, the embedded `Lucene104PostingsWriterTerms` sub-header + `BLOCK_SIZE` check, per-field `numTerms`/`sumTotalTermFreq`/`sumDocFreq`/`docCount`/`minTerm`/`maxTerm`), and now a **full trie decode** (all three node shapes -- `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN`, `SIGN_SINGLE_CHILD_WITH_OUTPUT`/`WITHOUT_OUTPUT`, `SIGN_MULTI_CHILDREN` with all three `ChildSaveStrategy` label encodings -- `BITS`/`ARRAY`/`REVERSE_ARRAY`) plus floor-block resolution (`LEAF_NODE_HAS_FLOOR`/`NON_LEAF_NODE_HAS_FLOOR`, the `numFollowFloorBlocks`/`(label, code)` byte layout). **Design**: rather than walking one root-to-leaf trie path per lookup (what real `SegmentTermsEnum.seekExact` does), `open()` recursively visits every reachable trie node, resolves every floor sub-block, decodes every resulting `.tim` block (re-attaching each block's own trie-path prefix, since a block only stores its suffix bytes), and merges everything into one sorted `Vec` -- the same shape the prior single-block slice used, just now fed by a full traversal instead of one root-node read. This eagerly decodes blocks a real `seekExact` for one term would never touch (acceptable for now: no enumeration/streaming consumer exists yet to notice, and correctness came first) -- see the module doc for the full tradeoff writeup. **Real bug this slice's fixture caught**: an interior trie node can have its own output block flagged `hasTerms=false` (a "pass-through" block that itself holds nothing but pointers to its own further-split children, produced by `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter.writeBlocks` recursing to a deeper prefix instead of floor-splitting) -- the first implementation treated this as an unsupported non-leaf block and errored; the fix is to just skip that one physical block, since `PendingBlock.compileIndex` unconditionally merges every deeper recursion's own trie into the same trie this code already walks, so every term routed through the pointer-only block is independently reachable as a deeper node anyway. Caught by the new "many" field in `fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java` (400 distinct terms, forcing real `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter` past the default 25/48 min/maxItemsInBlock thresholds into both a multi-child trie and at least one floor split) -- every other fixture field stayed single-block and would never have hit this. **Still deferred** (`Error::Unsupported`): a `.tim` block that is itself non-leaf (`isLeafBlock` false, i.e. decoding it would require following in-block sub-block pointers rather than raw term suffixes) -- every block this port's fixtures actually decode is a leaf block, since pointer-only blocks are skipped rather than opened (see above), but a field shaped so that a *decoded* block is non-leaf remains unhandled; automaton intersection (`IntersectTermsEnum`). **Suffix compression (read-side) is now supported**: `decode_block` dispatches on `code_l & 0x03` (`CompressionAlgorithm.NO_COMPRESSION`/`LOWERCASE_ASCII`/`LZ4`), reusing this port's own `lz4.rs` decompressor for LZ4 (a real, general-purpose decompressor, not a stub) and a small standalone port of `LowercaseAsciiCompression.decompress` for the other mode (`blocktree.rs::decompress_lowercase_ascii`); code `3` (never assigned to a `CompressionAlgorithm` constant) is rejected as `Error::Store(Corrupted)`, matching `CompressionAlgorithm.byCode`'s own `IllegalArgumentException`. This is purely read-side interop with real Lucene-written segments -- this port's own blocktree *writer* still only ever emits `NO_COMPRESSION`. **Verification, stated precisely**: LZ4 is verified against an actual `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter`-produced fixture (200 terms sharing a long, highly repetitive-suffix common prefix, past the default min/maxItemsInBlock thresholds so the real writer chose LZ4 for several blocks) -- `fixtures/data/blocktree_compressed_index/`, `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_compressed_fixture.rs` (`lz4_compressed_terms_match_real_lucene`, `lz4_compressed_enumeration_matches_real_lucene_terms_enum_next`). `LOWERCASE_ASCII` could **not** be forced out of a real `IndexWriter` in reasonable effort (the writer only takes that branch once LZ4 already failed to save 25% *and* the block's average suffix length still clears its own `prefixLength > 2`/`length > 2*numEntries` gates -- every term shape tried here landed on `NO_COMPRESSION` instead), so it's instead verified against a byte vector produced by directly invoking real Lucene's own `LowercaseAsciiCompression.compress` from the pinned 10.5.0 jar (real Lucene *bytes*, just not embedded in an on-disk segment) -- see `decompress_lowercase_ascii_matches_real_lucene_compress_output`/`decode_block_lowercase_ascii_compressed_suffixes` in `blocktree.rs`. A hand-built (this port's own `lz4::compress`-round-tripped) vector additionally covers the LZ4 dispatch path directly (`decode_block_lz4_compressed_suffixes`). **Ordered enumeration (`TermsEnum.next()`) and nearest-match seeking (`seekCeil()`) are now ported** -- `FieldTerms::iter()` returns a `TermsEnum` cursor (`next()`/`seek_ceil()`/`current()`) over the field's already-sorted `entries` `Vec`. **Design choice**: this is a thin index-bump/binary-search cursor over the Vec the prior slice already materializes, not a reimplementation of real `SegmentTermsEnum`/`SegmentTermsEnumFrame`'s stack-based lazy block-walk -- the eager-whole-field-materialization tradeoff was made by the prior slice, and once every term is already in one sorted Vec, replicating Java's per-frame FST/trie-path push/pop machinery on top of it would only reintroduce complexity this port deliberately avoided (see the `rust-performance` skill). Fixture-verified against the `many` field (400 terms, multi-block/floor-split) via real `TermsEnum.next()` -- the full 400-term ordered sequence (term bytes + docFreq/totalTermFreq) matches exactly, proving enumeration walks block/floor boundaries in the right order and not just within one block -- and `seekCeil()` against four real-Lucene-verified cases (exact match, a between-terms ceiling match, before-the-first-term, and after-the-last-term/`END`); no decode bug surfaced this time, matching on the first real-Lucene run (see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`). Unit tests cover cursor edge cases no real fixture reaches: an empty field, a single-term field, `seekCeil()` followed by `next()` continuing from the landed-on position, and `next()` called repeatedly past the end staying idempotent. Per-term postings-metadata bytes are decoded by `crate::postings::decode_term_metadata` per block (threaded across each block's own entries, `absolute` true only for each block's first entry -- blocks never share metadata state) and threaded into `FieldTerms`, which exposes `FieldTerms::postings(term, doc_in)`/`positions(...)` alongside `seek_exact`'s stats. Fixture-verified against a real `IndexWriter` (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java`): "body"/"id"/"big"/"pos" (unchanged from the prior slice, all single-block) plus the new "many" field above, sampled across its range (first/last, several mid values spanning different trie branches and floor sub-blocks) and checked exhaustively (all 400 terms independently looked up) against real `TermsEnum.seekExact`/`docFreq`/`totalTermFreq`; see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs`. Unit tests cover the new trie-decode primitives directly (hand-built single-child-with-output+floor, all three multi-children strategies incl. a `REVERSE_ARRAY` gap case, an end-to-end two-floor-block `open()` round trip, and corruption paths -- invalid strategy code, child-delta-exceeds-parent-fp, trie-nesting-depth guard) that no small real fixture reaches. **Wildcard/prefix automaton-shaped intersection is now ported, scoped to glob matching over the already-materialized `Vec`, not real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton`.** `FieldTerms::intersect(&WildcardPattern) -> impl Iterator<Item = (&[u8], TermStats)>` (`crates/lucene-codecs/src/blocktree.rs`) narrows `entries` to the sorted sub-range starting with the pattern's literal prefix (two `partition_point` binary searches -- free, since `entries` is already sorted for `seek_exact`; see the new `prefix_upper_bound` helper) and then linearly filters that range against `crate::wildcard::WildcardPattern` (`crates/lucene-codecs/src/wildcard.rs`, new module), a from-scratch glob matcher (`*` = zero-or-more bytes, `?` = exactly one Unicode codepoint (1-4 UTF-8 bytes, falling back to 1 byte on invalid UTF-8), everything else literal) plus a `WildcardPattern::prefix()` constructor for pure `PrefixQuery` semantics. **Design tradeoff, stated plainly**: this is *not* `CompiledAutomaton`/`ByteRunAutomaton` DFA compilation and *not* real `IntersectTermsEnum` trie-block-skipping -- real Lucene can visit only the `.tip`/`.tim` blocks a compiled automaton's reachable states could lead to, potentially sub-linear in dictionary size; this port's `intersect` is `O(n)` in the field's term count once the literal-prefix range is applied, degrading to a full field scan for a pattern with no literal prefix (e.g. `*foo`); the per-candidate `WildcardPattern::matches` cost itself is *not* `O(1)` -- it's a backtracking matcher that is multiplicative (`O(term.len()^k)`), not additive, in the number of `*` tokens `k` (see `wildcard.rs`'s own doc comment), so a pattern with several `*`s against long terms is a genuine unguarded pathological case, not just a theoretical one. This mirrors the same "correctness first, honest about what's actually optimized" stance the postings work took (see the `postings.rs` row's lazy-cursor slices) rather than transliterating Java's per-frame automaton-driven stack machine on top of a representation (one eagerly sorted `Vec`) that no longer matches it -- reusing the existing `entries` `Vec`/binary-search idiom `seek_exact`/`TermsEnum` already established, not a new automaton-shaped subsystem. **Also deliberately out of scope this slice**: no regex (`RegexpQuery`) and no fuzzy/Levenshtein automaton (`FuzzyQuery`) -- both need a real automaton/edit-distance representation that's a materially larger scope than glob matching over a sorted `Vec`; (task #34 added `\`-escape support for a literal `*`/`?`/`\` byte, matching real `WildcardQuery.toAutomaton`'s `WILDCARD_ESCAPE` handling exactly -- see the task #34 row below). Fixture-verified against real `WildcardQuery`/`CompiledAutomaton.getTermsEnum` ground truth (`fixtures/src/GenBlockTree.java::appendWildcardIntersectManifest`, extended "many" field, 400 terms) for four patterns: an exact prefix run (`term037*`), a `*`-suffix pattern equivalent to a `PrefixQuery` (`term039*`), a `?` single-char wildcard (`term010?`), and a pattern matching zero terms (`zzz*`) -- `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs::many_field_wildcard_intersect_matches_real_lucene_wildcard_query`, matched on the first real-Lucene run. Unit tests (`wildcard.rs`) cover the matcher's own edge cases directly: empty pattern (matches only the empty term), pure `*` (matches everything including empty), literal-only pattern, `?` boundary cases (including on an empty term), `*` at the start/middle/end, adjacent `*`s collapsing to one, non-UTF-8 byte matching, and `literal_prefix()` extraction; `blocktree.rs` adds `intersect_prefix_and_wildcard_over_materialized_field` (prefix/`?`/mid-`*`/match-everything/match-nothing-in-range/match-nothing-out-of-range/exact-pattern/`WildcardPattern::prefix()` cases over a hand-built multi-term field) and `prefix_upper_bound_handles_ff_bytes_and_empty` (the `0xFF`-byte-run and empty-prefix corner cases the real fixture's ASCII terms never reach) |
| `codecs/lucene104/Lucene104PostingsWriter`, `codecs/lucene103/blocktree/Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter` (`.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` write side) | `lucene-codecs/src/postings_writer.rs::write_single_field` | **write path started, narrowly scoped to a single field, single `.tim` block, term-frequency-only postings.** Given one field's already-tokenized/inverted term dictionary (`FieldPostingsInput { field_number, index_options, doc_count, terms: &[TermPostings] }`, each `TermPostings` a term's bytes plus its `(doc_id, freq)` pairs sorted ascending by `doc_id`), produces `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` bytes. **Exactly proven correct, no more**: (1) **single field per call** -- `numFields = 1` in `.tmd`; (2) **single `.tim` block, single trie node** -- every term must fit in one physical leaf block, and `.tip` is one root `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN` node with `hasTerms` set and no floor data (block-splitting, floor sub-blocks, and multi-level tries are not implemented -- a real writer would split once past `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter`'s min/maxItemsInBlock thresholds, this one never does); (3) **`docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE` (256) for every term** -- only the group-varint "tail block" encoding is ever written (`Lucene104PostingsWriter`'s `flushDocBlock(true)` branch that never reaches `docBufferUpto == BLOCK_SIZE`); no full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-bit-packed blocks, no skip data, no impacts are ever produced, and a term at or above `BLOCK_SIZE` docs is rejected with `Error::DocFreqTooLarge` rather than silently producing wrong bytes; (4) **term frequency only, no positions/offsets/payloads** -- only `IndexOptions::Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` are accepted (`Error::UnsupportedIndexOptions` otherwise), `.pos`/`.pay` are never written; (5) **`docFreq == 1` is pulsed into the term dictionary**, matching the real writer exactly -- no `.doc` bytes at all for a singleton term, `postings::singleton_postings` reads it back purely from the per-term metadata. The per-term postings-metadata bytes always take the bit-clear ("absolute-ish `docStartFP` delta") branch of `decodeTerm`'s encoding, never the zigzag-singleton-delta branch -- a correct but less compact simplification, since this writer has no need for that branch's extra savings. **Caller obligations, not re-validated beyond what's checked**: `terms` must already be sorted ascending by term bytes with no duplicates (checked, `Error::TermsNotSorted`), each term's `docs` must be sorted ascending by doc ID with no duplicates (checked, `Error::DocIdsNotSorted`) and every `freq >= 1` (checked, `Error::NonPositiveFreq`) -- `doc_count` itself (the field-level distinct-docs count written to `.tmd`) is taken as given from the caller, not cross-checked against `terms`. **Does not duplicate the read side's decode logic** -- it only emits bytes; correctness is proven entirely by round-tripping through the *existing, unmodified* `blocktree::open`/`postings::DocInput::open`/`postings::singleton_postings`, the same functions real Java-Lucene fixtures are opened with elsewhere in this port. Unit-tested in `postings_writer.rs` (mixed singleton/multi-doc terms; `IndexOptions::Docs`-only totalTermFreq aliasing; an all-singleton field needing no `.doc` file at all; the `doc_start_fp` delta-threading correctness across 20 terms/5 docs each; every validation-rejection path). **The required end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`** (this crate must not depend upward on `lucene-search`, see the `architecture` skill): `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::term_query_finds_correct_docs_over_freshly_written_postings` writes a 3-term field with a mix of singleton and multi-doc terms via `write_single_field`, opens it with the unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::open`, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_term_query` (the same public query entry point real-fixture tests use) for every term plus a missing term, asserting the exact doc-ID sets Lucene's own `TermQuery`/`PostingsEnum` would return; a second test (`term_query_respects_live_docs_filter`) confirms the written postings compose correctly with a `.liv`-style deletion bitset. **Not verified against real Lucene bytes** -- unlike every read-side row in this table, there is no `fixtures/src/Gen*.java` generator for this writer (there is nothing for it to differentially test against: the point of a first write-side slice is proving this port's own writer and this port's own unmodified reader agree, not that this port's writer produces byte-identical output to `Lucene104PostingsWriter`/`Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter` -- those writers' actual on-wire choices, e.g. singleton run-length compression, real block-splitting thresholds, are known not to be replicated here, see above). **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing**: multi-block terms (`docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`, full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil` blocks, skip data, impacts), multi-block/floor-split/multi-child-trie term dictionaries (more than one field or more than one `.tim` block/`.tip` node), positions/offsets/payloads (`.pos`/`.pay`), suffix compression, and singleton run-length stat encoding -- all separate future slices. **Now wired into `IndexWriter::commit()`** (follow-up task, see PLAN.md): `IndexWriter::set_postings_field(Some(field_name))` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) opts a writer into calling this function for exactly one field of every segment `commit()` flushes, sourcing `TermPostings` from `crate::indexing_chain::invert_documents` over that field's `FieldValue::String` values -- the same one-field/single-`.tim`-block/`docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE`/term-frequency-only scope above, unchanged, now reachable from a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` call rather than only from hand-built test input. A `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` term in one commit's pending-doc batch makes the whole `commit()` fail atomically (nothing written), rather than silently truncating. **Still not wired for more than one field per commit** -- `IndexWriter` has no per-field file-suffix machinery to fan this out, so a second call to `set_postings_field` simply replaces the first rather than adding a second indexed field. **Merge-policy interaction, fixed during review**: `execute_merge`/`merge_stored_only_segments` have no `.doc`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` awareness at all, so a segment carrying postings could otherwise be silently merged away with no error the moment automatic merge triggering (task #71) fires -- `segment_stats()` now excludes any segment whose `.si` lists a `.doc` file from `find_merges`' candidate pool entirely, keeping it permanently un-mergeable rather than mergeable-with-silent-data-loss. Covered by `segments_with_postings_are_never_automatically_merged_away`, which enables both `set_postings_field` and `set_merge_policy`, crosses the merge threshold with postings-carrying commits, and asserts the segment count never drops and every `.tim` file survives. Required end-to-end proof: `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_postings_fixtures.rs::documents_added_via_index_writer_are_searchable_by_term_query` adds documents via `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` (not a hand-built fixture) and runs `lucene_search::search_term_query` against the result, plus a sibling test proving the `docFreq >= 256` commit is rejected. | **Positions write-side added (this task): `.pos` now supported, still term-frequency-scoped in every other way.** `write_single_field` accepts `IndexOptions::DocsAndFreqsAndPositions` in addition to `Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` (`DocsAndFreqsAndPositionsAndOffsets` still rejected with `Error::UnsupportedIndexOptions` -- offsets/payloads remain unimplemented on the write side, a further deferred layer). `TermPostings` gained a `positions: Vec<Vec<i32>>` field, parallel to `docs`: each entry is a doc's absolute, ascending occurrence positions (e.g. `[0, 3, 4]`), required to have exactly `docs.len()` entries with `positions[i].len() == docs[i].1` (that doc's freq) whenever `index_options` indexes positions (`Error::MissingPositions`/`Error::PositionsFreqMismatch` otherwise); left empty for `Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs` fields. Scoped identically to the existing `.doc` tail-block restriction: **`total_term_freq < BLOCK_SIZE` (256) for every term with positions** -- only the vint-tail encoding (`refillLastPositionBlock`) is ever written, never a full `ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-encoded `.pos` block; a term at or above that bound is rejected with `Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`. A singleton term (`docFreq == 1`, pulsed out of `.doc`) still gets real `.pos` bytes when it indexes positions -- position data is independent of the `.doc` singleton optimization. Per-term metadata (`write_term_metadata`) now also threads a running `pos_start_fp` delta exactly like `doc_start_fp`, written whenever the field indexes positions. **Still not reimplementing the read side**: correctness is proven by round-tripping through the existing, unmodified `postings::read_positions`/`blocktree::FieldTerms::positions`. Unit-tested in `postings_writer.rs` (position round-trip via `read_positions` covering a singleton term with multiple occurrences and a multi-doc term with a position-accumulator reset between docs; every new rejection path). **The required phrase-query end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::phrase_query_finds_correct_docs_over_freshly_written_positions` writes a 3-term field (`"fox"`/`"jumps"`/`"quick"`) across two docs that share every term but only align adjacently in one of them, opens it through the unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::open`/`PosInput::open`, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_phrase_query` for `["quick", "fox"]`, `["fox", "jumps"]`, and `["quick", "jumps", "fox"]`, asserting the exact doc each phrase matches -- including the negative case where both docs contain every term but only one doc has them in that exact adjacent order, proving this isn't just a doc-ID conjunction. **`IndexWriter` wiring explicitly NOT touched by this task**: `IndexWriter::build_postings_output` (`crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`) still only ever builds term-frequency-only `TermPostings` (`positions: Vec::new()`, `set_postings_field` still only accepts `Docs`/`DocsAndFreqs`) -- a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` session still cannot produce a `.pos` file yet; wiring positions into `IndexWriter` (sourcing per-doc position lists from `invert_documents`'s already-recorded `PostingEntry::positions`) is left for a follow-up task. **Multi-field support added (this task): `numFields > 1` in `.tmd` is now supported.** `write_single_field` is now a one-element-slice wrapper over the new `write_fields(inputs: &[FieldPostingsInput], segment_id, segment_suffix) -> Result<Output>`, which loops the same per-field write steps (unchanged) over every element of `inputs`, appending each field's `.doc`/`.pos` tail blocks and `.tim` block/`.tip` root node into the *same* shared byte buffers and writing one `.tmd` field record per field. **Per-field limits are exactly as before and apply independently to each field** -- every field is still capped at a single `.tim` block/root trie node, `docFreq < BLOCK_SIZE` (256), and (if it indexes positions) `total_term_freq < BLOCK_SIZE`; none of these bounds are shared or relaxed across fields, and a field violating its own bound still fails the whole call (`Error::DocFreqTooLarge`/`Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`) as before. Multi-block terms and multi-level tries remain out of scope (a separate, still-deferred slice). Unit-tested in `postings_writer.rs` (`write_fields_two_fields_share_one_tmd_and_stay_isolated`: two fields, one with positions, one without, opened via the unmodified `blocktree::open` and checked independently). **The required end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::multi_field_segment_term_queries_are_isolated_per_field` writes a "title" field (`DocsAndFreqs`) and a "body" field (`DocsAndFreqsAndPositions`) in one `write_fields` call, where both fields index a term with the *same bytes* ("rust") but different postings, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_term_query`/`search_phrase_query` against both fields in the same segment, asserting each field's results are correct and that neither field's postings leak into the other's lookups. **`IndexWriter` wiring NOT touched by this task**: `IndexWriter::set_postings_field` still only tracks one configured field per commit (unchanged) -- extending it to multiple fields is a separate follow-up, not attempted here. **Multi-block writer added (this task): a field's terms can now span more than one physical `.tim` block, addressed by a `SIGN_MULTI_CHILDREN` `.tip` root, not just one block/one `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN` root.** Splitting policy, deliberately the simplest one that stays correct without floor blocks or a second trie level: `write_fields` groups a field's (already-sorted) terms by their **first byte** (`group_terms_by_leading_byte`). A field with only one leading byte (or one term, or a term with zero bytes -- there's no leading byte to strip/route on) still gets the original single-block/single-`SIGN_NO_CHILDREN`-root shape, byte-for-byte unchanged (verified: none of the pre-existing single-block tests changed behavior, since their fixtures already exercise both shapes -- e.g. `mixed_singleton_and_multi_doc_terms_round_trip`'s "fox"/"quick"/"the" already has 3 distinct leading bytes and was already taking the multi-block path even before this task added a dedicated test for it). A field spanning 2..=33 distinct leading bytes gets one leaf `.tim` block per group (`write_tim_block`, parameterized by `strip_prefix_len` so the same function serves both the single-block case, prefix length 0, and each group, prefix length 1 -- a block only ever stores the bytes *after* its shared leading byte, matching `crate::blocktree::collect_leaf_blocks`'s "a block only stores its own suffix" contract on the read side), each addressed by its own `SIGN_NO_CHILDREN`/`hasTerms`/no-floor leaf node (`write_leaf_node`), with the field's `.tip` root being a single `SIGN_MULTI_CHILDREN` node with no output of its own (`write_multi_children_root`, always `ChildSaveStrategy::ARRAY` -- the simplest of the three label encodings `crate::blocktree::multi_children_labels_and_fps` supports on the read side; `BITS`/`REVERSE_ARRAY` are never emitted). Each block's per-term metadata delta-threading (`doc_start_fp`/`pos_start_fp`) resets fresh per block, matching `SegmentTermsEnumFrame`'s per-frame reset the read side (`decode_block`) already assumes -- blocks never share metadata state, whether split by floor (not implemented here) or by sibling leaf block (this task). **Explicitly still unimplemented, narrowed further than a first cut might suggest**: floor sub-blocks (a single leading-byte group with too many terms for one block -- this writer has no notion of a per-block term-count cap at all, so an enormous single-leading-byte group still produces one arbitrarily large block, not a floor split); a second/deeper trie level (a field needing more than 33 distinct leading bytes is rejected outright with `Error::TooManyLeadingByteGroups` rather than silently misencoding the multi-children node's 5-bit `strategyBytes-1` header field, which can only address 2..=33 children); and the `BITS`/`REVERSE_ARRAY` label-encoding strategies. This is a deliberately narrower scope than "any field exceeding one block's term-count capacity splits automatically" -- the chosen policy (group by leading byte) is the simplest split that maps cleanly onto a *single-level* multi-child trie without floor data, at the cost of only working when a field's terms are naturally spread across enough distinct leading bytes (true of essentially any real natural-language field, false in principle for a pathological field where thousands of terms share one leading byte). **Proof, mirroring the single-block slice's own bar**: `postings_writer.rs::many_leading_byte_groups_force_multi_child_trie_root` (26 terms, one per lowercase letter -- 26 physical `.tim` blocks under one multi-child root, every term independently looked up through the unmodified `blocktree::open`, not just first/last), `rejects_field_needing_more_than_33_leading_byte_groups`, and `empty_term_falls_back_to_single_block_even_with_other_distinct_leading_bytes`. **The required end-to-end proof lives in `lucene-search`**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/postings_writer_round_trip.rs::term_query_finds_correct_docs_across_multiple_tim_blocks` writes the same 26-leading-byte-group field, opens it through the unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::open`, and runs the unmodified `lucene_search::search_term_query` for terms in the first, a middle, and the last physical block plus a missing term, proving every block is independently reachable and correctly decoded through the real query layer, not just that the writer's own bytes decode in isolation. **Not verified against real Lucene bytes**, same caveat as every other row segment above -- this proves the port's own writer and the port's own unmodified reader agree on a multi-block/multi-child-trie shape, not that it's byte-identical to what `Lucene103BlockTreeTermsWriter`'s real min/maxItemsInBlock-threshold-driven splitting would produce for the same input. **`IndexWriter` wiring NOT touched by this task**: `IndexWriter::build_postings_output`/`set_postings_field` are unchanged -- a real `IndexWriter::add_document`/`commit()` session still only ever produces single-field output via the (now multi-block-capable) `write_single_field`/`write_fields`, so this new splitting path already reaches `commit()` for whatever field is configured, but wiring a *second* configured field or otherwise changing `IndexWriter`'s own scope is a separate follow-up, not attempted here. **Full-block `.doc` doc-delta/freq emission added (this task): `docFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE` (256) is no longer rejected.** `write_full_block` (new) emits, for every complete 256-doc chunk of a term's postings, a level-0 skip header (`level0NumBytes` skip pointer -- any valid vlong, unused by the reader; `docDelta`/`blockLength` via new `write_vint15`/`write_vlong15` helpers, the exact write-side inverse of `postings::read_vint15`/`read_vlong15`) followed by the doc-delta/freq body, reusing `for_util::for_encode` (doc deltas) and `for_util::pfor_encode` (freqs) directly -- no bit-packing logic is reimplemented here, only called. **Encoding choices, stated plainly**: doc deltas always take the plain positive-`bitsPerValue` `ForUtil` shape; this writer never emits the `bitsPerValue == 0` ("all-256-consecutive") or `bitsPerValue < 0` (dense unary bit-set) alternate encodings the real writer picks for space efficiency (both already decode correctly on the read side, see the `postings.rs` row above, but this writer doesn't choose them) -- one correct, always-decodable shape was chosen over replicating every space-optimization the real writer has. Impacts are always an empty byte region (no competitive-impact computation at all); the reader accepts a zero-length impacts run and decodes it to an empty list, so this is valid, just not space- or query-optimized. The `docFreq % BLOCK_SIZE` remainder still uses the pre-existing group-varint tail-block path, with `prev_doc_id` now threaded from the last full block's last doc ID instead of always `-1`. **The per-term upper bound moved, not disappeared**: `validate_field` now rejects at `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (8192, `Error::DocFreqTooLarge`'s condition changed accordingly) rather than `>= BLOCK_SIZE`, since this writer still never emits the level-1 skip entries `postings.rs`'s reader expects to find interleaved above that threshold -- a term that large would round-trip incorrectly, so it is still rejected rather than silently misencoded. **Positions still explicitly out of scope for full blocks**: `total_term_freq >= BLOCK_SIZE` is still rejected with `Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge`, unchanged -- a term reaching the new `.doc` full-block path can never also need a `.pos` full block in the same call regardless (`total_term_freq >= doc_freq` always), so this is a real, not merely theoretical, non-interaction, not an oversight. **Proof, mirroring the existing bar**: unit tests in `postings_writer.rs` cover `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE` (one full block, no tail), `docFreq == BLOCK_SIZE + 1` (one full block plus a one-doc tail), `docFreq == 600` (two full blocks plus an 88-doc tail, exercising full-block-to-full-block `prev_doc_id` chaining, not just full-block-to-tail), a full block with `IndexOptions::Docs` (no freqs, no impacts field, no `pfor_encode` call), and small/full-block terms mixed in one field -- every one of these round-trips through the *existing, unmodified* `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::read_postings`, the same functions real Java-Lucene fixtures are opened with elsewhere in this port, asserting every decoded doc/freq exactly, not just "opened without erroring". **No new `fixtures/src/Gen*.java` generator was added for this task** -- deliberately: the existing "big"/"everywhere" fixture field (`docFreq == 300`) already forces the real Lucene *writer*'s own full-block path and fixture-verifies the *reader* side (`postings.rs`) against it; this task's job was proving this port's *own* new writer output is byte-compatible with this port's *own* already-fixture-verified reader, which is a Rust-only round-trip question (no new wire-format understanding is being claimed, unlike a decoder task) -- the same reasoning the original single-block writer slice gave for having no generator of its own (see this row's first paragraph). `for_util.rs`'s `for_encode`/`pfor_encode`/`bits_required` lost their `#[allow(dead_code)]` markers now that a real production caller exists. **Still explicitly deferred**: `.pos` full-block emission (`total_term_freq >= BLOCK_SIZE`, see above -- currently provably unreachable from this writer's own `.doc` full-block path, not merely unimplemented); real competitive-impact computation; the all-consecutive/dense-bitset alternate doc-delta encodings; `IndexWriter` wiring (`set_postings_field`/`build_postings_output`) is untouched by this task, so a real `add_document`/`commit()` session still cannot reach a `docFreq >= 256` term without separately tripping `flush_stored_only_segment`'s own pre-existing, unrelated `write_best_speed` `< 128`-docs-per-flush-chunk cap first -- see `crates/lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs`'s `commit_succeeds_below_the_doc_freq_boundary` test doc comment and `crates/lucene-search/tests/index_writer_postings_fixtures.rs`'s trailing comment for the full explanation of why no end-to-end `IndexWriter`-level test of the new boundary exists. **Level-1 skip-entry emission added (this task): `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (8192) is no longer rejected, and there is no further per-term docFreq ceiling.** `write_level1_span` (new) emits, before every complete span of `LEVEL1_FACTOR` (32) full level-0 blocks, a level-1 skip entry -- the exact write-side inverse of the existing, unmodified `postings::read_level1_entry`/`LazyDocsCursor::skip_level1_to`. The entry's vlong byte-length field is the one subtle part: `read_level1_entry` computes `doc_end_fp` as that field's value added to the reader's position measured *right after* the vlong itself, i.e. before the freq-gated `skip1EndFP`/`numImpactBytes` fields are read -- so the vlong must span every byte from there through the end of the whole entry plus its 32-block span, not just the span's own bytes (this writer's first draft got that wrong, undercounting by the 4 header bytes, caught by an `advance()` landing 33 docs off from the expected target). **Same encoding choices as level-0**: the level-1 entry's impacts region is always empty (`numImpactBytes = 0`, no competitive-impact computation at either level -- the reader accepts a zero-length impacts run); the `indexHasPos`-gated pos/pay sub-fields `read_level1_entry` supports are never written, because they're provably unreachable from this writer -- a term reaching `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` has `total_term_freq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS`, which would already have tripped `Error::TotalTermFreqTooLarge` had it indexed positions (the same non-interaction argument `write_full_block`'s own doc comment gives for its level-0 header). **`validate_field`'s docFreq bound is removed entirely, not merely raised**: `postings.rs`'s reader has no level-2 skip structure at all (`Lucene104` postings only ever have levels 0 and 1), so there is nothing left for a further ceiling to protect against -- a term spanning any number of level-1 spans plus a final partial span round-trips exactly like a sub-8192 term always did. **Proof, mirroring the level-0 bar**: unit tests in `postings_writer.rs` round-trip `docFreq == LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (one span, no remainder), `LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS + 1` (one span plus a one-doc tail), and `2 * LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` (two spans back to back, exercising `level1_last_doc_id`/`prev_doc_id` threading across more than one span) through the existing, unmodified `blocktree::open`/`DocInput::read_postings`, asserting the exact doc/freq lists; the same three boundaries are re-proven through `LazyDocsCursor::advance` (`docfreq_at_level1_boundaries_advance_via_lazy_cursor`); and `writer_level1_span_advance_past_it_skips_corrupted_first_block_header` writes a real span, corrupts its first level-0 block's header bytes in place, and confirms `advance()` past the whole span still succeeds (never decoding the corruption) while `advance()` into the span surfaces it -- the write-side mirror of `postings.rs`'s own `lazy_cursor_advance_skips_whole_corrupted_level1_span_without_decoding_it` proof. **No new `fixtures/src/Gen*.java` generator**, same reasoning as the level-0 task: this is a Rust-only "writer and already-fixture-verified reader agree" question, not a new wire-format claim. **Still explicitly deferred**: real competitive-impact computation (both levels' impacts regions stay empty), the all-consecutive/dense-bitset alternate doc-delta encodings, `.pos` full-block emission, and `IndexWriter` wiring -- `set_postings_field`/`build_postings_output` are untouched by this task, and reaching `docFreq >= LEVEL1_NUM_DOCS` via a real `add_document`/`commit()` session was already unreachable before this task (blocked by `flush_stored_only_segment`'s own unrelated `< 128`-docs-per-flush cap) and remains so.

**Recommended next slice**: step back to a different Phase -- see below for why the wildcard/prefix intersection slice just landed is intentionally not followed by more work in this same subsystem. Glob-based wildcard/prefix term intersection (`FieldTerms::intersect`, `crate::wildcard::WildcardPattern`) landed this slice: a linear scan (narrowed by a literal-prefix binary-search range) over the already-materialized `entries` `Vec`, covering `PrefixQuery` exactly and `WildcardQuery`'s `*`/`?` glob subset, fixture-verified against real `WildcardQuery`/`CompiledAutomaton.getTermsEnum` output on the "many" field (see the `blocktree.rs` row above for the full writeup). This was explicitly scoped down from real `IntersectTermsEnum`/`CompiledAutomaton` automaton-driven trie-block-skipping (deferred, see that row) and does not include regex (`RegexpQuery`) or fuzzy/Levenshtein (`FuzzyQuery`) automata, both flagged as separate future slices requiring real automaton/edit-distance machinery rather than glob matching. Three reasonable next moves: (1) **regex or fuzzy automaton support**, building a real byte-level automaton/edit-distance representation now that glob/prefix has proven the `FieldTerms::intersect` shape works end-to-end against real Lucene; (2) **real `IntersectTermsEnum`-style trie-block-skipping**, replacing today's "scan the sorted `Vec`" approach with one that walks only the `.tip` trie nodes/`.tim` blocks an automaton's reachable states could lead to -- valuable once a field is large enough that `O(n)` scanning actually shows up in a profile, not before; (3) **step back to a different Phase entirely** -- this subsystem (`postings.rs`/`blocktree.rs`/`for_util.rs`/`wildcard.rs`) has now had a very long consecutive run of slices (level-0/level-1 skip data, positions, lazy cursors, enumeration, impacts, and now wildcard intersection), and PLAN.md's other Phase-1/2 read-path formats (points/BKD query execution, doc-values-backed sorting, or the actual `IndexSearcher`/`Weight`/`Scorer` plumbing that would let any of this get exercised end-to-end against a real query) are likely higher-value to de-risk before this subsystem's next increment -- this is the option this slice's own author recommends. Also still open but narrower: a real-fixture-verified full-`ForUtil`/`PForUtil`-block position path (`totalTermFreq >= BLOCK_SIZE`, currently only unit-tested).

## lucene-index

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `codecs/lucene99/Lucene99SegmentInfoFormat` (`.si` read + write) | `lucene-index/src/segment_info.rs::{parse, write}` | **both directions ported.** `write` is the exact byte-level inverse of `parse`, emits `numSortFields = 0` unless `SegmentInfo::index_sort` is set (single-field index sort, see below), and does not re-validate that `files` entries are segment-name-prefixed (callers are trusted, matching the parser's own stance) -- exercised via own-reader round-trip unit tests. **Verified against real Lucene in the write→read direction** (unsorted case only, see below): `crates/lucene-index/examples/write_segment_info_fixture.rs` writes two `.si` files (`_0`: compound file, with minVersion, with diagnostics/files/attributes; `_1`: non-compound, with `hasBlocks`, no minVersion, everything else empty) and `fixtures/src/VerifySegmentInfo.java` opens them directly through `Lucene99SegmentInfoFormat.read` and confirms every property matches each segment's manifest -- passed on the first real-Lucene run |
| `index/SegmentInfo.indexSort` / `SortField`/`SortFieldProvider` (multi-field NUMERIC index sort, `.si` encoding) | `lucene-index/src/segment_info.rs::{IndexSortField, SortMissingValue, read_sort_field, write_sort_field}`, `SegmentInfo::index_sort: Option<Vec<IndexSortField>>` | **partial, NUMERIC-fields-only (any count).** Task #49 supported exactly one NUMERIC `SortField`; task #52 extended this to a real multi-field `Sort` -- `numSortFields` is written/read genuinely (0, or N priority-ordered `SortField` descriptors), matching real Lucene's `Sort` being an array of `SortField`s applied in order. Only NUMERIC fields are supported; any other `SortType` byte is rejected as `Error::UnknownSortFieldType` (arbitrary `SortFieldProvider` decoding would need either a matching plugin registry or a hard-coded allowlist this port doesn't have). **Byte-format status: NOT verified against real Lucene.** Real Lucene's index-sort `.si` bytes are written by pluggable `SortFieldProvider` Java classes and no real-Lucene-written sorted-segment `.si` fixture exists under `fixtures/` to derive the true byte layout from, for either a single-field or a multi-field sort -- the `SortField` encoding this port reads/writes (now repeated N times) is **this port's own internal format** (round-trip-correct against its own `parse`/`write`, confirmed by unit tests in `segment_info.rs` including 2- and 3-field round trips with mixed reverse/missing policies), not a byte-compatible port of `Lucene99SegmentInfoFormat`'s real encoding. A real Lucene reader would not be able to open a `.si` this port writes with an index sort set, and vice versa. Closing this gap needs either a real sorted-index `.si` fixture (to derive the true `SortFieldProvider` wire format) or accepting the divergence permanently and documenting it as this port's own extension. |
| `index/DocumentsWriterPerThread` sort-on-flush (physically reordering a flushed segment's documents by the index sort) | `lucene-index/src/segment_writer.rs::flush_sorted_stored_only_segment`, `SortKeySpec` | **partial.** Takes a non-empty, priority-ordered slice of `SortKeySpec`s (one per sort field, each with its own field name, in-memory `&[Option<i64>]` per-doc sort key, `reverse`, and `SortMissingValue`), stable-sorts the whole batch by comparing field 0 first and falling through to field 1, field 2, etc. only on a tie at every prior tier (ties/both-missing-at-every-tier keep original relative order), reorders stored fields accordingly, and records the full sort in the flushed `.si`. Each field's `reverse`/missing-value policy is applied independently at its own tier -- one field can be descending with missing-last while another is ascending with missing-first, matching real Lucene's per-`SortField` configuration. This port has no write-side doc-values format yet, so each field's sort keys can't be read back from an already-written file the way real Lucene's `DocValuesConsumer`-fed sort does -- they must already be in memory, parallel to `docs`. No query-side early-termination optimization either (irrelevant to correctness in this port regardless of index sort support). |
| `index/SegmentMerger` sort-preserving merge (k-way merge of already-sorted segments by the shared index sort) | `lucene-index/src/merge.rs::{merge_sorted_stored_only_segments, MergeSortKeySpec, compare_heads}` | **done, stored-fields-only scope (task #53, closing the gap task #49/#52 explicitly deferred).** Given `sort_fields` (one `MergeSortKeySpec` per priority tier, each carrying every source's per-doc sort key for that field, `reverse`, and `SortMissingValue`) and a list of `MergeSource`s, performs a genuine k-way merge: at each step it picks whichever source's current (undeleted) head doc has the smallest key across all tiers -- comparator logic reused, not reimplemented, via `crate::segment_writer::sort_key_rank` (made `pub(crate)` for exactly this reuse) -- and appends that doc, so the merged output is globally sorted across every source, not source A's docs followed by source B's. Field-number reconciliation and deleted-doc dropping work exactly as in `merge_stored_only_segments`. The merged `.si` correctly keeps `index_sort: Some(...)` (the concatenating `merge_stored_only_segments` still always writes `index_sort: None`, since it does not preserve sort order). **Precondition, not re-checked by this function:** every source must already be internally ordered by the same `sort_fields` key (true for anything written by `flush_sorted_stored_only_segment` or a previous call to this same function) and every source must share the same index sort as every other (real Lucene's hard "same sort or reject the merge" rule) -- the caller is responsible for having verified this (e.g. comparing each source's own `SegmentInfo.index_sort`); this function has no dependency on `SegmentInfo` and does not attempt to detect an out-of-order or mismatched source. **Scope: stored fields only**, matching this port's existing write-side limit -- doc values, norms, and term vectors attached to a `MergeSource` are silently ignored by this function (unaffected: still only reachable via `merge_stored_only_segments`'s concatenation-order merge). **No new Java fixture**: this is composition of two already-verified primitives (task #52's sort-key comparator, task #15/#37/#38's segment-writing path), following the precedent of prior composition tasks (#36-38, #47) -- unit-tested instead: two sources with interleaved keys where naive concatenation would visibly break sort order (confirmed the real merge doesn't), three sources, a primary-field tie broken by a secondary field, `.si` index-sort-descriptor preservation, deleted-doc dropping mid-merge, field-number reconciliation during the k-way walk, an empty-sources edge case, and a dedicated check that a multi-field document's content stays attached to the correct doc through reordering (not shuffled independently of its sort key). |
| `index/SegmentInfos` (`segments_N` read: header/footer, per-segment commit metadata, user data) | `lucene-index/src/segment_infos.rs` | ported (read-only), fixture-verified against a real 2-commit `IndexWriter` output |
| `index/DocumentsWriterPerThread`/`IndexingChain` (tokenize + build an in-memory inverted index from indexed field text) | `lucene-index/src/indexing_chain.rs::{InMemoryInvertedIndex, PostingEntry, invert_documents}` | **in-memory only, no persistence path (task #63) -- read this status carefully before assuming more.** `invert_documents` runs each `(doc_id, field, text)` triple through a `lucene_analysis::Analyzer` and groups the result into `InMemoryInvertedIndex { terms: BTreeMap<(field, term), Vec<PostingEntry>> }`, each `PostingEntry` holding a doc's `doc_id` plus its occurrences' resolved absolute positions and character offsets (`term_freq()` = occurrence count) -- the same per-term/per-doc grouping shape real Lucene's `TermsHashPerField`/`FreqProxTermsWriterPerField` build while indexing. `lucene-index/Cargo.toml` gained a `lucene-analysis` path dependency (clean downward edge, `lucene-analysis` has zero workspace deps). **This does NOT make documents indexed/searchable via analyzed text**: `segment_writer.rs` still has no write-side postings encoder (every flushed field remains `IndexOptions::None`, unchanged by this task, per that module's own "what this deliberately is not" section), so there is no code path from `InMemoryInvertedIndex` to any file on disk -- this structure cannot be persisted or read back until a postings writer exists (tracked separately, task #75). The output shape (doc-ID-sorted `Vec<PostingEntry>` per term, each with freq/positions/offsets) is chosen to match exactly what `Lucene104PostingsWriter`'s `.doc`/`.pos`/`.pay` encode needs as input, so that future writer can consume it directly. **Verified by unit tests only** (composition of task #61's already cross-engine-verified `Analyzer` plus this task's new grouping logic, same precedent as task #62's `query_parser.rs` wiring -- no new Java fixture): single doc/field exact shape, multiple docs sharing a term produce a doc-ID-sorted list, a repeated term's `term_freq`/positions are all recorded (not just the first occurrence), independent per-field entries for the same term text (no cross-field merging), and stopword-filtered text excludes the stopword while preserving surviving tokens' positions (reusing `StopFilter`'s position-increment-preservation guarantee). Coverage: `indexing_chain.rs` 100% lines. |
| `index/SegmentInfos.write` | `lucene-index/src/segment_infos.rs::write` | **ported.** Byte-level inverse of `parse`, always emits `VERSION_CURRENT` (so the SciId marker byte is always written, matching `parse`'s expectation for this format) and derives the `segments_N` file name from `generation` via the existing `lucene_store::directory::segments_file_name` helper rather than re-deriving the base-36 suffix a second time. Unlike `segment_info::write`/`field_infos::write` (which return `Vec<u8>` and let the caller route bytes through a `Directory`), this one takes a `&dyn Directory` directly and performs the write-then-sync itself: a `segments_N` file's correctness as a *commit* depends on being fsynced before it's durable, mirroring real `IndexWriter.commit()`'s write-then-`Directory.sync` sequencing rather than leaving that easy-to-forget step to the caller. Unit-tested by round-tripping through `parse` via a real `FsDirectory` (empty commit, single segment, multi-segment with SciId/del-counts/DV-update-files/user-data, generation-0 plain `segments` name, negative-generation rejection). **This is also the milestone verified by `crates/lucene-index/examples/write_segment_infos_fixture.rs` + `fixtures/src/VerifySegmentInfos.java`: a genuinely complete single-segment index (`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` + `.fnm` + `.si` + `segments_N`, reusing the already-verified `stored_fields::write_best_speed`/`field_infos::write`/`segment_info::write`) opened via real, high-level `DirectoryReader.open(FSDirectory.open(path))` -- not hand-built codec-level access -- succeeded on the first run, confirming doc count and stored field values through ordinary `IndexReader`/`StoredFields` calls.** The fixture's fields are deliberately stored-only (`IndexOptions::None`, no doc values/term vectors/points/vectors): `SegmentCoreReaders` (`org.apache.lucene.index.SegmentCoreReaders`) only opens a `FieldsProducer` when `FieldInfos.hasPostings()` is true, so a segment with zero indexed fields needs no `.tim`/`.tip`/`.doc` postings files at all -- this port has no postings/doc-values/points/vector *write* path yet (those remain read-only, see the rows above), so a fully-indexed segment (a real `TextField`, sorted doc values, etc.) is not yet achievable through `DirectoryReader.open`; only the stored-fields-only case was in scope for this milestone and is what's verified |
