| `index/IndexWriter` (unifying add/update/delete/commit facade) | `lucene-index/src/index_writer.rs::IndexWriter` | **facade over already-built primitives, not a reimplementation of any of them.** `IndexWriter::open(dir, fields, codec_name, lucene_version)` resumes an existing commit (via `lucene_store::directory::last_commit_generation`, distinguishing "no commit yet" from "a commit file exists but is corrupt") or starts a fresh empty index; `add_document` buffers in memory; `commit()` flushes the buffer through the existing `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment` and writes the updated segment list via the existing `segment_infos::write`; `update_document`/`delete_documents` delegate straight to the existing `update_document::update_document`/`term_delete::resolve_and_apply_term_delete` + `deletes::apply_deletes`, unchanged; `apply_merge` folds an already-executed `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` result back into the writer's committed state. Every one of those underlying functions existed before this task -- this module's only new logic is the state threading (current `SegmentInfos`, buffered docs, segment-name counter) that previously had to be hand-carried by each caller/test across calls. Segment/commit ids are generated by hashing a monotonic counter with the current time (`DefaultHasher`, not a CSPRNG) since this workspace has no `rand` dependency and the only property a segment id needs here is uniqueness across a session, not statistical randomness. **Update (automatic merge triggering):** `IndexWriter::set_merge_policy(Some(config))` now opts a writer into automatic merging -- every subsequent `commit()`, right after writing its own `segments_N`, loops calling the existing `merge_policy::find_merges` against the writer's now-committed segments (stats built from each segment's `.si` via `segment_info::parse` + `merge_policy::segment_byte_size`, plus `del_count` already in memory) and, for each proposed group, executes it via the existing `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` and folds the result in via the existing `apply_merge`, repeating until `find_merges` proposes nothing further (guaranteed to terminate: every merge strictly shrinks the segment count). With no merge policy set (the default a freshly-opened writer starts with), `commit()` is byte-for-byte unchanged from before this feature, so none of the original tests needed updating. New tests: no-merge-policy commits never auto-merge; a commit sequence staying at/under `segments_per_tier` stays unmerged; a sequence crossing it merges down to fewer segments with every original document still readable; and 20 consecutive single-document commits under a tight policy converge without panicking or looping (segment count never exceeds commit count). **Explicitly deferred, not silently missing:** no merge-policy configurability from `open()` itself (only via the separate `set_merge_policy` setter), no concurrent/background merging, no multi-tier scheduling beyond one `merge_policy::find_merges` call, `update_document`/`delete_documents` do not trigger this check (only `commit()` does), no RAM-based flush triggering (only an explicit `commit()` flushes), no multi-threaded `DocumentsWriterPerThread`-style pooling, and `update_document`/`delete_documents` still only resolve against segments the caller supplies an opened `SegmentDeleteSource` for (inherited from `update_document.rs`/`term_delete.rs` -- no reader pool that opens every segment automatically). **No new Java fixture** (composition of already-verified primitives, same precedent as `update_document.rs`/`merge.rs`): unit tests cover opening a fresh directory, add+commit producing one readable segment (read back both through the returned struct and by re-reading `segments_N` off disk), a no-pending-documents commit still producing a valid next generation, multiple commits producing multiple independent, non-colliding segment names, resuming a writer against an already-committed directory without a segment-name collision, `update_document`/`delete_documents` against the same real-Lucene postings fixture `term_delete.rs`/`update_document.rs` already use (including a failing delete leaving the writer's in-memory state and on-disk `segments_N` untouched), and `apply_merge` folding a real `merge_stored_only_segments` result over two committed segments back into the writer. `SegmentInfos`/`SegmentCommitInfo` gained `PartialEq` (needed to assert a failed call left state byte-for-byte unchanged) -- a mechanical addition, no behavior change. **Update (postings/term-vectors/doc-values wiring):** `set_postings_field`, `set_term_vector_field`, and `set_doc_values_field` (NUMERIC only) each opt a writer into building and writing real postings/term vectors/doc values for one field per commit, respectively -- see this crate's/`lucene-codecs`'s own parity rows above for each feature's exact scope. All three can be configured at once, in the same or different fields, in one commit. `segment_stats()` excludes any segment carrying `.doc`/`.tvd`/`.dvd` files from automatic-merge candidacy, since `execute_merge` only merges stored fields. **Update (`rollback()`):** `IndexWriter::rollback(&mut self)` discards every document buffered by `add_document` since the last `commit()` -- a pure in-memory reset of `pending_docs` only, never touching `dir`/`segment_infos` (no `segment_infos::write` call). Writer configuration (`set_postings_field`/`set_term_vector_field`/`set_doc_values_field`/`set_merge_policy`) and any prior commit's segments both survive a rollback untouched, matching real Lucene's split between `IndexWriterConfig` (survives) and buffered documents (discarded). **Not replicated**: real `IndexWriter.rollback()` also closes the writer and releases its write lock permanently; this facade has no open/close lifecycle at all, so `rollback()` leaves the writer fully usable for further `add_document`/`commit()` calls. New tests: rollback discards pending docs so the next commit is empty of them; rollback with nothing pending is a safe no-op; rollback after a prior commit leaves that commit's segment untouched while discarding a second, uncommitted batch; and rollback preserves postings/term-vector/doc-values/merge-policy configuration for a later commit. **Update (two-phase commit, `prepare_commit()`/`finish_commit()`):** `commit()` is now `prepare_commit()` immediately followed by `finish_commit()`, kept as one call for backward compatibility -- every existing caller/test is unchanged. `prepare_commit()` does everything `commit()` used to do (flush `pending_docs` via `flush_stored_only_segment`, build/write postings/term-vectors/doc-values files) *except* the final `segment_infos::write` call, and stashes the resulting in-memory `SegmentInfos` in a new `prepared_commit: Option<SegmentInfos>` field; `finish_commit()` takes that stashed value and calls `segment_infos::write` (the one call that actually produces the next `segments_N`), then runs auto-merge exactly as `commit()` always has. **Honest scope, read before relying on this for anything crash-related**: real `IndexWriter.prepareCommit()`/`SegmentInfos.prepareCommit` write a `pending_segments_N` file plus enough on-disk state that a *new process* opening the index after a crash can discover a prepared-but-not-yet-committed generation and roll it forward or back. This port's `segment_infos::write` has no `pending_segments_N` equivalent and no `segments.gen` pointer file -- there is exactly one kind of `segments_N`, and "what's current" is simply "the highest-numbered `segments_N` that exists" (`lucene_store::directory::last_commit_generation`/`segment_infos::read_latest`). That does make the split genuinely meaningful, not cosmetic: after `prepare_commit()` returns, the new segment's data files are durably on disk and synced, but no `segments_N` references them yet, so a fresh `IndexWriter::open`/reader against the same directory still sees only the previous commit. But `prepared_commit` lives purely in the live `IndexWriter` value's memory -- if the process crashes (or the value is dropped) between `prepare_commit()` and `finish_commit()`, that prepared state is gone with no on-disk trace to recover, discover, or roll forward; the orphaned segment files are just inert bytes no `segments_N` ever points at. So: real caller-visible durability/visibility split, yes; crash-survivable two-phase commit or cross-process/cross-restart handoff, no. `finish_commit()` without a preceding `prepare_commit()` (or called a second time) returns `Error::NoPreparedCommit` rather than silently no-opping. New tests: `prepare_commit()` + `finish_commit()` produces byte-identical on-disk results to calling `commit()` directly (compared against two independent directories fed the same docs), including confirming the prepared generation is invisible to a fresh reader until `finish_commit()` runs; `prepare_commit()` alone (simulating a crash before activation) leaves the previous commit as the only one a fresh `read_latest`/reopened writer sees; `finish_commit()` with no prior `prepare_commit()`, and a second `finish_commit()` right after a successful one, both return `Error::NoPreparedCommit`; and a second `prepare_commit()` before `finish_commit()` replaces the pending prepared state rather than stacking. **Update (FFI exposure):** `open`/`add_document`/`commit`/`prepare_commit`/`finish_commit`/`rollback`/`set_merge_policy` are now reachable over the C ABI too -- see the `lucene-ffi/src/writer.rs` row below for the exact wire shape and what is not exposed. |
| `lucene-ffi` C-ABI wrapper over `IndexWriter` (IndexWriter commit/merge-policy/postings/term-vector/doc-values/update/delete FFI exposure) | `lucene-ffi/src/writer.rs::{ffi_open_writer, ffi_writer_add_document, ffi_writer_commit, ffi_writer_prepare_commit, ffi_writer_finish_commit, ffi_writer_rollback, ffi_writer_set_merge_policy, ffi_writer_set_postings_field, ffi_writer_set_term_vector_field, ffi_writer_set_doc_values_field, ffi_writer_update_document, ffi_writer_delete_documents, ffi_writer_segment_infos_len, ffi_writer_segment_info_name, ffi_writer_pending_doc_count, ffi_close_writer}` | Wraps seven `IndexWriter` methods behind a new opaque handle (`registry::WriterHandle`, `handle::RegistryTag::Writer`), same `guard`/`catch_unwind`/last-error/handle-validation conventions every other module in this crate already follows -- no write-side logic reimplemented. `ffi_open_writer` takes a filesystem path plus a caller's field list as five parallel arrays (name, number, `IndexOptions` ordinal, `DocValuesType` ordinal, store-term-vectors flag); `ffi_writer_add_document` takes one document's fields as four parallel arrays, with a `kind` byte per field selecting how its raw bytes decode (string/binary/i32/i64/f32/f64). Because `IndexWriter<'d>` borrows `&'d dyn Directory` and there is no owned/`'static` `IndexWriter` type, `WriterHandle` owns a heap-boxed `FsDirectory` alongside the writer and builds the writer's borrow against that stable heap address via one contained, documented `unsafe` block (`writer.rs::open_writer_handle`) -- sound because struct field declaration order guarantees the borrowing `writer` field drops before the owning `dir` field ever does. `WriterHandle` also needed explicit (documented) `unsafe impl Send/Sync`, since a bare `&dyn Directory` carries no auto-trait bound the compiler can see on its own, even though this crate's `Mutex`-guarded, one-thread-at-a-time access pattern makes both sound. `SlotMap::get_mut` -- previously `#[cfg(test)]`-only, since every earlier handle type was immutable once inserted -- is now a real (non-test) part of the crate's handle API, since a writer handle's whole point is in-place mutation across calls. **Update (postings/term-vector/doc-values FFI exposure):** `ffi_writer_set_postings_field`/`ffi_writer_set_term_vector_field`/`ffi_writer_set_doc_values_field` now wrap `IndexWriter::set_postings_field`/`set_term_vector_field`/`set_doc_values_field` too, one C function per setter, each taking an `enabled` flag (mirroring `ffi_writer_set_merge_policy`'s own `enabled == 0` -> `None` convention) plus a `(field_name, field_name_len)` pair decoded via this crate's existing `str_from_raw`; `enabled == 0` clears the setting (`None`), ignoring the name/length arguments. Caller-input errors these three can now surface (`UnknownPostingsField`/`UnsupportedPostingsIndexOptions`/`UnknownTermVectorField`/`UnsupportedTermVectorField`/`UnknownDocValuesField`/`UnsupportedDocValuesType`/`MissingDenseDocValue`/`NonNumericDocValue`/`NonBinaryDocValue`) all map to `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`, extending `map_writer_error`'s existing status-mapping table. Tests: unknown-handle rejection and a disabled (`enabled == 0`) no-op for each of the three, an unknown-field-name rejection for each, and one real end-to-end test per setter (`set_postings_field_end_to_end_writes_readable_postings`, `set_term_vector_field_end_to_end_writes_readable_term_vectors`, `set_doc_values_field_end_to_end_writes_readable_numeric_values`) that opts a field in over FFI, adds documents and commits over FFI, then reads the resulting segment back Rust-side through this crate's own unmodified read side (`lucene_codecs::blocktree`/`postings`, `lucene_codecs::term_vectors::open`, `lucene_codecs::doc_values::parse_meta`/`numeric_value` respectively) to prove the field was genuinely written, not just that the FFI call returned `Ok`. **Update (update_document/delete_documents FFI exposure):** `ffi_writer_update_document`/`ffi_writer_delete_documents` now wrap `IndexWriter::update_document`/`delete_documents`. Both take `(field_name, field_name_len, term_ptr, term_len)` identifying the delete term as raw, already-analyzed bytes (no analysis happens at this FFI boundary, same stance as `query.rs`'s own raw-bytes terms); `ffi_writer_update_document` additionally takes the replacement document's fields via the same four parallel arrays/`kind` byte convention `ffi_writer_add_document` already uses. Neither is buffered -- both commit immediately on success, matching `IndexWriter::update_document`/`delete_documents`'s own atomicity. Since `SegmentDeleteSource` requires an opened `BlockTreeFields`/`DocInput` per segment (`update_document.rs`'s own scope: only segments the caller supplies an opened source for are considered), this FFI layer builds that itself: a new `writer.rs::open_all_segment_sources` reopens every one of the writer's currently-committed segments that has a `.tim` file on disk (i.e. was flushed with `ffi_writer_set_postings_field` enabled at that commit), plus its `.liv` if one exists; a segment with no `.tim` file is skipped, not errored, matching `SegmentDeleteSource`'s own "unlisted segment left untouched" contract. `IndexWriter` gained two small read-only accessors, `dir()`/`fields()`, so this FFI-side helper can reopen those files and know the field schema to decode postings against, without either becoming part of the writer's mutable surface. Tests: unknown-handle and null-field-name rejection for both, a real end-to-end `ffi_writer_update_document` test (add two docs with real postings on `id`, commit, update one by term over FFI, then read every live doc back through this crate's own unmodified `stored_fields`/`live_docs` read side to confirm the old doc is gone and the new one present), a real end-to-end `ffi_writer_delete_documents` test (same shape, proving only the matching doc is removed), and a no-postings-segment no-op test (deleting against a writer whose only segment was flushed stored-only leaves `del_count` at `0`, proving the "skip, don't error" contract). **Update (segment_infos/pending_doc_count introspection FFI exposure):** `ffi_writer_segment_infos_len`/`ffi_writer_segment_info_name` now wrap `IndexWriter::segment_infos` (length-then-per-index-name accessor, the same "length first" shape `results_fragments.rs`'s `ffi_fragment_results_len`/`ffi_fragment_result_text` already established), and `ffi_writer_pending_doc_count` wraps `IndexWriter::pending_doc_count`. Both are read-only, infallible aside from handle/index/buffer validation. Tests: unknown-handle rejection and null-out-pointer rejection for all three, an out-of-bounds segment index, a too-small name buffer (`BufferTooSmall`, nothing written), and one end-to-end test (`segment_infos_and_pending_doc_count_reflect_writer_state_across_commits`) confirming 0 segments/0 pending on a fresh writer, 2 pending after two buffered `add_document` calls with 0 segments before any commit, 1 segment named `_0`/0 pending right after the first commit, and 2 segments after a second commit. **Still deliberately not exposed, tracked here rather than silently missing:** `IndexWriter::apply_merge` has no FFI wrapper. `apply_merge` only makes sense once a caller has already run `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` to produce the `SegmentCommitInfo` it folds in, and this crate exposes no FFI surface to run that merge (merging today only ever happens automatically, inside `commit()`, via `ffi_writer_set_merge_policy`) -- wrapping `apply_merge` alone would be a bookkeeping-only call a JVM caller could never actually drive. Manual merge execution FFI (and `apply_merge` alongside it) is left as a separate, larger task. `ffi_open_writer`'s field-schema wire format is deliberately minimal: every `FieldInfo` flag beyond name/number/index-options/doc-values-type/store-term-vectors (`omit_norms`, `store_payloads`, `soft_deletes_field`, `parent_field`, points/vector dimensions) is fixed at its off/default value, since this task's field list only needs to support stored-fields-only documents. `ffi_writer_set_merge_policy` exposes exactly the four knobs `lucene_index::merge_policy::MergePolicyConfig` has today (`max_merge_at_once`, `segments_per_tier`, `max_merged_segment_size`, `reclaim_weight`) -- no additional real-`TieredMergePolicy` knobs (`floorSegmentMB`, `forceMergeDeletesPctAllowed`, etc.) are invented, since this port's `merge_policy.rs` does not implement them either. Tests: null-pointer rejection (`open_writer_null_out_handle_is_null_pointer_error`, `open_writer_null_field_array_with_nonzero_count_is_null_pointer_error`, `add_document_null_array_with_nonzero_count_is_null_pointer_error`), invalid-UTF-8 path rejection, out-of-range enum-ordinal rejection, invalid/unknown-handle rejection for every one of the eight functions, double-close rejection, a cross-registry rejection (a directory handle passed to a writer function), and a real end-to-end test (`open_add_commit_end_to_end_produces_a_readable_segment`) that opens a writer over FFI, adds documents over FFI, commits over FFI, then reopens the same on-disk directory Rust-side (`segment_infos::read_latest` + `lucene_codecs::stored_fields::open`, bypassing the FFI writer handle entirely) and reads every document back to confirm the commit is genuinely valid and queryable, not just `Ok`-returning. Two more end-to-end tests cover the two-phase commit split and the merge-policy convergence behavior the same way. |

## lucene-search

| Java | Rust | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `search/TermQuery` (matching + BM25 scoring) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::TermQuery`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_term_query, search_term_query_scored}` | **ported.** Plain `{ field, term }` struct — no `TermStates`/cross-segment stats attached (nothing to reuse them for yet). `search_term_query` (matching only) is unchanged; `search_term_query_scored` is its new scored sibling (task #13): same field/term/`live_docs` handling, additionally reading each matched doc's `freq` and computing a BM25 score via `similarity::score` (see that module's row for the norms/avg-field-length approximation every score here inherits) into a [`ScoringCollector`]. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/scoring_fixtures.rs` scores the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment and asserts (a) the scored doc set exactly equals the already-fixture-verified unscored doc set, (b) `TopDocsCollector` output is correctly ordered (score descending, doc ID ascending on ties), and (c) every score matches a BM25 formula reimplemented independently in the test file from the segment's real `docFreq`/`doc_count`/per-doc `freq` — not real-Lucene score equality (deferred, see the norms gap above), but full internal-consistency and formula-fidelity verification against real postings data. |
| `index/DocumentsWriterPerThread.flush` + `IndexWriter.commit` (minimal, no-merge multi-segment slice) | `lucene-index/src/segment_writer.rs::flush_stored_only_segment` | **ported, deliberately minimal.** `flush_stored_only_segment` takes an in-memory `Vec<Document>` + `Vec<FieldInfo>` and writes one brand-new stored-fields-only segment (`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm`/`.si`, all synced through a real `Directory`), returning the `SegmentCommitInfo` to push into `SegmentInfos::segments`. Calling it more than once against the same `Directory` with distinct segment names/ids and passing all the resulting `SegmentCommitInfo`s to one `segment_infos::write` call produces a single commit describing multiple, independently-flushed segments -- proven by `crates/lucene-index/examples/write_multi_segment_commit_fixture.rs` (two flushes, `_0` with 2 docs + `_1` with 3 docs, one `segments_N`) opened via real `DirectoryReader.open` + `fixtures/src/VerifySegmentInfos.java` (unchanged from the single-segment case -- it was already segment-count-agnostic, and passed first try: `DirectoryReader.open` correctly federates the two Rust-written segments into one 5-doc space). Note `segment_infos::write`/`parse` needed **no changes** for this: `SegmentInfos::segments` was already `Vec<SegmentCommitInfo>` with a plain loop on both the encode and decode side, so describing N segments in one commit was already mechanical; the actual gap this closes is the reusable "flush one batch of documents to one new segment" building block (previously hand-duplicated per fixture example -- `write_segment_infos_fixture.rs` now calls this same function instead of inlining its own copy). **Deliberately not implemented, out of scope for this slice** (see the module doc for the full list): no RAM accounting/automatic flush-triggering, no merging (`TieredMergePolicy`/`ConcurrentMergeScheduler`), no deletes/updates during indexing (`BufferedUpdates`), no NRT reopen, no concurrent `DocumentsWriterPerThread`-per-thread pooling, and -- same constraint as the single-segment fixture below -- every field is stored-only, since there is still no write-side postings/doc-values/points/vectors format. **Compound-file packing (task #38):** `flush_stored_only_segment` now takes a `use_compound_file: bool`. `false` (unchanged) writes the four files loose; `true` packs those same already-complete codec files through `compound_format::write` (task above) into `<name>.cfs`/`.cfe` instead and sets `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file: true` in the `.si`. Real Lucene's `IndexWriter` decides this per-flush via `TieredMergePolicy`'s size-based `noCFSRatio`/`maxCFSSegmentSizeMB` heuristic; this port has no merge policy or segment-size accounting at all yet (`PLAN.md` Phase 5 item 6), so rather than fake a heuristic with nothing real behind it, the caller decides directly with a plain boolean -- `update_document.rs` passes `false`, keeping its existing commits' on-disk shape unchanged. No new Java fixture needed since `compound_format`'s codec itself is already differentially verified (see its row above); this task is Rust-side composition, verified end-to-end by a unit test that flushes with `use_compound_file: true`, recovers the `.fnm`/`.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` bytes *through* `compound_format::parse_entries`/`open_input` (not the original in-memory buffers), and confirms both `field_infos::parse` and `stored_fields::open`/`.document()` still work reading through those recovered slices, plus a regression test confirming `.si`/loose-file output for `use_compound_file: false` is unchanged (`.cfs`/`.cfe` files absent, `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm` present) |
| `index/SegmentMerger` | `lucene-index/src/merge.rs::merge_stored_only_segments` | **ported, scoped to exactly what's mergeable today.** Merges N already-flushed segments into one new segment: reads each source's `FieldInfos` (`field_infos::parse`) and `Document`s back out (`stored_fields::open` + `.document()`), drops non-live docs per an optional per-source `FixedBitSet` (`live_docs::parse`), reconciles field numbering across sources by field name (`reconcile_field_numbers`), renumbers surviving docs contiguously by concatenating sources in source order, and writes `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm`/`.si`. **Field-number reconciliation**: does the numbering half only (first-seen-across-sources order, one merged `FieldInfo` per distinct name using the first source's metadata) and skips real Lucene's `verifySameSchema` check. **Edge cases**: a source with no `live_docs` is treated as fully live; a fully-deleted source contributes zero docs (merged anyway rather than requiring the caller to pre-filter). Now also merges doc values, norms, and term vectors, if a caller supplies them per source (`MergeSource::numeric_doc_values`/`norms`/`term_vectors`, all optional): decodes each source's per-doc data via the existing read-side decoders (`doc_values::numeric_value`, `norms::norm_value`, `term_vectors::TermVectorsReader::document`), drops non-live docs and renumbers contiguously the same way stored fields are, remaps field numbers through the same reconciliation, and re-encodes via the existing single-field write-side encoders (`doc_values::write_single_dense_numeric_field`, `norms::write_single_dense_field`, `term_vectors::write_best_speed`), writing whichever of `.dvm`/`.dvd`/`.dvs`, `.nvm`/`.nvd`, `.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm` result. **Scope of the doc-values/norms merge**: since the underlying write-side encoders only support one field per `.dvd`/`.nvd` file (no multi-field container yet), at most one numeric-doc-values field and at most one norms field may be merged per call (`Error::TooManyNumericDocValuesFields`/`TooManyNormsFields` otherwise); term vectors have no such limit. **Sparse-across-sources rule**: a doc-values/norms field can only be merged if every source contributing at least one live doc supplies decodable, fully-dense data for that field (matches the write-side encoders' dense-only requirement) -- a source missing the field, or only sparsely populating it, is `Error::DocValuesFieldMissingInSource`/`NormsFieldMissingInSource` rather than a silent drop. Term vectors have no such constraint: a source with no term-vectors reader, or a doc with none, contributes an empty `TermVectorsDocument`. **Important caveat**: this port's only write-side path that produces a full segment, `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment`, still only ever writes stored-fields-only segments -- nothing in this port's normal flush path produces doc values/norms/term vectors yet, so this merge logic is exercised only by its own unit/round-trip tests supplying synthetic per-source data, not by a real "flush two segments, then merge them" scenario. Unit-tested: field-number reconciliation in isolation; stored-fields merging (two segments no deletions, some docs deleted in each, a fully-deleted source, mismatched field numbers reconciled end-to-end through a re-parsed `.fnm`, zero sources, a real `.liv` round trip); numeric doc values, norms, and term vectors each merged in isolation (two sources, deletions, a source missing the field/reader entirely); the too-many-fields and missing-in-a-live-source error paths; and one full round-trip test merging stored fields + doc values + norms + term vectors together via real `Directory` I/O, verified by reading back every format through this port's own readers, including checking the `.si` file lists every written file. **Deliberately not implemented**: no merge *policy* (`TieredMergePolicy`-style "which segments, when" -- the caller picks sources), no background/concurrent merging, no merge-time codec upgrade, no multi-field `.dvd`/`.nvd` support, and no points/postings/binary-or-sorted-doc-values/offsets-or-payloads-term-vectors merging |
| `index/TieredMergePolicy.findMerges`/`findForcedMerges` (merge-set decision, not execution/scheduling) | `lucene-index/src/merge_policy.rs::{find_merges, find_forced_merges}` | **ported (task #47), a simplified but real-shaped scoring/selection algorithm, not naive size-only bin-packing and not a byte-for-byte port of real Lucene's own (considerably more complex) algorithm.** Decides which currently-existing segments should merge next; execution stays `merge.rs`'s job (its own doc comment already flagged "not a merge policy" as out of scope -- this closes that gap), and background/concurrent scheduling (`MergeScheduler`) remains untouched. **New `SegmentStat` type, not `SegmentCommitInfo` directly**: `SegmentCommitInfo` (`segments_N`) carries `del_count` but not doc count or byte size -- those live in the separate per-segment `.si` file (`segment_info::SegmentInfo`); `SegmentStat` (name/doc_count/del_count/size_bytes) is the minimal shape the algorithm needs, built from either. **Size-unit decision**: real `TieredMergePolicy` sizes segments by on-disk byte size (`segBytes`); this port provides `segment_byte_size(dir, info)`, which sums real file lengths for a segment's `.si`-listed files through the existing `Directory` trait (no new trait method needed) for the honest, byte-accurate case, and `SegmentStat::from_segment_info` as a documented doc-count approximation for callers without a `Directory` handy -- the algorithm itself is unit-agnostic, it only needs a monotonic comparable size. **Kept real-shaped**: already-oversized segments (>= `max_merged_segment_size`) excluded from further merge input; a reclaim-weighted score (`size * (1 - reclaim_weight * del_count/doc_count)`) so a heavily-deleted segment is preferred over an equally-sized clean one, matching real Lucene's intent of favoring merges that reclaim deleted space; a `segments_per_tier` target suppressing merges once segment count is already at/below it; a `max_merge_at_once` cap no proposed group ever exceeds; smaller/more-deleted segments preferred by sorting before grouping. **Simplified/dropped, explicitly**: real Lucene's exact `MergeScore` (log-based skew penalty, floor/ceiling tier smoothing, iterative multi-candidate search with rollback) replaced by one simpler score; one greedy grouping pass instead of an iterative multi-merge search; no compound-file awareness; `find_forced_merges` merges the excess down to a target count in a single group rather than real Lucene's own chunked multi-pass forced-merge walk. `MergePolicyConfig` defaults mirror real `TieredMergePolicy`'s (`maxMergeAtOnce=10`, `segmentsPerTier=10`, `maxMergedSegmentMB=5000`). **Closing the loop with `merge.rs`**: `lucene-index/tests/merge_policy_to_merge_integration.rs` flushes three real stored-fields-only segments, has `find_merges` pick all three, and feeds that exact chosen name group into `merge::merge_stored_only_segments` (re-reading each segment's files off disk by name), confirming the merged segment holds all six docs -- proves the decide/execute handoff has no shape mismatch, without building a full automatic merge-triggering pipeline (real `IndexWriter`/`MergeScheduler` integration remains out of scope). This is a pure heuristic decision function, not new byte-format decoding, so no Java fixture applies -- correctness here means matching the documented simplified rules, verified by direct unit tests (many-small-segments proposes a merge, oversized segment excluded, high-del-ratio preferred over equal-size low-del-ratio, already-optimal segment count proposes nothing, `max_merge_at_once` cap respected). |
| `index/IndexWriter` deletes (doc-ID-level mechanics, plus single-segment delete-by-term resolution) | `lucene-index/src/deletes.rs::{mark_deleted, apply_deletes}`, `lucene-index/src/term_delete.rs::{resolve_term_doc_ids, resolve_and_apply_term_delete}` | **ported: doc-ID-level apply mechanics (task #16) plus single-segment delete-by-term resolution (task #27).** Real Lucene's delete path is two halves: (1) `BufferedUpdates`/`ReaderPool` resolve *which* doc IDs a `deleteDocuments(Term/Query)` call names, per segment, by running the query against that segment's live postings/doc-values reader; (2) `ReadersAndUpdates.writeLiveDocs` takes the resolved doc IDs and turns them into an updated live-docs bitset, a new `.liv` file, and a bumped `delGen`/`delCount`. `deletes.rs` is half (2): `mark_deleted` clears the given doc IDs out of a `FixedBitSet` (starting from "all live" when the segment has no deletions yet, i.e. `del_gen == -1`, or from an existing bitset otherwise), returning the updated bitset plus a count of *newly* deleted docs (already-deleted doc IDs are idempotent, not double-counted); `apply_deletes` wraps that around a `SegmentCommitInfo`, writing the result via the existing `live_docs::write` to a **newly established filename convention** (`liv_file_name`: `_<segment>_<delGen in base36>.liv`, matching real Lucene's `IndexFileNames.fileNameFromGeneration(segment, "liv", delGen)`) and returning a new `SegmentCommitInfo` with `del_gen` incremented (`-1` -> `1` on first delete, else `+1`, matching `SegmentCommitInfo.getNextDelGen()`) and `del_count` increased by the newly-deleted count. Out-of-range doc IDs are a hard `Err`, never a silent no-op or a panic. `term_delete.rs` is (part of) half (1), **scoped to exactly one already-opened segment**: `resolve_term_doc_ids` takes that segment's `BlockTreeFields` + opened `.doc` file + a `(field, term)` pair and returns the matching live doc IDs ascending -- an unknown field or an absent term yields an empty `Vec`, not an error, matching `TermQuery.createWeight`'s `null`-`Scorer` "no matches" outcome. This reimplements the same lookup `lucene-search::term_doc_ids` already does (`field.postings(term, doc_in)` filtered by `live_docs`) directly against `lucene-codecs` primitives (`BlockTreeFields`, `DocInput`) rather than depending on `lucene-search` from `lucene-index`: the intended dependency graph is `util ← store ← codecs ← index ← search ← core ← ffi`, and `lucene-search` already depends on `lucene-index`, so the reverse edge would invert it into a cycle -- since every primitive the lookup needs already lives in `lucene-codecs`, which `lucene-index` depends on directly, reimplementing the handful of lines there avoids both the cycle and a speculative new shared-primitive extraction in `lucene-codecs`. `resolve_and_apply_term_delete` composes `resolve_term_doc_ids` with `apply_deletes` for the full per-segment resolve-then-apply flow, finally closing the "here's a term to delete" -> "here's the actual `mark_deleted`/`apply_deletes` call" gap for one segment. **Deliberately not implemented**: true multi-segment *resolution* (a real `IndexWriter`'s `BufferedUpdates`/`ReaderPool` opens and searches every currently-open segment's live postings reader itself; this port has no reader pool, so a caller of `update_document` — see the row below — still has to hand it whichever segments' `BlockTreeFields` it already has open) and delete-by-query beyond a single exact term. `updateDocument` itself is now implemented as an atomic wrapper — see `lucene-index/src/update_document.rs` below — fanning the per-segment delete-by-term resolution here out across a whole `SegmentInfos`'s segment list and committing it together with a new segment in one `segments_N` write. Unit-tested (`deletes.rs`): `mark_deleted` from an all-live (`None`) state, from an existing partially-deleted bitset, idempotent re-deletion of an already-deleted doc, boundary doc IDs (`0`, `max_doc-1`), out-of-range and negative doc IDs (both `Err`), empty doc-ID batch, plus full round-trip tests via a real `FsDirectory` (first delete round, second round incrementing `del_gen` and unioning with the first, re-deleting the same doc not double-counting, an out-of-range doc ID erroring without writing a file). 99.51% line coverage. Unit-tested (`term_delete.rs`), reusing the checked-in real-Lucene `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture: `resolve_term_doc_ids` for a multi-doc term, a singleton term needing no `.doc` file, a missing term, a missing field, and `live_docs` filtering out an already-deleted doc; `resolve_and_apply_term_delete` end to end against a real `FsDirectory` (`del_gen`/`del_count`/`.liv` bytes all correct for the term's actual matching docs), deleting the same term twice across two rounds confirming `del_gen` increments without double-counting already-deleted docs, and a term with no matches producing a no-op round that still bumps `del_gen`. 98.78% line coverage. |
| `index/IndexWriter` delete-by-point-range resolution (BKD, single segment) | `lucene-index/src/points_delete.rs::{resolve_points_range_doc_ids, resolve_and_apply_points_range_delete}` | **ported (task #36).** The BKD-range analog of task #27's `term_delete.rs`, same two-halves split: `resolve_points_range_doc_ids` is (part of) half (1), scoped to one already-opened segment's `lucene_codecs::points::PointsReader` + one `field_number` + an inclusive `[min_packed, max_packed]` packed-byte range (`PointRangeQuery`'s own default `newRangeQuery` semantics) — decodes every point via the existing `PointsReader::decode_all_points`, keeps only points where **every** dimension's slice independently satisfies `min[dim] <= value[dim] <= max[dim]` (unsigned byte-wise, matching `Arrays.compareUnsigned` and `PointRangeQuery.matches`), filters by `live_docs`, and returns the matching doc IDs ascending and deduplicated (a multi-valued point field can put more than one matching value on the same doc). An unknown `field_number` yields an empty `Vec`, not an error, same "no matches, not a caller bug" convention `term_delete` uses. `resolve_and_apply_points_range_delete` composes that with `deletes::apply_deletes`, the same resolve-then-apply shape as `resolve_and_apply_term_delete`. **Reused vs. newly written, stated plainly**: unlike delete-by-term, where `lucene-search::term_doc_ids` already existed and `term_delete.rs` just reimplemented its handful of lines locally (to avoid `lucene-index` depending back on `lucene-search` — confirmed again here by reading both `Cargo.toml`s: `lucene-search` depends on `lucene-index`, not the reverse), **no BKD range-query matcher existed anywhere in the workspace to reuse**: `lucene-search`'s only range-shaped queries (`search_numeric_range`/`search_sorted_ord_range`/`search_multi_valued_range` in `doc_value_query.rs`) walk doc-values data, the "slow" `SortedNumericDocValuesField.newSlowRangeQuery` fallback path real Lucene uses when no BKD index exists — not the BKD tree at all; and `lucene_codecs::points` has no intersection/pruning logic either, only the already-existing `PointsReader::decode_all_points` (decodes every point in a field unconditionally, see `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/points_fixtures.rs`). So this module's range-matching logic (`packed_value_in_range`) is genuinely new, reusing only `decode_all_points` as its data source — a real, honest gap against real `BKDReader.intersect`'s tree-pruning traversal (which can skip whole leaves/subtrees the packed index proves are entirely in/out of range): this port's approach is `O(field's total point count)` per call, not sublinear, tracked here rather than hidden. **Cross-engine verification approach**: no new checked-in real-Lucene fixture — the existing `fixtures/data/points_index/` fixture (task #18/#22, `GenPoints.java`) is single-dimension only, and this module's own tests need a hand-built 2D (`LatLonPoint`-shaped) fixture anyway to exercise the "every dimension independently in range" semantics that fixture can't reach; extending it with a new `Append*Manifest.java` would add Java-side machinery without covering anything the in-memory fixture (built via the existing, already real-Lucene-verified `points::write`/`points::open` round trip from task #18/#22) doesn't already cover byte-for-byte. Unit-tested: exact range match, inclusive boundaries on both ends, a zero-match range (no-op, empty `Vec`), a range matching every doc, an unknown field number, `live_docs` filtering an already-deleted doc out of the match set, a 2D multi-dimension field where one dimension alone would over-match but the AND-across-dimensions rule correctly excludes it, and end-to-end `resolve_and_apply_points_range_delete` against a real `FsDirectory` (`del_gen`/`del_count`/`.liv` bytes correct, plus a zero-match round still bumping `del_gen`). 99.38% line coverage. **Deliberately not implemented**: multi-segment resolution and delete-by-query beyond a single field's point range, same scope limits as `term_delete.rs`. |
| `search/PointRangeQuery` (search-side, single already-opened segment) | `lucene-search/src/points_query.rs::search_points_range` | **ported (task #81), the read-only, non-deleting sibling of task feeds matches through this crate's existing `Collector` trait instead of returning a bare `Vec<i32>` — the same "feed matches through a collector" composition `search_term_query`/`doc_value_query.rs`'s `search_*` functions already use, so it composes with `collector::VecCollector` (just the doc IDs) or any other `Collector` a caller wires in as one clause lucene_codecs::points::Error)` variant on this crate's own `Error` enum (mirroring the existing `Error::DocValues`) — the per-dimension unsigned-byte-wise comparison, `decode_all_points` call, and `points_query.rs` row for `ffi_search_points_range`. **Deliberately out of scope** (same honest gaps task #36's row already documents, inherited unchanged here): a scored variant (`PointRangeQuery` is `ConstantScoreQuery`-shaped in real Lucene too — no relevance score to add), the sublinear `BKDReader.intersect` tree-pruning traversal (this is `O(field's point count)` per call via `decode_all_points`, not sublinear), and multi-segment federation (single already-opened segment's `PointsReader`, same scope as every other query module in this crate). **This port's already-built multi-dimension BKD points support is exercised, not just the single-dimension case**: one test builds a 2D `LatLonPoint`-shaped fixture in-memory (via the existing `points::write`) and confirms a doc whose dimension-0 value alone would match but whose dimension-1 value doesn't is correctly excluded, proving the same AND-across-dimensions semantics task #36 proved at the delete layer now holds at this new search-side entry point too. **Cross-engine verification approach**: same as task #36 — no new checked-in real-Lucene fixture (the existing `fixtures/data/points_index/` fixture is single-dimension only and can't exercise the 2D case anyway); fixtures are hand-built in-memory via the already real-Lucene-verified `points::write`/`points::open` round trip from tasks #18/#22. Tests (8): exact range match, inclusive boundaries on both ends, a zero-match range, a range matching every doc, an unknown field number (empty result, not an error), `live_docs` filtering an already-deleted doc out, the 2D multi-dimension case above, and a corrupt-`.kdd`-leaf-data case (bytes scrambled strictly between the codec header and footer, so `points::open` itself still succeeds but `decode_all_points`'s leaf read fails partway through) confirming `Error::Points` surfaces correctly through `search_points_range` itself, not just through `points::open`. `cargo test -p lucene-search`: 450 lib tests pass (up from 442). `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean. 98.72% line coverage on `points_query.rs`. |
| `index/IndexWriter.updateDocument(Term, doc)` | `lucene-index/src/update_document.rs::update_document` | **ported (task #37).** The atomic delete-by-term + add-document composition real Lucene defines `updateDocument` as, built entirely by wiring together already-verified primitives rather than new byte-format work: task #27's `term_delete::resolve_and_apply_term_delete` (delete half, fanned out over every segment in the caller's `SegmentInfos` that it supplies an opened [`SegmentDeleteSource`] for — segments with no supplied source are left untouched, not silently dropped) and task #11's `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment` (add half — a brand-new segment for the replacement document). Both halves are applied to an in-memory copy of the segment list; the **only** durable state transition is one `segment_infos::write` call at the very end, after every fallible step has already succeeded — so a reader opening any `segments_N` this port writes either sees the fully-old state (previous generation, if `update_document` errored before its final write) or the fully-new one (old segments with bumped `del_gen`s + the one new segment, all in the next generation's single fsync'd file), never a half-applied mix. This is a state-machine/ordering guarantee, not a new decoder, so no new byte format needed cross-engine fixture verification (same reasoning as task #36's points-delete "reused vs. newly written" note) — what *is* verified against the checked-in real-Lucene `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture (the same one `term_delete.rs`'s own tests use) is that the delete half's resolution is correct within this composition, not just in isolation. **Free function, not a method on a stateful writer**: this port has no long-lived `IndexWriter`-equivalent struct (task #11's "minimal multi-segment writer" is itself a free function, `flush_stored_only_segment`, operating on `Directory` state the caller owns) — `update_document` follows that same style rather than introducing a new stateful abstraction unprompted. **Known, inherited limitation, not new to this task**: this port's only write path (`flush_stored_only_segment`) writes stored-fields-only segments (no write-side postings format exists yet, `PLAN.md` Phase 5 item 2), so a delete-by-term issued against *only* a segment this port wrote itself can never actually match anything — there is nothing to resolve against. Unit-tested: updating replaces a single existing doc (singleton-postings term, no `.doc` file needed) and the deletion is verified on disk via `live_docs::parse` while the replacement document is verified via `stored_fields::open`/`.document()`; a term matching zero existing docs behaves exactly like a pure insert (old segment's `del_count` untouched, `del_gen` still bumped per `resolve_and_apply_term_delete`'s existing no-op-round convention); a term matching multiple docs deletes all of them and adds exactly one new document; a segment with no supplied delete source is left completely untouched in the new commit; and a failing delete step (an out-of-range doc ID from a deliberately-too-small `max_doc`) aborts before any `segments_N`/new-segment file is written, confirmed by asserting neither exists on disk afterward. Also confirms the new commit round-trips through `segment_infos::parse`. 99.25% line coverage. |
| `search/IndexSearcher.search(Query, Collector)` (single-segment slice) | `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::search_term_query` | **ported, scoped to one already-opened segment.** Takes an already-opened `blocktree::BlockTreeFields`, an optional opened `.doc` (`postings::DocInput`, needed only when the matched term's `docFreq > 1`), and an optional `.liv`-derived `FixedBitSet` (`None` = no deletions, matching `IndexSearcher`'s `Bits liveDocs == null` convention) — `seekExact`s the term, decodes its postings eagerly (`FieldTerms::postings`, not the lazy skip-ahead `LazyDocsCursor`: no skip-driven query shape exists yet to need it — see `rust-performance`'s "profile before optimizing"), and feeds every live doc ID to a `Collector` in ascending order. A missing field or a term absent from the dictionary yields zero matches, not an error (mirrors `TermQuery.createWeight`'s null-`Scorer` outcome). **No `SegmentReader`/multi-segment federation existed at the time this function was written** — this function's caller is responsible for opening the segment's files the same way `crates/lucene-codecs/tests/blocktree_fixtures.rs` already does. A minimal `SegmentReader`/`DirectoryReader` now exists (task #45, see its row below `multi_segment.rs`'s), but this single-segment function itself is unchanged -- callers open one segment directly the same way, whether by hand or via `DirectoryReader::segment_readers()`. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/term_query_fixtures.rs` runs `search_term_query` against the real `IndexWriter`-produced segment in `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` and asserts the exact doc-ID sets match `manifest.properties`' `postingsDocs` entries (themselves real `PostingsEnum.nextDoc()` output) for fields spanning the singleton (`id`), multi-doc (`body`), multi-block (`big`, `docFreq == 300`), and level-1-skip (`l1`, `docFreq == 8250`) postings shapes already covered at the decode layer. |

Generic (`search_term_query<C: Collector>`), not `dyn`, per `rust-performance`'s "monomorphize per-doc loops" rule. |

| `search/TopScoreDocCollector` | `lucene-search/src/collector.rs::TopDocsCollector` | **ported (task #13).** Keeps the top `n` `(doc_id, score)` hits, tie-broken by lower doc ID on an exact score tie — verified against `HitQueue.lessThan` (`org.apache.lucene.search.HitQueue`), not assumed. Implemented as a sorted `Vec` with a binary-search insert position rather than real Lucene's binary-heap `HitQueue` — `O(n)` per insert instead of `O(log n)`, an explicit "simple first cut" tradeoff matching this crate's `docid_set::Disjunction` precedent (see that module's doc comment); revisit if `top_n`/query throughput ever demands the heap. No `TotalHits`/`TotalHits.Relation` tracking (nothing here does early termination yet — every `collect` call is a fully evaluated hit). Unit-tested for fewer-than-`n`, exactly-`n`, more-than-`n` (eviction), tie-break (both on initial fill and on eviction), and empty-input cases. |
| `search/similarities/Similarity`/`BM25Similarity` (formula only) | `lucene-search/src/similarity.rs` | **ported: the pure BM25 scoring formula, plus real per-doc/avg norms decoding (this task).** Formula verified against `BM25Similarity.java`/`BM25Scorer.doScore` (Lucene 10.5.0) — `idf(docFreq, docCount) = ln(1 + (docCount - docFreq + 0.5) / (docFreq + 0.5))`, `tfNorm(freq, fieldLength, avgFieldLength, k1, b) = freq / (freq + k1*(1-b+b*fieldLength/avgFieldLength))`, `score = idf * tfNorm`, defaults `k1 = 1.2`, `b = 0.75` (`BM25Similarity()`'s no-arg constructor). **Correctness fix (task #32)**: `tfNorm` previously carried a spurious `(k1+1)` numerator factor (the textbook Robertson/Sparck-Jones BM25 term, not real Lucene 10.5.0's actual formula, which folds no such factor into `BM25Scorer.doScore`'s `weight - weight / (1 + freq * normInverse)`); every self-consistency test in this crate had independently reimplemented the same wrong factor, so none of them could catch it. It was caught by `DisjunctionMaxQuery`'s (task #32) new cross-engine test comparing an absolute score against real `IndexSearcher.explain()` output for the first time in this port, rather than a hand-rederivation of this module's own formula — fixed in `similarity::tf_norm`, with `scoring_fixtures.rs`'s/`phrase_query_fixtures.rs`'s hand-computed expected values updated to match; every dependent test (`scoring_fixtures.rs`, `phrase_query_fixtures.rs`, `boolean_query_fixtures.rs`, `dismax_query_fixtures.rs`) still passes since they only assert relative/self-consistent properties, except the one new test that now checks the literal real-Lucene-comparable magnitude. No query-time boost is folded in (none exists in this port). **The norms gap, previously stated here as open, is now closed**: `crates/lucene-codecs/src/norms.rs`'s read side (`norm_value`) is fixture-verified and complete (see that row above); real Lucene's default `Similarity.computeNorm` encodes a field's token-count length via `SmallFloat.intToByte4` (a lossy 4-bit-mantissa byte encoding), and `BM25Similarity.LENGTH_TABLE`/`SimScorer.score` decode it back with `SmallFloat.byte4ToInt` — this port now has that exact decode (`lucene_util::small_float::byte4_to_int`, wrapped by `similarity::decode_norm`), verified against hand-derived known byte↔length values from `SmallFloat.java`'s algorithm. `lucene-search/src/field_norms.rs::FieldNorms::open` computes `avgFieldLength` once per field per query (summing every live doc's decoded length, not recomputed per scored doc — see the `rust-performance` skill), and `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` take an optional `FieldNorms`/`HashMap<String, FieldNorms>`, using it for real per-doc/avg field length when present. **The one remaining, explicitly-scoped gap**: passing `None` (a field with no opened norms — norms disabled for that field, or a caller that hasn't wired norms opening up yet) still falls back to the constant `1.0`/`1.0` substitution (`similarity::UNNORMED_FIELD_LENGTH`) — a documented, deliberate fallback for that one case, not a blanket approximation anymore. Also still open: no cross-engine Java-side BM25-score fixture generator exists, so a full query's *final* score hasn't been diffed byte-for-byte against real Lucene's own output (only the length-normalization term's liveness and the decoded lengths themselves are differentially verified) — deferred. Differential-verified in `crates/lucene-search/tests/scoring_fixtures.rs` against the real `_0.nvm`/`_0.nvd` this fixture's `IndexWriter` wrote: decoded per-doc lengths match hand-derived values from the fixture's own known per-term postings frequencies (a doc's BM25 length is the sum of its terms' frequencies), `avgFieldLength` is their mean, and real-norms scores differ from the constant-fallback scores for the same query/term. Unit-tested with independently hand-computed expected values (not just asserting the implementation's own output) for `idf`/`tf_norm`/`score`/`decode_norm`, plus monotonicity properties (more common term → lower idf, longer field → lower tf_norm, higher freq → higher score, real length ratio → correctly ordered scores). |
| `util/SmallFloat` (`intToByte4`/`byte4ToInt` only) | `lucene-util/src/small_float.rs` | **ported**, scoped to exactly the pair BM25 norms need (not the general `byteToFloat`/`floatToByte` 24-bit-mantissa pair used elsewhere in Lucene for unrelated float encodings). Verified byte-for-byte against `SmallFloat.java` (Lucene 10.5.0): `longToInt4`/`int4ToLong`'s "top 4 significant bits plus a biased shift" scheme, `NUM_FREE_VALUES = 255 - longToInt4(Integer.MAX_VALUE) = 24` (asserted as a concrete value, not just trusted from the derivation). Unit-tested: subnormal range (bytes 0-23) decodes exactly, hand-derived known byte→length values, monotonicity (SmallFloat's whole purpose — larger byte never decodes to a smaller length), and encode→decode→re-encode fixed-point round trips for both subnormal and lossy normal-range values. |
| `util/BytesRefHash` (term/byte-sequence interning pool) | `lucene-util/src/term_interner.rs::{TermInterner, TermId}` | **new standalone primitive (task #67), not a byte-for-byte port of `BytesRefHash.java` and NOT yet wired into any indexing or query path.** Real `BytesRefHash` is tied to Lucene's `ByteBlockPool` allocation strategy and exposes sort/compact/rehash machinery for the indexing chain's per-field term dictionaries; this module has none of that. It only carries the core value proposition -- deduplicating recurring byte sequences into a stable, cheap-to-copy handle -- as a from-scratch `HashMap`-backed pool: `TermInterner::intern(&[u8]) -> TermId` returns the same `TermId` for byte-identical input and a fresh one otherwise, `TermInterner::get(TermId) -> Option<&[u8]>` looks the bytes back up, `TermId` is a plain `Copy` `u32` wrapper. No `unsafe` (workspace only permits it in `lucene-util`/`lucene-store`/`lucene-ffi`, and this module doesn't need it). Unit-tested: repeated identical bytes intern to the same ID, distinct bytes get distinct IDs, ID→bytes round trip, the empty byte string as a valid distinct term, lookup of an unrecognized/out-of-range `TermId` returns `None` rather than panicking, and a stress case interning 20,000 calls over a 50-word vocabulary that confirms `TermInterner::len()` collapses to exactly 50 stored entries (dedup actually happening, not just returning arbitrary IDs), plus a separate 5,000-all-distinct-terms case. **Explicitly deferred**: wiring this into `lucene-index`'s indexing chain or `lucene-search`'s query terms (future task), `ByteBlockPool`-style bulk/arena allocation, sorting/compaction, and any on-disk format tie-in -- this is purely an in-memory helper. |
| `search/Weight`, `search/Scorer`, `search/BulkScorer` (as a trait hierarchy) | — | **deferred, not started.** This port's scoring is wired directly into `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` as plain functions (see the `TermQuery`/`BooleanQuery` rows below), not through a `Weight`/`Scorer` class hierarchy — same "no speculative polymorphism with a single implementation" reasoning `lib.rs`'s module doc already applies to unscored matching. Revisit once a second query type or multi-segment federation gives the hierarchy a real second caller. |
| `search/BooleanQuery` (matching + BM25 scoring, `minimumNumberShouldMatch`, nested `BooleanQuery` clauses, `PhraseQuery` clauses) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{BooleanQuery, Clause}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_boolean_query, search_boolean_query_scored, matched_boolean_docs, resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores, should_match_counts}` | **ported**, including `minimumNumberShouldMatch` (task #24), nested `BooleanQuery` clauses (task #25), and `PhraseQuery` clauses (task #29, closing the gap this row previously noted as deferred). `must`/`should`/`must_not` are `Vec<Clause>` plus `minimum_should_match: usize`; `Clause` is a closed **three**-variant enum — `Clause::Term(TermQuery)`, `Clause::Phrase(PhraseQuery)`, or `Clause::Boolean(Box<BooleanQuery>)`, recursively (an enum, not a `Weight`/`Scorer`-style trait object, since exactly three query shapes need to nest here today — see the `rust-performance` skill's "enums where the closed set allows" guidance). `BooleanQuery::with_must`/`with_should`/`with_must_not` take `impl Into<Clause>` items — `Clause`'s `From<TermQuery>`/`From<PhraseQuery>`/`From<BooleanQuery>` impls kept every existing call site compiling unchanged. Matching semantics verified against real `BooleanQuery.rewrite()`/`BooleanWeight.scorer`/`bulkScorer`/`explain` source, not guessed: no `must`/`should` clauses at all (with or without `must_not`) matches **nothing** — real Lucene rewrites both "empty clause list" and "only `MUST_NOT` clauses" ("pure negative BooleanQuery") to `MatchNoDocsQuery`; a pure-exclusion query is *not* "every doc except the excluded ones". `minimum_should_match` gates `should` **regardless of whether `must` is also non-empty** — verified against `BooleanWeight` source specifically because this is the one place the pre-#24 rule ("`should` is score-only once `must` exists") is easy to get backwards: that rule only holds at `minimum_should_match == 0`; for `minimum_should_match > 0`, a doc drawn from `must`'s conjunction (or, when `must` is empty, `should`'s disjunction) is only kept if it also matches at least `minimum_should_match` of the `should` clauses — a genuine behavior change gated purely on `minimum_should_match > 0`. The counting mechanism ([`should_match_counts`]) is a `HashMap<i32, usize>` tally of how many `should` clauses' doc-ID lists contain each candidate doc — needed because a plain `Disjunction` only reports "in the union", not "how many clauses agreed". `minimum_should_match` exceeding `should.len()` needs no special-case branch: real `BooleanQuery.rewrite()` turns that into an explicit `MatchNoDocsQuery` at query-construction time, but no doc's should-match count can ever reach an unreachable threshold either way, so the same threshold comparison already yields the identical "matches nothing" result. `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored`'s previously-duplicated matched-doc-set computation is unified in one shared `matched_boolean_docs` helper. **Nested clauses**: [`resolve_clause_docs`] recursively resolves a `Clause::Boolean` clause via a fresh `matched_boolean_docs` call on the nested query — respecting *that* query's own `must`/`should`/`must_not`/`minimum_should_match` completely independently of the parent's, with no hardcoded nesting-depth limit (verified with 2–3 levels of nesting, not just one extra level). [`clause_scores`] is the scoring sibling: a nested `BooleanQuery`'s own score contribution is the sum of *its own* matching `must`/`should` sub-clauses' scores, restricted to the doc set the nested query itself actually matched — mirroring real Lucene's additive `BooleanScorer` recursion, so a should-clause hit the nested query's own `must_not`/`minimum_should_match` excludes can't leak a score contribution into the parent. **`Clause::Phrase` (task #29)**: `resolve_clause_docs` delegates matching straight to `search_phrase_query` (collected via a local `VecCollector`), and `clause_scores` delegates scoring straight to `search_phrase_query_scored` (collected via a tiny inline `ScoringCollector`) — both reusing the standalone phrase-query functions' logic rather than duplicating it. Because a `Clause::Phrase` needs the segment's opened `.pos`/`.pay` files, `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored` (and every internal helper in the recursive chain — `matched_boolean_docs`, `resolve_clause_docs`, `clause_scores`) now additionally take `pos_in: Option<&PosInput>`/`pay_in: Option<&PayInput>` (a breaking signature change from the pre-task-#29 four/six-argument shape; every call site in this crate and `lucene-ffi` was updated to pass `None`/`None` where no phrase clause is used) — `None` is fine for a query with no multi-term `Clause::Phrase` at any nesting depth, surfacing `Error::MissingPosInput` only if one turns out to need it, same convention `search_phrase_query` already established. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/boolean_query_fixtures.rs` computes expected conjunction/disjunction/difference from `manifest.properties`' real `PostingsEnum`-derived doc sets and asserts `search_boolean_query` matches exactly, including a `minimum_should_match`-with-`must`-present case, a nested-`must`-clause case, and a three-level-deep nesting case. **`search_boolean_query_scored`** (task #13) computes the identical matched-doc set, then reports each doc's score as the sum of its BM25 score across every `must`/`should` clause it satisfies (mirroring real Lucene's additive `BooleanScorer`; `must_not` never contributes, matching `Occur.MUST_NOT`'s filter-only contract) — verified in `crates/lucene-search/tests/scoring_fixtures.rs` against the real segment, including a dedicated test that a `must_not` clause never changes the score, a test (task #24) proving `minimum_should_match` gates matching only, not the score sum, a test (task #25) proving a nested `must` clause's own score sums correctly into the parent's additive total, and a test (task #29) proving a `Clause::Phrase`'s own score sums correctly alongside a sibling `Clause::Term`, against the `pos` field's real alpha/beta postings. Unit tests in `lib.rs`/`query.rs` additionally confirm a nested clause's own `minimum_should_match` and the parent's are fully independent settings (no cross-contamination in either direction), plus a `Clause::Phrase` nested inside a `Clause::Boolean` resolves both matching and scoring correctly. **Still deferred**: `lucene-ffi`'s `ffi_search_boolean_query` still only ever constructs flat `Clause::Term` clauses from its four-parallel-array C-ABI wire format — exposing `Clause::Phrase`/`Clause::Boolean` *construction* over that wire format remains a separate, deferred FFI design question (alongside the already-deferred `_scored` FFI wrappers). **Edge cases (task #60)**: six real Lucene `BooleanQuery`/`BooleanWeight` corner cases were individually verified against this port's actual `matched_boolean_docs`/`should_match_counts`/`clause_scores` code (not assumed) and found already correct, locked in with new regression tests rather than requiring a fix: a pure `must_not`-only query matches nothing (confirmed *before* `must_not` ever enters the merge, not via an "everything except excluded" shortcut); `minimum_should_match > 0` with zero `should` clauses at all (a nonsensical-but-configurable combination) correctly matches nothing, not "trivially satisfied"; `minimum_should_match` exceeding `should.len()` has no distinct code path from the ordinary case, so no off-by-one is possible at or past the boundary; a nested `Clause::Boolean`'s own `must_not` never leaks into or is leaked into by an outer level's `must_not` (each nesting level gets a fresh `matched_boolean_docs` call); and — deliberately **not** a bug — a literal duplicate `should` clause (the same `TermQuery` twice) double-counts toward `minimum_should_match` and double-scores, matching real `BooleanQuery`'s own documented non-deduping behavior (duplicating a clause is itself a known, intentional way to boost it in real Lucene), not something this port needed to special-case away. **Rewrite pass (task #79)**: `BooleanQuery::rewrite`/`Clause::rewrite` add a pure, standalone, **opt-in** simplification pass -- never called by `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored` themselves, so existing execution is unchanged. Implements exactly three rules: (1) a single-clause query with no `must_not` collapses to that clause, but only in the two cases proven not to change matching -- `must.len() == 1` with `should` empty and `minimum_should_match == 0`, or `should.len() == 1` with `must` empty and `minimum_should_match <= 1` (both boundary cases where a positive `minimum_should_match` would otherwise turn "matches nothing" into a false positive are deliberately excluded); (2) zero-clause/`must_not`-only "matches nothing" is a documented no-op, since `matched_boolean_docs` already produces that result with no `MatchNoDocsQuery`-equivalent `Clause` to rewrite to; (3) every clause is rewritten recursively, bottom-up, including through nested `DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`. **Explicitly not implemented: duplicate-clause deduplication** -- would contradict task #60's own finding just above (a duplicate `should` clause is meant to double-count/double-score, and the same additive scoring applies to duplicate `must` clauses), so deduping would change scores/matches rather than merely avoid redundant work. Proven scoring-equivalent, not just structurally simplified: `crates/lucene-search/tests/boolean_query_fixtures.rs`'s `rewrite_produces_identical_scored_results_for_single_must_clause`/`_for_single_should_clause`/`_for_nested_single_clause_boolean` run the same query pre- and post-`rewrite()` through `search_boolean_query_scored` against the real fixture segment and assert identical `TopDocsCollector` output (doc IDs and scores both). |
| `search/PhraseQuery`/`ExactPhraseScorer`/`SloppyPhraseMatcher` (in-order sloppy matching, no reordering; BM25 scoring) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::PhraseQuery`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_phrase_query, search_phrase_query_scored, phrase_matches_in_doc, phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy, phrase_freq_exact}` | **ported: exact adjacent-position matching (`slop == 0`, task #19), in-order sloppy matching (`slop > 0`, task #28), and BM25 scoring (task #29, closing that gap) -- term reordering within the slop budget, and graduated sloppy match-quality scoring, are not supported, see below.** `PhraseQuery { field: String, terms: Vec<Vec<u8>>, slop: u32 }` implicitly places `terms[i]` at query-relative position `i` (still no `PhraseQuery.Builder.add(Term, int position)`-style arbitrary/non-adjacent positions -- `slop` widens how far apart the implicitly-numbered terms may drift at match time, it doesn't let a caller assign arbitrary per-term positions). `slop` defaults to `0` (matching real `PhraseQuery.Builder`'s default); `PhraseQuery::with_slop` is the builder method. **Exact alignment algorithm** (`phrase_matches_in_doc`, unchanged from task #19): every position in the first term's list is a candidate base `p`, checked against every other term's sorted position list via `binary_search` for `p+i`. **Sloppy alignment algorithm** (`phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy`, task #28's addition): for a candidate base position `p_0` (every occurrence in the first term's list), a doc matches at slop `s` iff there exists a strictly-increasing, in-order alignment `p_0 < p_1 < ... < p_{n-1}` (one position per term, `p_i` drawn from `term_positions[i]`) whose total "moves" -- `sum_{i=1}^{n-1} (p_i - p_{i-1} - 1)`, which telescopes to `(p_{n-1} - p_0) - (n-1)` -- is at most `s`; for a fixed `p_0` the minimum such total is found by a greedy scan picking, at each step, the smallest position in the next term's list that's strictly greater than the previous chosen position (provably optimal since the total telescopes to a function of only `p_0` and the final position). This formula is derived from real `PhraseQuery`'s own Javadoc description of slop ("the number of positions all words need to move ... to line up in order"), cited in `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy`'s doc comment. **Scoped subset, stated precisely**: this is an **in-order-only** implementation -- it requires the chosen positions to be strictly increasing in phrase order. Real Lucene's general `SloppyPhraseMatcher` (`org.apache.lucene.search.SloppyPhraseMatcher`) additionally allows term **reordering** within the slop budget (e.g. "quick fox" matching "fox ... quick" at a high enough slop) via a priority-queue-based edit-distance computation over `PhrasePositions`/repeats -- that general algorithm was not implemented here: this task could not confidently re-derive and verify its exact edit-distance formula against real Lucene's source within scope, so reordering support is deliberately left out rather than guessed at (a correctness-first, honestly-scoped subset, per this port's established practice -- see BKD's split-heuristic and term_vectors' scoped write side for the same call). `search_phrase_query` computes the doc-level conjunction across every term's live-filtered doc-ID list first (reusing `docid_set::Conjunction`, since phrase match implies term match), then dispatches per candidate doc to `phrase_matches_in_doc` (unchanged fast path) when `query.slop == 0`, or `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy` otherwise. **Edge cases** (both paths): an empty `terms` list matches nothing (mirrors real `PhraseQuery.Builder.build()`'s `MatchNoDocsQuery` result for zero added terms); a single-term "phrase" degenerates to a plain `search_term_query` call regardless of `slop` (trivially aligned wherever the lone term occurs, never needs an opened `.pos` file); a term missing from the field matches nothing, not an error; a repeated term (e.g. "the the") is handled without special-casing. **BM25 scoring (task #29's addition)**: `search_phrase_query_scored` mirrors `search_phrase_query`'s matching exactly, additionally computing each matched doc's **phrase frequency** (in place of a single term's `freq`) and feeding it through the same BM25 machinery `search_term_query_scored` uses (`similarity::tf_norm`, real per-doc/avg norms via the same `FieldNorms` contract). The phrase's overall `idf` is the **sum of each constituent term's own `idf(docFreq, docCount)`** -- verified against `BM25Similarity.idf(CollectionStatistics, TermStatistics[])`'s real source, which sums per-term idf across a multi-term statistics array rather than inventing a single combined docFreq; this is not this port's own invention. **Exact phrase frequency** (`phrase_freq_exact`): counts every valid base position `p0` in the first term's own (sorted, deduplicated) position list for which the rest of the phrase aligns -- one match per distinct starting position of the phrase's first word, matching `ExactPhraseScorer`'s own per-start-position counting granularity (does not suppress overlapping matches, e.g. "the the the" counts 2 matches for phrase "the the"). **Sloppy phrase frequency**: **deliberately simplified** to `1` if any valid alignment exists (via `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy`), `0` otherwise -- real Lucene's `SloppyPhraseMatcher` instead accumulates a graduated per-match contribution of `1.0 / (matchLength + 1)` (tighter alignments score higher) summed across every alignment its priority-queue-based algorithm finds; this port could not confidently re-derive/verify that exact per-match weighting formula (on top of the alignment-enumeration algorithm already scoped down to in-order-only, see above) within this task's scope, so **graduated sloppy match-quality scoring is deliberately deferred**, tracked here, in favor of the simpler matches-or-not boolean signal -- consistent with this port's "scope down honestly rather than guess at unverified Lucene internals" practice (BKD's split heuristic, `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy` itself). **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/phrase_query_fixtures.rs` (task #19) reuses the existing `pos` field checked into `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` for the exact-matching (`slop == 0`) path (doc 8555: "alpha"@0, "beta"@1, adjacent; doc 8556: "alpha"@0 and @1, no "beta" at all); `two_term_phrase_scored_matches_hand_computed_bm25_score` (task #29) hand-derives the expected BM25 score from the manifest's real `docFreq` values and asserts `search_phrase_query_scored` matches, independently of `similarity::score`'s own unit tests. **The sloppy path's cross-engine gap is now closed**: `GenBlockTree.java` was extended with doc7 ("pos" field: "alpha"@0, "beta"@3, a real, known, non-adjacent gap requiring `(3-0)-(2-1) = 2` moves), and at fixture-generation time it *actually runs* real `IndexSearcher.search` with a real `PhraseQuery.Builder().add(alpha).add(beta).setSlop(n)` against that doc for `n` in `{0, 1, 2, 3, 5}`, recording each verdict in `manifest.properties` (`field.pos.sloppyGap.realLuceneSlopResults=0:false,1:false,2:true,3:true,5:true`). `crates/lucene-search/tests/phrase_query_fixtures.rs::sloppy_phrase_gap_matches_real_lucenes_phrase_query_set_slop_at_every_tested_value` reads that manifest key back and asserts `search_phrase_query`'s own sloppy-path verdict agrees with real Lucene's at every one of those five slop values -- confirmed passing, i.e. this port's `phrase_matches_in_doc_sloppy` formula is now cross-engine verified against actual `SloppyPhraseMatcher`/`PhraseQuery.setSlop(n)` behavior for a known non-adjacent gap, not just self-consistent unit tests. (The formula's own internal correctness was already covered by the hand-computed unit tests in `lib.rs` listed previously; this closes the gap those tests alone couldn't: agreement with real Lucene's actual output.) Term **reordering** within the slop budget remains unimplemented and unverified (see the scoped-subset note above) -- only in-order sloppy matching has cross-engine proof. |
| `search/DisjunctionMaxQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxScorer` (matching + BM25 scoring, nested `Clause` disjuncts) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{DisjunctionMaxQuery, Clause::DisjunctionMax}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{search_disjunction_max_query, search_disjunction_max_query_scored, resolve_dismax_docs, dismax_scores}` | **ported (task #32).** `DisjunctionMaxQuery { disjuncts: Vec<Clause>, tie_breaker: f32 }`; `Clause` grows a fourth variant, `Clause::DisjunctionMax(Box<DisjunctionMaxQuery>)`, nesting the same way `Clause::Boolean` already does (arbitrary depth, and a `DisjunctionMaxQuery` disjunct may itself be a `Term`/`Phrase`/`Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`). Matching is a pure union (`resolve_dismax_docs`, built on the same `Disjunction` merge combinator `BooleanQuery`'s `should`-only case uses) — unlike `BooleanQuery.should`, there is no `minimum_should_match`-style gate; a `DisjunctionMaxQuery` with zero disjuncts matches nothing, mirroring `BooleanQuery`'s own empty-clause-list rule. Scoring (`dismax_scores`) implements real `DisjunctionMaxScorer`'s exact formula, not an approximation: a matching doc's score is `max(disjunct scores) + tie_breaker * sum(every other matching disjunct's score)`, computed via the same recursive per-clause `clause_scores` a `Clause::Boolean` disjunct already uses (so a nested `Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax` disjunct scores correctly to arbitrary depth). `tie_breaker == 0.0` (real `DisjunctionMaxQuery(Collection<Query>)`'s single-arg constructor default) degenerates to pure max-of-disjuncts scoring. **Verified against real Lucene**: `crates/lucene-search/tests/dismax_query_fixtures.rs` reuses the checked-in `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture and its already-fixture-verified `body` postings (`cat`={0,2}, `dog`={0,1}, `bird`={1,4}), plus a genuine `IndexSearcher.search(new DisjunctionMaxQuery(...), 10)` run against that exact on-disk segment (`fixtures/src/AppendDismaxManifest.java`, appended to `manifest.properties` as `dismax.*` keys without perturbing the segment's already-committed random ID) asserting doc-for-doc, score-for-score agreement with real Lucene's own recorded `TopDocs` output — true cross-engine verification of the tie-breaker formula, not just self-consistency. Unit tests in `lib.rs` additionally cover: empty-disjunct-list, a missing-term disjunct contributing nothing, exact tie-breaker arithmetic, a doc matching only one disjunct getting exactly that disjunct's score, and nesting in both directions (`DisjunctionMax` inside `Boolean`, `Boolean` inside `DisjunctionMax`, `DisjunctionMax` inside `DisjunctionMax`). **Deferred, same as `BooleanQuery`**: `lucene-ffi` C-ABI construction of a `Clause::DisjunctionMax` disjunct (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses). |
| `search/ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery` (matching + scoring, nested `Clause` composition) | `lucene-search/src/query.rs::{ConstantScoreQuery, BoostQuery, Clause::ConstantScore, Clause::Boost}`, `lucene-search/src/lib.rs::{resolve_clause_docs, clause_scores}` | **ported (task #33).** `ConstantScoreQuery { inner: Box<Clause>, score: f32 }` and `BoostQuery { inner: Box<Clause>, boost: f32 }` each wrap any other `Clause`; `Clause` grows two more variants, `ConstantScore(Box<ConstantScoreQuery>)` and `Boost(Box<BoostQuery>)`, nesting the same way `Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax` already do (either direction, arbitrary depth — a `ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery` can wrap a `Boolean`/`DisjunctionMax`/each other, and a `BooleanQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery` clause can be a `ConstantScore`/`Boost`). Matching for both is exactly the wrapped clause's own matching set (`resolve_clause_docs`'s `ConstantScore`/`Boost` arms recurse straight into the inner clause, no narrowing). Scoring (`clause_scores`): `ConstantScoreQuery` discards the inner clause's own score entirely and reports `score` for every doc the inner clause matched (real `ConstantScoreWeight`/`ConstantScoreScorer`'s behavior — the wrapped query's score never surfaces); `BoostQuery` multiplies the inner clause's own score by `boost` (real `BoostQuery.BoostWeight`'s exact behavior — a pure rescale, not a replacement). **Cross-engine verification scope**: no new Java fixture generator was added — both wrappers are a trivial arithmetic composition (a literal constant; one `f32` multiply) over an inner clause whose own scoring is already cross-engine-verified against real `IndexSearcher`/`TopDocs` output (task #30's `scoring_fixtures.rs`, task #32's `dismax_query_fixtures.rs`), so there was no Lucene-specific formula or wire format left to get wrong that a new fixture could catch.
