| `search/IndexSearcher.search` fan-out + `TopDocs.merge` (matching/scoring fan-out and global merge, no `DirectoryReader` abstraction) | `lucene-search/src/multi_segment.rs::{OpenSegment, merge_multi_segment_scored, search_term_query_multi_segment, search_boolean_query_multi_segment}` | **ported (task #41), scoped precisely below.** Real `IndexSearcher.search` iterates every `LeafReaderContext`, scores/collects each one locally using that segment's own `docBase` to translate local doc IDs to global ones, then merges per-segment `TopDocs` (`TopDocs.merge`/`HitQueue` tie-break: score descending, lower doc ID wins a tie). This port has no `LeafReaderContext`/`DirectoryReader` object to iterate — callers instead pass a plain `&[OpenSegment]` (each entry bundling one already-opened segment's `fields`/`doc_in`/`pos_in`/`pay_in`/`live_docs` plus a caller-computed `doc_base`, the sum of every earlier segment's `maxDoc`). **One shared generic fan-out+merge core** (`merge_multi_segment_scored`), not one copy per query type: every scored query function in this crate already reduces to the same `Vec<ScoreDoc>` shape via `TopDocsCollector`, so the merge step (translate by `doc_base`, re-rank, truncate to `top_n`) needs nothing query-type-specific — `search_term_query_multi_segment`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment` are thin wrappers around that one core, calling `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored` per segment; a third query type's multi-segment entry point is another equally thin wrapper, not a second merge implementation. Each segment is collected into its own bounded `TopDocsCollector::new(top_n)` before the cross-segment merge (matching real per-leaf `TopFieldCollector` behavior, and provably lossless: a global top-`top_n` can never need more than `top_n` hits from one segment). The merge itself reuses `TopDocsCollector`'s own comparator a second time (feeding every segment's already-ranked, doc-base-translated hits through one more fresh collector) rather than reimplementing the tie-break rule. **Explicit idf/scoring-parity scope decision — read carefully**: real `BM25Similarity`'s `idf` is computed from `CollectionStatistics`/`TermStatistics` gathered **index-wide** across every segment (`IndexSearcher.termStatistics`/`collectionStatistics`), not per-segment. This port's existing scored query functions (`term_doc_scores`, `lib.rs`, unchanged by this task) compute `idf` from **that one segment's own** `docFreq`/`docCount` (`blocktree::FieldTerms`/`TermStats`) — there is no index-wide statistics aggregation anywhere in this port, and this task does not add one (that would need a `DirectoryReader`-level aggregation step across every segment's term dictionary before scoring starts, out of scope here). Consequently: **this task claims "correct matching + correct per-segment-relative BM25 scoring + correct global merge order," not "byte-for-byte parity with real multi-segment Lucene's BM25 scores"** — whenever a term's `docFreq`/`docCount` genuinely differ across segments (the common case for a >1-segment index), a per-segment idf and an index-wide idf diverge, and this port computes the former. **Verified**: unit tests in `multi_segment.rs` isolate the merge core with synthetic per-segment scores (interleaved/overlapping scores across 2-3 segments, truncation to `top_n`, a zero-match segment, cross-segment tie-break by ascending global doc ID, `top_n == 0`, zero segments, a single segment with nonzero `doc_base`), plus end-to-end calls through both public wrappers against the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment. **Cross-engine verification** (`tests/multi_segment_fixtures.rs`): no genuine 2+-segment real-Lucene fixture exists in this repo yet, so — per this task's documented next-best alternative — the same real, `IndexWriter`-produced `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment is opened **twice** (as "segment 0" at `doc_base=0` and "segment 1" at `doc_base=` that segment's own real `maxDoc`), modeling a genuine two-segment index; each "segment"'s real BM25 scores (already fixture-proven by `scoring_fixtures.rs`) are independently concatenated/translated/sorted by this test itself (not by calling the code under test twice) and asserted equal, doc-for-doc and score-for-score, to `search_term_query_multi_segment`'s actual output — proving the merge/doc-base-translation/tie-break logic against real recorded scores, the highest-risk "looks locally correct per-segment, wrong globally" bug class this task's brief specifically calls out. **Still deferred**: real index-wide `CollectionStatistics`-based idf (above); a genuine multi-segment Java fixture generator; multi-segment support for `PhraseQuery`/`DisjunctionMaxQuery`/`ConstantScoreQuery`/`BoostQuery`/`WildcardQuery`/`PrefixQuery` (each would be another thin wrapper around `merge_multi_segment_scored`, not yet added). `lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure is now closed by task #51 (see its own row below). **`doc_base` computation and per-file segment opening are no longer manual** -- see the `DirectoryReader`/`SegmentReader` row directly below (task #45). |
| `index/DirectoryReader.open(Directory)` + `SegmentReader` (federated segment-opening only, not `MultiTerms`/a unified leaf abstraction) | `lucene-search/src/directory_reader.rs::{DirectoryReader, SegmentReader, OpenedSegments}` | **ported (task #45), scoped precisely below.** `DirectoryReader::open(dir)` finds the latest `segments_N` (new `lucene_index::segment_infos::read_latest`, a thin wrapper over the already-existing `lucene_store::directory::read_latest_commit` + `parse`), opens one `SegmentReader` per listed segment, and computes each segment's `doc_base` as the running sum of every earlier segment's `maxDoc` -- the two things the task #41 row above flags as still manual. Per segment, only the files that segment actually has get opened, checked against `SegmentInfo.files` rather than assumed: `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd`/`.doc`/`.pos`/`.pay` are opened together or not at all (a segment with none of them -- e.g. this port's stored-fields-only fixtures, see `segment_writer.rs`'s doc comment -- gets an empty `blocktree::BlockTreeFields::empty()`, a small new constructor added alongside this task); `.liv` is opened only when `del_gen != -1`, reusing `lucene_index::deletes::liv_file_name` rather than re-deriving that filename convention. **Crate placement, worked out explicitly**: this lives in `lucene-search`, not `lucene-index`, because it has to hand back `lucene_search::multi_segment::OpenSegment` values and `lucene-index` cannot depend on `lucene-search` (same downward-dependency constraint already hit by tasks #27/#36). **Two-call API, not one**: `DirectoryReader::open_segments()` returns an `OpenedSegments` that owns the freshly-opened `DocInput`/`PosInput`/`PayInput` values (borrowing from each `SegmentReader`'s own byte buffers), and `OpenedSegments::as_open_segments()` returns the final `Vec<OpenSegment>` borrowing from that -- two calls because `OpenSegment` holds `&'a DocInput<'a>` (a reference to an already-constructed value, not owned bytes), and storing that value directly inside `SegmentReader` would be self-referential, which is illegal without `unsafe` (`lucene-search` is `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`). **Compound-file segments (`.cfs`/`.cfe`) are now wired in (task #76)**: this is read-path wiring of two *already-existing* primitives, not new codec work -- `SegmentReader::open` checks `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file` and, if set, opens the segment's `.cfs`/`.cfe` pair once (new `CompoundArchive`, `directory_reader.rs`) via `lucene_codecs::compound_format::{parse_entries, check_data_header_footer, open_input}` (unchanged, called exactly as `segment_writer.rs`'s own compound test already does), instead of returning `Error::CompoundFileUnsupported`. Every sub-file lookup (`.fnm`, `.tim`, `.tip`, `.tmd`, `.doc`, `.pos`, `.pay`) now goes through one shared helper, `open_segment_file` (plus `find_segment_file_name` for the name-only lookup `.tim`'s codec-suffix derivation needs), so there is exactly one branch point ("compound: read out of the archive by extension suffix; loose: `dir.open` the `SegmentInfo.files` entry ending in that extension, as before") rather than duplicated ad-hoc logic per file type -- non-compound segments are provably unaffected (same code path, same tests passing). **Verified against a real Java-written compound segment, not just this port's own writer**: `fixtures/data/compound_index/` (`GenCompoundFormat.java`, real `IndexWriter` with `useCompoundFile=true`, 5 docs, a real `.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd`/`.doc` postings quad packed alongside `.fnm`/stored-fields/doc-values files inside one `.cfs`) now opens successfully through `DirectoryReader::open` and answers a real term query correctly (`compound_file_segment_opens_and_is_queryable`, replacing the old rejection test) -- this is what proves postings-in-a-compound-file also works, not just `.fnm`. A second unit test flushes the same documents through this port's own `segment_writer::flush_stored_only_segment` twice, once loose and once with `use_compound_file: true`, and confirms the compound segment opens with fields/doc-count matching the loose one, with no loose `.fnm` present on disk to fall back to (`compound_flushed_segment_opens_with_field_infos_matching_non_compound_flush`). All prior tests (real single/live-docs fixtures, stored-fields-only, missing-`.fnm`, partial-blocktree, `open_if_changed` reuse/reopen) still pass unchanged. **Still not compound-aware, honestly**: doc-values, norms, and term-vector readers elsewhere in this crate (`doc_value_query.rs`, `field_norms.rs`, `term_vectors_query.rs`, `soft_deletes.rs`) each open their own files directly off the outer `Directory` by name, independent of `DirectoryReader`/`SegmentReader` -- none of them consult `SegmentInfo.is_compound_file` or this task's new `open_segment_file`/`CompoundArchive`, so a compound segment that also had doc-values/norms/term-vectors packed into its `.cfs` would still fail to open through *those* call sites (this port's own write side doesn't yet produce such a segment, so nothing exercises the gap today, but it is real and unclosed). A `MultiTerms`/unified multi-segment `Terms` iteration abstraction and real index-wide `CollectionStatistics`-based idf (task #41's own gaps) remain unchanged by this task. `lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure of this reader is closed by task #51 (see its own row below). NRT/reopen is closed by task #46 -- see the next row. Soft-delete visibility is closed by task #48 -- see the row below. |
| `index/IndexWriterConfig.setSoftDeletesField` + soft-delete **visibility** (`SoftDeletesDirectoryReaderWrapper`/`PendingSoftDeletes`'s read-side check only, not `IndexWriter.softUpdateDocument`'s write side) | `lucene-search/src/soft_deletes.rs::{SoftDeletesField, is_soft_deleted, is_live, effective_live_docs}` | **ported (task #48), read-side (visibility) only -- see the honest write-side scope call below.** Real Lucene's soft-delete rule is exactly a `DocValuesFieldExistsQuery` over the configured soft-deletes field: a doc is soft-deleted if that field has *any* value for it (presence, not a specific sentinel value). `is_soft_deleted`/`is_live`/`effective_live_docs` implement that same presence-based OR-with-hard-deletes rule against an already-opened `lucene_codecs::doc_values::NumericEntry` (the read side task #4/#21 already built): a doc is invisible if its `.liv` bit is cleared (hard-deleted) **or** its soft-deletes-field doc-values value is present (soft-deleted) -- both conditions independently sufficient, and a doc hit by both stays invisible, not double-counted or contradictory. **Integration point, chosen deliberately**: rather than growing every scored-query function in `lib.rs`/`multi_segment.rs` an extra "and also check this doc-values field" parameter, `effective_live_docs` computes one combined `FixedBitSet` (hard-live AND NOT soft-deleted) that a caller passes straight into any existing `live_docs: Option<&FixedBitSet>` parameter unchanged -- every pre-existing single-hard-delete-only call site is completely unaffected, since nothing forces it to call the new function at all. **Write-side scope decision, now partially closed by task #54**: real Lucene's soft-delete *write* path (`IndexWriter.softUpdateDocument`) relies on `NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates`, which appends a small delta record to an existing segment's doc-values generation rather than rewriting the whole `.dvm`/`.dvd`/`.dvs` triple. At the time this task (#48) was written, this port had no incremental doc-values update format/codec at all -- the only doc-values write primitive (`lucene_codecs::doc_values::write_single_dense_numeric_field`) always wrote a brand-new, complete, single-dense-field triple from scratch, so this task deliberately did not fake a "cheap incremental marking" shim on top of it. **Task #54 has since built exactly that missing incremental-update primitive** (`lucene_codecs::doc_values_updates`, a single-generation sparse `(docId, value)` overlay file, read-through-overlay decode) and wired it into this module as `mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay`/`is_soft_deleted_with_overlay`/`effective_live_docs_with_overlay`: marking one doc soft-deleted no longer requires touching the base `.dvd`/`.dvm` bytes at all. This closes the write-side gap for **one overlay round** -- it does not implement real Lucene's full multi-generation `docValuesGen` lifecycle (many sequential update rounds, newest-generation-wins across rounds) or `SegmentCommitInfo`/`.si` generation-metadata wiring; see `doc_values_updates.rs`'s own doc comment for that scope statement. **Verified**: unit tests cover all four hard/soft-delete combinations (hard-only invisible, soft-only invisible, neither live, both invisible-not-contradictory) plus `effective_live_docs`'s OR-composition (no-soft-deletes-field passthrough, all-live-state, combined-with-existing-hard-deletes, same-doc-both-mechanisms) -- all against the real checked-in `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture's genuinely sparse (`IndexedDISI`) `sparse` numeric field (task #4/#21's own real-Lucene-written bytes: docs 0/2/4 present, 1/3 absent), not a hand-built or dense-encoded stand-in (a dense field can't represent "no value at all" for any doc, so it can't stand in for a real soft-deletes field's presence semantics). An end-to-end composition test additionally reuses the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture (`body`/`bird` -> docs `[1, 4]`) together with that same real sparse doc-values field to confirm `effective_live_docs`'s output composes correctly with `search_term_query`: doc 4 (soft-deleted per the real doc-values fixture) is excluded from the real term-query match, leaving only doc 1, and additionally hard-deleting doc 1 leaves nothing live at all -- proving the OR-composition against real decoded bytes end-to-end, not just self-consistently. **Deliberately out of scope beyond the write-side gap above**: cross-segment orchestration (like `directory_reader.rs`, this operates on one already-opened segment at a time; a caller wires it in per segment) and `lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure. |
| `index/NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates` + `IndexWriter.updateNumericDocValue` (single-generation incremental numeric doc-values update, not the full multi-generation `docValuesGen` lifecycle) | `lucene-codecs/src/doc_values_updates.rs::{write_numeric_updates, read_numeric_updates, numeric_value_with_updates}`, wired into `lucene-search/src/soft_deletes.rs::{mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay, is_soft_deleted_with_overlay, effective_live_docs_with_overlay}` | **ported (task #54), single-generation MVP -- unblocks task #48's documented write-side gap.** Real Lucene marks a doc's doc-values field with a new value without rewriting the whole segment's `.dvd`/`.dvm` triple by appending a small "generation" file of sparse `(docId, value)` deltas (`NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates`/`FieldUpdatesWriter`), applied as an overlay over the base doc-values at read time, with `SegmentCommitInfo.docValuesGen` tracking which generations exist and newest-generation-wins when the same doc is touched across many rounds. This port implements exactly the core mechanism for **one** overlay round: `write_numeric_updates` encodes a sparse `(docId -> newValue)` map (sorted, de-duplicated keeping the last write per doc) into a small standalone file reusing this crate's `codec_util` header/footer/CRC conventions for structural integrity; `read_numeric_updates` decodes it back to a `HashMap<i32, i64>`, validating strictly-ascending doc ids; `numeric_value_with_updates` composes an already-decoded overlay map with the existing base `doc_values::numeric_value` decode, overlay winning when present. **Byte format is this port's own invention, not a real-Lucene port**: there is no checked-in fixture for `NumericDocValuesFieldUpdates`' actual on-disk generation-file bytes (same honest situation as task #49/#52's index-sort format), and given this task's own MVP scope decision (below), there's no plan to derive one either -- only the header/footer/CRC shell reuses `codec_util`, the field layout in between is invented for this task and documented as such in the module's own doc comment. **Scope decision, made explicit**: multiple sequential overlay generations with newest-wins semantics across rounds, and `SegmentCommitInfo`/`.si` `docValuesGen` metadata wiring, are both deliberately deferred -- this is "the update-overlay mechanism itself works and is correct" for one round, not the full commit-lifecycle integration. **Wired into task #48's soft-deletes flow**: `mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay` marks a doc soft-deleted by writing *only* an overlay file (any value, per task #48's presence-based semantics) with zero base-file I/O; `is_soft_deleted_with_overlay`/`effective_live_docs_with_overlay` extend task #48's existing presence check and combined-bitset computation to consult the overlay first, falling back to the base decode -- the concrete, real "incremental update without full rewrite" property task #48's own write-side gap called for. **Verified**: unit tests cover overlay round-trip (including unsorted input and duplicate-doc last-write-wins), an empty overlay round-tripping to an empty map, wrong-segment-id and truncated-file rejection, and a hand-built out-of-order-doc-ids rejection (exercising the validation path no honest writer output can reach); overlay-vs-base composition tests cover overlay-overrides-base, base-fallback-when-absent-from-overlay, and empty-overlay-is-a-no-op, all against a base numeric field built through the real `write_single_dense_numeric_field`/`parse_meta` round trip (not hand-rolled bytes). The soft-deletes integration is verified against the real checked-in `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` sparse fixture (task #4/#21/#48's own real-Lucene-written bytes, docs 0/2/4 soft-deleted in the base, 1/3 not): marking doc 3 soft-deleted via `mark_soft_deleted_via_overlay` alone (no base rewrite) makes `is_soft_deleted_with_overlay`/`effective_live_docs_with_overlay` correctly exclude it while the plain base-only `is_soft_deleted` still (correctly) reports it as not soft-deleted, proving the base bytes were genuinely untouched; additional tests cover the empty-overlay-matches-plain-version case and the no-base-soft-deletes-field-but-overlay-present case. |
| `index/DirectoryReader.openIfChanged(DirectoryReader)` (NRT reopen against an already-committed `Directory`, not the `ReaderPool`-backed writer overload) | `lucene-search/src/directory_reader.rs::DirectoryReader::open_if_changed` | **ported (task #46), scoped precisely below.** `reader.open_if_changed(dir)` reads `dir`'s latest `segments_N` and compares its generation to the one `reader` was opened from: identical generation returns `Ok(None)`, matching real `openIfChanged`'s "nothing changed" convention (callers keep using their existing reader rather than rebuild it). A changed generation builds a new `DirectoryReader` through a shared helper, `open_at_reusing`, which for each segment in the new commit looks for an already-open `SegmentReader` in `reader`'s own segment list matching on segment name **and** segment id **and** `del_gen`, reusing it in-memory (`SegmentReader::clone_reader`, a plain struct clone -- `BlockTreeFields`/`FixedBitSet` are already `Clone` -- no file I/O) only when all three match, and opening fresh from disk otherwise (`SegmentReader::open`, the same path `DirectoryReader::open_at` already used). `del_gen` is now tracked on `SegmentReader` (a new private field, populated from the owning commit at open time) precisely so a delete-only change on an otherwise-unchanged segment -- same name/id, bumped `del_gen` -- is never mistaken for "safe to reuse": that segment's `.liv`/`live_docs` genuinely differ under the new commit, and serving it from the old reader would silently show deleted documents as live. A merged-away or replaced segment always falls into "open fresh," since its replacement has a different name/id. **Verified**: `open_if_changed_returns_none_when_generation_unchanged` (no writes since open -> `None`); `open_if_changed_reuses_unchanged_segment_and_opens_new_one` (a second `flush_stored_only_segment` call adds segment `_1` under a new `segments_N` -- the reopened reader has both segments with correct `doc_base`s, and genuine reuse of segment `_0` is proven, not assumed, by deleting `_0`'s on-disk `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm`/`.fnm` files before calling `open_if_changed`: a fresh open of `_0` would then fail with a file-not-found error, so the call succeeding is only possible if the original in-memory reader was reused); `open_if_changed_reopens_segment_whose_del_gen_changed` (the correctness-critical case -- `deletes::apply_deletes` bumps segment `_0`'s `del_gen` with no new segment added, and the reopened reader's `live_docs` reflects the new deletion rather than the original "no deletions" state). **Deliberately scoped down from real Lucene's actual `openIfChanged`**: this is one reader reopening itself, not the `ReaderPool`-wide sharing real `IndexWriter`/`StandardDirectoryReader` provide (there, *every* open `DirectoryReader` in a process benefits from another reader's already-open segments, not just the one being reopened); no `SearcherFactory`/`ReaderManager` warm-up-listener hook runs on newly-opened sub-readers before they're handed back; and there is still no `openIfChanged(IndexWriter)` overload (reading uncommitted flushed segments directly from an in-memory writer rather than a committed `segments_N` on disk) -- that remains PLAN.md §2 item 7's larger, writer-integrated NRT scope, unaddressed here. |
| `index/IndexReader.getTermVector(int doc, String field)` (query-facing read API over term vectors) | `lucene-search/src/term_vectors_query.rs::{term_vector_for_doc, matched_term_offsets}` | **ported (task #39), a thin adapter -- no new byte-format decoding.** `term_vector_for_doc` resolves a `(doc, field name)` pair to `crates/lucene-codecs/src/term_vectors.rs`'s `(doc, field number)` shape via `FieldInfos` and returns that already-decoded `TermVectorField` (every term with its frequency, and whichever of positions/offsets/payloads that field had turned on at index time -- all already fully decodable per task #3/#26's work, nothing new added here). Mirrors real `IndexReader.getTermVector`'s `null`-return convention: `Ok(None)` for an unknown field name, a doc with no term vectors at all, or a doc missing that particular field; `Err` only propagates straight from `TermVectorsReader::document` (doc ID out of range, or a corrupt `.tvd`/`.tvx` region), the same passthrough convention every other `lucene-search` query function already uses for its codec reader. **Highlighting primitive, precisely scoped**: `matched_term_offsets` computes `(term, start_offset, end_offset)` spans for a set of matched terms in one field -- exactly what a `Highlighter`/`UnifiedHighlighter` needs to slice source text at match boundaries -- but only this one primitive; there is no fragment selection, snippet assembly, or `PassageFormatter`-equivalent, and it returns `None` outright (not a fabricated guess) when the field wasn't indexed with offsets (`has_offsets == false`), since this port never decoded any to begin with. Positions and payloads are equally already-decodable but aren't surfaced through a dedicated function here -- callers read them straight off the `TermVectorField`/`TermVectorTerm` `term_vector_for_doc` returns. **No new fixture generated**: per the `differential-testing` skill's precedent for composition/wiring tasks (#36-38), this task's logic (field-name resolution, error passthrough, span computation) touches no new byte format, so its tests reuse the real, already cross-engine-verified `fixtures/data/term_vectors_index/` fixture (task #3's) rather than generating new Java output. Unit-tested: field resolved by name with real offsets returned; unmatched term yields no spans; unknown field name, a field known in `FieldInfos` but not stored for that doc, and a doc with no term vectors at all all return `None`; an out-of-range doc ID surfaces as `Err`; a field without offsets makes `matched_term_offsets` return `None`. **Deliberately out of scope**: multi-segment federation (this function still takes one already-opened segment's `TermVectorsReader` directly; task #45's `DirectoryReader` doesn't open term-vectors files at all -- `OpenSegment` has no term-vectors field, see that row above), and the write side's existing offsets/payloads gap (`write_best_speed` still only supports positions -- unrelated to this read-side task, tracked in the write-side row above). **Fragment selection/snippet assembly, the one thing this row's own note above deferred, is now addressed by task #56 -- see the next row.** |
| `search/uhighlight/UnifiedHighlighter` + `PassageFormatter` (fragment assembly / text-snippet highlighting; not `BreakIterator`-based sentence detection or term-density passage scoring) | `lucene-search/src/highlighter.rs::{Fragment, FragmentConfig, assemble_fragments}` | **ported (task #56), a real but honestly-scoped MVP -- simplified passage-boundary heuristic, not `BreakIterator`.** Given the original field text and a set of task #39's `TermOffsetSpan`s, `assemble_fragments` slices out fixed-size (`window_chars`-configurable) character windows around each match (or cluster of nearby matches), wraps matches in caller-configurable `pre`/`post` markers (default `<b>`/`</b>`, real Lucene's `PassageFormatter` default), and merges overlapping/abutting windows into one fragment rather than emitting duplicates -- capped at `max_fragments`. **Passage-boundary heuristic, documented as a simplification, not silently pretended sentence-aware**: window edges are snapped outward to the nearest whitespace boundary so a fragment doesn't start/end mid-word, but there is no term-density scoring; fragments are simply emitted in left-to-right document order and truncated at `max_fragments`. **Sentence-boundary snapping, opt-in via `FragmentConfig::snap_to_sentence` (default `false`, prior behavior unchanged)**: when set, a fragment's rendered edges snap to the sentence(s) containing its match(es) instead of the fixed window -- a real but deliberately narrow terminator rule (`.`/`!`/`?` followed, after skipping whitespace, by an uppercase letter or the text's end), **not** ICU/`BreakIterator`-grade Unicode sentence segmentation: no locale rules, no comprehensive abbreviation dictionary. **Extended (still not ICU-grade)**: a small hardcoded English-only abbreviation list (`ABBREVIATIONS` -- "mr"/"mrs"/"ms"/"dr"/"jr"/"sr"/"vs"/"etc"/"inc"/"st"/"prof"/"capt"/"co"/"ltd"/"gen") now suppresses a sentence break after these specific words' trailing `.`, closing the previously-documented "Mr. Smith" false positive (re-tested by `sentence_snap_abbreviation_list_closes_mr_smith_false_positive`, now asserting no break); any abbreviation not on this short fixed list still produces the old false positive (`sentence_snap_unlisted_abbreviation_still_breaks`, using "Cmdr."), so this is a targeted fix, not universal period-suppression. **Found in review**: "st" on the list (for "St." as in a street name) would otherwise also swallow the sentence break after any ordinal number ending in "st" (21st., 1st., 91st., ...) -- e.g. "He finished 21st. She started next." incorrectly merging into one fragment. Fixed by excluding an alphabetic run directly preceded by a digit from the abbreviation check (an ordinal suffix, not a real abbreviation), covered by `sentence_snap_ordinal_number_is_not_mistaken_for_st_abbreviation`. A terminator immediately followed by a closing quote (`"`/`'`/U+201D/U+2019) or paren/bracket (`)`/`]`/`}`) before any whitespace is now recognized as a sentence end too (the closing punctuation is skipped before the whitespace+uppercase check) -- previously e.g. `He said "Stop." Then left.` wasn't recognized as a break at all, since the character right after `.` wasn't whitespace (`sentence_snap_closing_quote_after_terminator_is_recognized`, `sentence_snap_closing_paren_after_terminator_is_recognized`). Decimal numbers ("3.5", "$5.00") were already handled correctly by the base terminator rule and needed no change. **Marker-insertion correctness for multi-match fragments**: `render_cluster` inserts `pre`/`post` around each match within a merged fragment working from the last match backward, so an earlier (leftward) insertion's byte offsets are never invalidated by a later one -- the one part of this logic genuinely easy to get subtly wrong, and covered by a dedicated test with two nearby matches merging into one fragment with both terms highlighted and neither original word corrupted. **Offset-unit finding**: term-vector offsets are decoded verbatim by task #3/#39 and never reinterpreted, carrying whatever unit real Lucene's `Analyzer` wrote at index time (UTF-16 code units in real Lucene); this port's checked-in fixture is ASCII-only so byte/UTF-16/scalar counts are indistinguishable there. `highlighter.rs` treats incoming offsets as Unicode-scalar (`char`) counts (equivalent to UTF-16 for the entire Basic Multilingual Plane) and converts to UTF-8 byte offsets via `char_indices()` before any slicing, so a match spanning a multi-byte UTF-8 character cannot panic even on out-of-range/mis-unitted input (offsets are clamped to the text's char count first). **No new Java fixture needed for the fragment-assembly logic itself** (there is no "real Lucene bytes" to check string-slicing/highlighting against -- correctness here means "produces a sensible readable snippet," checked by direct unit tests), but one test composes task #39/#3's real, cross-engine-verified fixture offsets (`fixtures/data/term_vectors_index/`, doc 0's "text" field: "cat"/"car"/"cat" at char offsets 0..3/4..7/8..11) with the real text those exact offsets denote (`"cat car cat"`, per `fixtures/src/GenTermVectors.java`'s `CannedTokenStream` token list), not a made-up string. Unit-tested: single match windowed/highlighted correctly; two nearby matches merge into one fragment with both terms highlighted; two far-apart matches stay separate; window clamping at text start/end without panicking; `max_fragments` truncation; a multi-byte UTF-8 match; out-of-range/invalid spans (negative, end-before-start, past text end) dropped defensively rather than panicking. **Deliberately out of scope**: term-density passage scoring/ranking, and full ICU/`BreakIterator`-grade Unicode sentence segmentation (locale rules, abbreviation dictionaries) even though a real, scoped-down sentence-boundary heuristic is now implemented (see above) -- real, substantial follow-on work, not silently skipped. ~~`lucene-ffi` C-ABI exposure~~ -- closed by the Highlighter FFI exposure task: see the `lucene-ffi` section's `highlighter.rs`/`results_fragments.rs` row for `ffi_assemble_fragments`. |
| `index/CheckIndex` (standalone segment-consistency verifier, self-check only -- not the differential-testing harness) | `lucene-index/src/check_index.rs::{Check, CheckResult, check_segment, check_directory}` | **ported (task #57), scoped to the cross-file/cross-structure checks this port's current write-side scope makes valuable -- not full `CheckIndex`.** Deliberately *not* built on top of `lucene-search`'s `DirectoryReader`/`SegmentReader` (task #45): those types expose only the curated subset of state a query needs and hide exactly what a self-check must cross-reference (`SegmentInfo.files`, per-field flags, raw `.si`/`.fnm`/stored-fields bytes). Lives in `lucene-index` (not `lucene-search`, which it has no actual dependency on -- every type it composes is already available here), and reuses `crate::segment_infos::read_latest` for the shared "find the latest commit, list its segments" step, then opens each segment's files directly through the same lower-level decoders `lucene-search`'s `directory_reader.rs` itself calls. Each check reports independently as a named pass/fail (`Check { name, passed, message }`), matching real `CheckIndex`'s own per-check `Status` reporting style rather than a single boolean. **Implemented**: every file `.si` lists opens and has a structurally valid codec footer (`codec_util::retrieve_checksum` -- doubles as a "forgot to write/list a file" check); `.si` doc_count vs `.liv`'s byte-size-implied word count, derived independently of `si.doc_count` (not by passing it into the decode call, which would make the check vacuous by construction); `live_docs` cardinality vs `SegmentCommitInfo.del_count` (surfaced through `live_docs::parse`'s own `DelCountMismatch`, since that cross-check is already enforced at decode time -- this module reports it under its own named check rather than re-deriving the same arithmetic); `.fnm`'s per-field flags (doc values, norms, term vectors, postings via `index_options != None`) cross-checked in both directions against which of `.dvd`/`.dvm`/`.nvd`/`.nvm`/`.tvd`/`.tvx`/`.tvm`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` the segment's file list actually includes (a field claiming a feature with no matching files is flagged, and so is a file group present with no field claiming it); stored-fields reader's own `max_doc()` vs `.si`'s declared `doc_count`. A `.si` that fails to open/parse short-circuits every other check for that segment (nothing else can be trusted without a valid file list) and reports a single `si.open` failure. **Deliberately deferred** (real, substantial follow-on work per format, not an oversight): postings term-by-term re-derivation (recomputing docFreq/totalTermFreq from raw postings and cross-checking against the term dictionary's own recorded stats -- real `CheckIndex`'s single most expensive check), doc-values value-range sanity, points-tree structural invariants, and vectors-graph structural invariants; each needs its own per-format traversal (blocktree iteration, points-tree traversal, HNSW graph traversal), not a natural extension of this module's cross-file bookkeeping. **No new Java fixture generated**: this is self-consistency logic layered over already-differentially-verified decoders, not new byte-format decoding, so direct unit tests (including deliberately-corrupted inputs) are the right verification method, per the `differential-testing` skill's precedent. Unit-tested: the real `blocktree_index` and `live_docs_index` fixtures pass every check cleanly; deliberately corrupted cases confirm each failure mode reports clearly rather than panicking or false-passing -- a hand-mutated `SegmentCommitInfo.del_count`, a truncated `.liv` file, a `.si` listing a nonexistent file, a `.si` that won't parse at all, a `.liv` whose byte size disagrees with `si.doc_count`, a file with a corrupted footer, a partial `.fdt`/`.fdx`/`.fdm` file set, and a `si.doc_count` that disagrees with a real stored-fields reader's `max_doc()`. Coverage: `lucene-index/src/check_index.rs` 96.97% lines (workspace total 97.25% lines, `cargo llvm-cov --fail-under-lines 95` passing). |
| `search/LRUQueryCache` (per-segment matching-docs bitset cache) | `lucene-search/src/query_cache.rs::QueryCache`, `query_cache.rs::search_term_query_cached` | **new standalone primitive, not a byte-for-byte port of `LRUQueryCache.java`, now wired into one real search entry point (`TermQuery` only) via an opt-in cached wrapper -- the underlying `search_term_query`/`QueryCache::get_or_compute` logic itself is unchanged.** Real `LRUQueryCache` tracks per-segment `IndexReader.CacheKey` identity via weak references, bounds itself by both entry count and estimated RAM usage, and applies a `shouldCache` heuristic to skip caching queries that aren't worth it; none of that is implemented. This module keeps only the core value proposition: given a `(segment, query)` pair, hand back a previously computed `FixedBitSet` of matching doc IDs instead of recomputing it. `QueryCache<S, Q>` is generic over any segment identifier `S: Eq + Hash + Clone` (this port has no `IndexReader.CacheKey`-style segment identity object yet, so a caller-supplied key such as a segment name or generation number stands in) and any query representation `Q: Eq + Hash + Clone`; `query::TermQuery` picked up an additive `Hash` derive (alongside its existing `PartialEq + Eq`) so it can be used directly as `Q`. API: `QueryCache::new(max_entries)`, `get_or_compute(segment, query, || -> FixedBitSet)`, `invalidate_segment(&segment) -> usize`, `remove(&segment, &query) -> bool`, `clear()`, `len()`/`is_empty()`. Eviction is bounded by entry count only (no RAM-based sizing), least-recently-used-first, tracked via a monotonic access counter rather than an external LRU-list crate. No `unsafe` (`lucene-search` is `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`). Unit-tested (`QueryCache` itself): cache miss computes and stores; cache hit reuses the stored bitset without recomputing (verified via a call counter); distinct queries against the same segment get distinct entries; the same query against different segments get distinct entries; inserting past `max_entries` evicts the correct least-recently-used entry; `invalidate_segment` removes only that segment's entries, leaving other segments untouched; a `max_entries == 0` cache never actually retains anything; `clear()` empties every entry; `TermQuery` used end-to-end as a concrete `Q`. **Wired entry point**: `search_term_query_cached(cache, segment, fields, doc_in, live_docs, num_docs, query, collector) -> Result<()>` composes `QueryCache::get_or_compute` with the existing, unchanged `search_term_query` -- opt-in, `search_term_query` itself and every existing caller of it are unaffected. Real-fixture-tested (`blocktree_index`, not synthetic data): the same query run twice against the same segment returns identical, correct doc IDs on both calls, with the second call proven to be a genuine cache hit (not a silent recompute) by omitting `.doc` input on the second call -- both fixture terms tested (`docFreq == 2`) require `.doc` input to actually execute, so a real recompute without it fails with `Error::BlockTree`, making an `Ok` result on the second call proof the cache path was taken; a different query against the same segment key, and the same query against a different segment key, are each proven to be genuine fresh misses the same way; `invalidate_segment` is proven to force a real recompute on the next call for that segment, also the same way. **Explicitly deferred**: RAM-based cache sizing, automatic per-segment invalidation hooks tied to real segment open/close/merge lifecycle events (`invalidate_segment` exists and is correct, but nothing in this port calls it automatically yet -- a caller of `search_term_query_cached` still invokes it manually), cache-worthiness heuristics like real `LRUQueryCache.shouldCache`, and wiring any query type other than `TermQuery` (in particular `BooleanQuery`, blocked on its `Clause::DisjunctionMax` variant embedding a non-`Eq`/`Hash` `f32 tie_breaker`) into a cached entry point. |

## lucene-ffi

| Java file/class | Rust module | Status/notes |
|---|---|---|
| — (no direct Java equivalent; this is the JNI/C-ABI boundary itself, task #20) | `lucene-ffi/src/directory.rs::{ffi_open_directory, ffi_close_directory}` | **new.** Opens/closes a real `lucene_store::directory::FsDirectory` at a caller-given filesystem path, behind an opaque `u64` handle (`lucene-ffi/src/handle.rs::SlotMap`, a hand-rolled generation-tagged slotmap — see that module's doc comment for why it isn't reused from elsewhere in the workspace). Each handle also carries an 8-bit registry-type tag (`RegistryTag::{Directory,Segment,Results,ScoredResults,SortedResults,DirectoryReader,FacetResults}`, the last one added by the Faceted search FFI exposure task) alongside its index/generation bits, so a handle from one of this crate's seven registries is rejected outright by another registry's `get`/`remove` on a tag mismatch, rather than only being caught if its index/generation also happens to miss. |
| — | `lucene-ffi/src/segment.rs::{ffi_open_segment, ffi_close_segment}` | **new, partial.** Opens one segment's `.fnm`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` term dictionary (`lucene_codecs::blocktree::open`) plus, optionally, its `.doc`/`.pos` postings files, from already-known file names/segment ID/suffix/`maxDoc` (a real caller is expected to have already parsed `segments_N`/`.si` to discover these — see that module's doc comment for why this doesn't parse `.si` itself). **Task #30**: `ffi_open_segment` grew optional `nvm_name`/`nvd_name` parameters, opening the segment's `.nvm`/`.nvd` norms pair (`lucene_codecs::norms::{parse_meta, check_data_header_footer}`, always validated against the empty codec suffix — real Lucene's norms format has none, unlike `.tim`/`.doc`/etc) so `ffi_search_*_query_scored` can use real per-doc/avg field lengths instead of always falling back to `similarity::UNNORMED_FIELD_LENGTH`; `SegmentHandle` now also carries the parsed `field_infos` (needed to map a scored query's field *name* to the field *number* `NormsEntry`/`Norms` are keyed by — `BlockTreeFields` has no such mapping of its own). **No `.pay` (payload) parameter yet** — `search_phrase_query`/`search_phrase_query_scored` are always called with `pay_in: None` from `query.rs`. **Task #40**: `ffi_open_segment` grew optional `dvm_name`/`dvd_name`/`dv_suffix` parameters, opening the segment's `.dvm`/`.dvd` doc-values pair (`lucene_codecs::doc_values::{parse_meta, check_data_header_footer}`) so `ffi_sort_by_doc_value`/`ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value` (see below) have real doc-values bytes to sort by; unlike `.nvm`/`.nvd`, `.dvm`/`.dvd` carry their own per-field codec-suffix component in their index header, so `dv_suffix` is a separate parameter from `segment_suffix` rather than reusing it. `SegmentHandle` grew matching `dv_data`/`dv_meta` fields, both `None` when the segment was opened without doc values (the two sort entry points then return `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument` — unlike norms, there's no meaningful constant fallback for "nothing to sort by"). **Points range query FFI exposure task**: `ffi_open_segment` grew optional `kdm_name`/`kdi_name`/`kdd_name` parameters, opening the segment's `.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` BKD points meta/index/data files (`lucene_codecs::points::open`, validated once at open time then stored as owned bytes on a new `SegmentHandle::points_data` field) so `ffi_search_points_range` (see below) has points data to search; like `.nvm`/`.nvd`, always validated against the empty codec suffix (`""`), not `segment_suffix`/`dv_suffix` — real Lucene's points format has no per-field codec-suffix component in its index header either. A segment opened without them can't serve `ffi_search_points_range` (`FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`, same "no sensible fallback" story as doc values' absence). |
| `search/SortField.Type.LONG`/`INT`/`SortedNumericSortField`/`SortedSetSortField` (single-key ascending doc-value sort, C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/sort.rs::{ffi_sort_by_doc_value, ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value}` | **new, task #40.** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrappers around `lucene_search::{sort_by_numeric_doc_value, doc_value_query::sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value}`, following task #30's exact FFI shape: resolve a field name to a NUMERIC/SORTED_NUMERIC `.dvm` entry via the segment's `field_infos` (same name -> number lookup `open_field_norms` already does for norms), run the sort over a caller-given candidate doc-ID list, and store the resulting ascending `(doc_id, value)` pairs under a new `SortedResultsHandle`. The missing-value policy (`lucene_search::MissingValue::Exclude`/`Default(i64)`) crosses the wire as `missing_is_default: bool` + `missing_default: i64` (ignored when the bool is `false`) rather than a tagged union; `ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value`'s `ValueSelector` (MIN/MAX) crosses as an `i32` (`0`/`1`, anything else is `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`). Same "also serves SORTED_SET" reuse `doc_value_query.rs` documents for the multi-valued function applies here too — passing a SORTED_SET field's ordinal-array entry works unchanged. **Ascending-only, single-sort-key-only** (see the deferred row below) — matches `doc_value_query.rs`'s own documented scope; a `descending` flag isn't exposed since the wrapped Rust functions don't support it and a reverse-then-relabel hack wouldn't be real Lucene sort semantics. |
| `search/TopFieldCollector` + `PointRangeQuery`/`SortedNumericDocValuesField.newSlowRangeQuery` (numeric range query, ranked by a doc-value field, ascending or descending — C-ABI wrapper, single- and multi-segment) | `lucene-ffi/src/range_sort.rs::{ffi_search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field, ffi_search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field_multi_segment}` | **new, TopFieldCollector FFI exposure task.** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrappers around `lucene_search::doc_value_query::search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field` (single segment, task #80) and `lucene_search::multi_segment::search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field_multi_segment` (multi-segment fan-out/merge, task #88) — no range-matching, sorting, or doc-ID-translation logic reimplemented, only C-ABI marshaling. **Result-handle shape reuses the existing `SortedResultsHandle`/`registry::sorted_results()` (task #40)**, not a new handle type: both wrapped functions return `Vec<FieldValueDoc>`, i.e. exactly the same `(doc_id: i32, value: i64)` wire shape `SortedResultsHandle` already carries for `ffi_sort_by_doc_value`/`ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value` — read back via the existing `ffi_sorted_results_len`/`ffi_sorted_results_copy`/`ffi_close_sorted_results` trio, no new accessor functions needed. `direction` crosses the wire as an `i32` (`0` = `SortDirection::Ascending`, `1` = `SortDirection::Descending`, anything else is `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`), the same `0`/`1`-selector convention `ffi_sort_by_multi_valued_doc_value`'s `ValueSelector` already established; `range_field`/`sort_field` are looked up via the existing `sort.rs::numeric_entry_for` helper (now `pub(crate)`, reused rather than duplicated), and `missing_is_default`/`missing_default` reuse `sort.rs::missing_value` unchanged. **Multi-segment wire format is a flat array of already-open segment handles plus a parallel caller-supplied `doc_base` array, not a `DirectoryReaderHandle`**: task #51's `DirectoryReaderHandle` carries no `.dvm`/`.dvd` doc-values data per segment at all, so there is nothing for a reader-handle-based entry point to read a doc-value from — each already-opened `ffi_open_segment` handle already carries its own `dv_data`/`dv_meta` (task #40), so this function instead looks up each handle in the existing `segments()` registry and builds the exact `lucene_search::multi_segment::DocValueSegment` list that function already expects, with the caller supplying each segment's `doc_base` explicitly (a segment has no way to know its own position in a larger commit on its own). `live_docs` is always `None`, the same documented "no `.liv` FFI surface yet" behavior every other query entry point in this crate already has. **Verified**: differential test asserting the FFI wrapper's output matches calling `search_numeric_range_sorted_by_field` directly against the same real `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture bytes; both sort directions and top-`n` truncation; the missing-value default policy; multi-segment doc-ID translation and tie-break (the same fixture segment opened twice with different `doc_base`s, mirroring `multi_segment.rs`'s own cross-segment tests); and the usual null-pointer/unknown-handle/decode-error/invalid-direction/invalid-field/segment-without-doc-values error paths for both entry points. No new Java fixture generator needed — this is FFI wiring around already cross-engine-verified `lucene-search` logic (tasks #80/#88), not new correctness surface. Coverage: `range_sort.rs` 99.33% lines, 99.03% regions. |
| `search/PointRangeQuery` (search-side, single already-opened segment — C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/points_query.rs::ffi_search_points_range` | **new, Points range query FFI exposure task.** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrapper around `lucene_search::points_query::search_points_range` (task #81) — no BKD read/traversal or packed-value comparison logic reimplemented, only C-ABI marshaling: resolve `field` (a caller-supplied name) to a field *number* via the segment's `field_infos` (same `find(|f| f.name == field)` pattern `sort.rs::numeric_entry_for`/`query.rs::open_field_norms` already use — an unknown name is `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`, distinct from `search_points_range`'s own "unknown field *number* matches nothing" convention, which only applies once a valid number is already in hand), reconstruct a `PointsReader` from the segment's stored `.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` bytes (see the segment-open row above for the new `kdm_name`/`kdi_name`/`kdd_name` parameters), and collect matches into a new `ResultsHandle`. **Result-handle shape reuses the existing `ResultsHandle`/`registry::results()` (task #20's original unscored FFI work), no new handle type**: `search_points_range` collects through this crate's plain `Collector` trait into a flat, ascending `Vec<i32>` of matched doc IDs — exactly the same shape `query.rs`'s `ffi_search_term_query`/`ffi_search_boolean_query`/`ffi_search_phrase_query` already collect into `ResultsHandle`; a `PointRangeQuery`-shaped match has no score and no sort key of its own (real Lucene's is `ConstantScoreQuery`-shaped, per `search_points_range`'s own module doc), so neither `ScoredResultsHandle` nor `SortedResultsHandle` fit — reused verbatim via the existing `ffi_results_len`/`ffi_results_copy`/`ffi_close_results` trio, no new accessor trio needed. **Explicit packed-length check, not a caught panic**: `search_points_range` documents that a wrong `min_packed`/`max_packed` length panics via a slice index — reachable here from adversarial caller bytes (unlike, e.g., `range_sort.rs`'s array-length check, noted unreachable by construction there), so this wrapper checks the expected length itself first and returns `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument` rather than relying on `guard`'s `catch_unwind` to produce `FfiStatus::Panic`. `live_docs` is always `None`, matching every other query entry point in this crate. **Verified**: a differential test asserting the FFI wrapper's output matches calling `search_points_range` directly, against the real `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture's real `.fnm`/`.tim`/`.tip`/`.tmd` plus hand-written single-dimension `.kdm`/`.kdi`/`.kdd` files keyed to that fixture's real "gcd" field number (no pre-generated fixture combines real field infos with points data yet); inclusive boundary values on both ends; the 2D multi-dimension case (mirroring `points_query.rs`'s own two-dimension test); an empty-range case; and the usual null-out-handle/unknown-segment-handle/directory-handle-as-segment-handle/unknown-field-name/segment-without-points-data/wrong-packed-length/decode-error paths. `cargo test -p lucene-ffi`: 300 tests pass (up from 289). Coverage: `points_query.rs` 98.90% regions / 98.83% lines. No new Java fixture generator needed — this is FFI wiring around already cross-engine-verified `lucene-search` logic (task #81), not new correctness surface. |
| `facet/sortedset/SortedSetDocValuesFacetCounts` + `facet/range/LongRangeFacetCounts`/`DoubleRangeFacetCounts` (basic per-ordinal and bucket counting only, C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/facets.rs::{ffi_facet_counts_sorted_set, ffi_range_facet_counts}`, `lucene-ffi/src/results_facets.rs::{ffi_facet_results_len, ffi_facet_results_copy, ffi_facet_result_label, ffi_close_facet_results}` | **new (Faceted search FFI exposure).** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrappers around tasks #50/#58's `lucene_search::facets::{facet_counts, resolve_labels, top_n_facets, range_facet_counts}` — **no facet-counting logic is reimplemented here**, `facets.rs` (the `lucene-search` module) is unchanged by this task. `ffi_facet_counts_sorted_set` resolves `field` to a SORTED_SET `.dvm` entry via the segment's `field_infos` (same name -> number lookup `sort.rs`'s `numeric_entry_for` already uses), runs `facet_counts` + `resolve_labels` over a caller-given candidate doc-ID list, then `top_n_facets` only when `top_n > 0` (`top_n == 0` returns every facet in ordinal order, untruncated, by simply not calling it), storing the resolved `(ord, label, count)` triples under a new `FacetResultsHandle`/`RegistryTag::FacetResults`. **Only `SortedSetKind::Multi` is supported** — a `Single`-kind field is `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument`, since `facet_counts` itself has no counting path for that representation (not a gap this FFI layer introduces; see `facets.rs`'s module doc). `ffi_range_facet_counts` resolves `field` to a NUMERIC `.dvm` entry the same way, builds `ranges_count` `NumericRange`s from five parallel input arrays (`range_mins`/`range_min_inclusive`/`range_maxs`/`range_max_inclusive`/label bytes sliced by `range_label_lens`), runs `range_facet_counts`, and writes counts straight into a caller-allocated `out_counts: *mut u64` buffer — **no output handle at all**, since every range's label is caller-supplied input already known to the caller, unlike the SortedSet case's index-resolved labels. `ffi_facet_results_len`/`ffi_facet_results_copy` read the SortedSet handle's `(ord, count)` pairs back via parallel `i64`/`u64` buffers (same shape `results_sorted.rs` established); `ffi_facet_result_label` is a new per-index string accessor reusing this crate's existing `buf`/`buf_len`/`out_written`/`BufferTooSmall` contract from `ffi_get_last_error_message`, since a facet's resolved label is a variable-length string that doesn't fit the fixed-size parallel-buffer shape. **Verified**: `facets::tests` cross-checks the SortedSet FFI path's output against calling `lucene_search::facets::{facet_counts, resolve_labels}` directly on the same real `fixtures/data/multi_valued_dv_index/` fixture bytes (`tags` field), plus `top_n` truncation, unknown/wrong-entry-kind field, unknown segment handle, null out-handle, null candidates with a nonzero length, empty candidates, and a field with no SORTED_SET entry; the range path is verified against the real `fixtures/data/doc_values_index/` fixture's `varying` field (same values `sort.rs`'s own tests use), plus zero-ranges, unknown field, a field with no NUMERIC entry, null out-counts/candidates/mins/label-data, an invalid-UTF-8 label, and unknown segment handle cases. `results_facets::tests` covers len/copy/label round-trip, buffer-too-small on both the copy and label calls, a null label buffer, empty-results no-op, null-pointer variants, an out-of-bounds label index, and unknown/double-close handle rejection. `cargo test -p lucene-ffi`: 189 tests pass (up from 156). **Deferred, not a gap introduced by this task**: `SortedSetKind::Single` counting (no underlying `facets.rs` support exists to wrap); index-wide/multi-segment facet aggregation (same scope boundary tasks #50/#58 already documented for the non-FFI functions); hierarchical/taxonomy facets, drill-down/drill-sideways (no `lucene-facet`-module equivalent exists anywhere in this port, FFI or otherwise). |
| `search/uhighlight/UnifiedHighlighter` + `PassageFormatter` (fragment assembly only, C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/highlighter.rs::{ffi_assemble_fragments}`, `lucene-ffi/src/results_fragments.rs::{ffi_fragment_results_len, ffi_fragment_result_text, ffi_fragment_result_matched_terms_len, ffi_fragment_result_matched_term, ffi_close_fragment_results}` | **new (Highlighter FFI exposure).** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrapper around task #56's `lucene_search::highlighter::assemble_fragments` — **no fragment-assembly logic is reimplemented here**, `highlighter.rs` (the `lucene-search` module) is unchanged by this task. Unlike every other function in this crate, `ffi_assemble_fragments` needs no segment/directory handle at all: `assemble_fragments` only takes a field's full text plus a set of `TermOffsetSpan`s, so both cross the wire as plain input buffers rather than a handle lookup — full text as a `(ptr, len)` pair, and `spans_count` spans as four parallel arrays (`span_start_offsets`/`span_end_offsets` plus a concatenated `span_term_data` buffer sliced by `span_term_lens`, the same concatenated-buffer convention `facets.rs`'s `ranges_from_raw` already established for per-range labels). `window_chars`/`pre`/`post`/`max_fragments` build a `FragmentConfig` directly; `max_fragments == 0` is rejected as `FfiStatus::InvalidArgument` rather than silently returning zero fragments. Assembled fragments are collected into a new `FragmentResultsHandle`/`RegistryTag::FragmentResults`, read back via `ffi_fragment_results_len`/`ffi_fragment_result_text`/`ffi_fragment_result_matched_terms_len`/`ffi_fragment_result_matched_term` — all per-index string accessors reusing this crate's existing `buf`/`buf_len`/`out_written`/`BufferTooSmall` contract from `ffi_get_last_error_message`, with **no `_copy` bulk call**: unlike a facet result's `(ord, count)` half, a `Fragment` has no fixed-size field at all (both `text` and `matched_terms` are variable-length). **Verified**: `highlighter::tests` cross-checks the FFI path's output against calling `lucene_search::highlighter::assemble_fragments` directly, reusing task #39/#3's real, cross-engine-verified `fixtures/data/term_vectors_index/`-derived offsets (`"cat car cat"` at char offsets 0..3/4..7/8..11) the same way `highlighter.rs`'s own differential test composes them, plus empty spans, empty full_text with a null pointer and zero length, out-of-range spans dropped rather than erroring, null out-handle, null full_text with nonzero length, null pre/post, null span_term_lens/span_term_data with nonzero counts, an invalid-UTF-8 term, and zero `max_fragments`. `results_fragments::tests` covers len/text/matched-terms-len/matched-term round-trip, out-of-bounds fragment index and out-of-bounds term index on every accessor, buffer-too-small on both text and matched-term calls, null buffers, and unknown/double-close handle rejection. `cargo test -p lucene-ffi`: 221 tests pass (up from 189). New-file coverage: `highlighter.rs` 100.00% lines, `results_fragments.rs` 100.00% lines. **Deferred, not a gap introduced by this task**: `term_vectors_query::matched_term_offsets` has no FFI wrapper of its own yet — a JNI-only caller with no direct Rust-side access to `lucene-search` would need that exposed too before it could compute real `TermOffsetSpan`s itself; `ffi_assemble_fragments` takes spans as plain caller-supplied input rather than assuming that gap closed. Term-density passage scoring and full ICU/`BreakIterator`-grade sentence segmentation remain out of scope, matching `highlighter.rs`'s own already-documented scope boundary. `ffi_assemble_fragments` now also takes a `snap_to_sentence: u8` flag (C-`bool`-style) so `highlighter.rs`'s opt-in sentence-boundary-snapping mode is reachable across the FFI boundary, cross-checked against a direct `lucene_search::highlighter::assemble_fragments` call in `highlighter::tests::assemble_fragments_snap_to_sentence_flag_matches_direct_call`. |
| `search/IndexSearcher.explain(Query, int)` + `search/Explanation` (C-ABI wrapper, term/phrase/flat-boolean clauses only) | `lucene-ffi/src/explain.rs::{ffi_explain_term_query, ffi_explain_phrase_query, ffi_explain_boolean_query}`, `lucene-ffi/src/results_explain.rs::{ffi_explain_results_len, ffi_explain_node_value, ffi_explain_node_matched, ffi_explain_node_description, ffi_explain_node_child_count, ffi_explain_node_child_at, ffi_close_explain_results}` | **new (Explain FFI exposure).** Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrappers around task #59's `lucene_search::explain::explain_clause` — **no explain logic is reimplemented here**, `lucene-search/src/explain.rs` is unchanged by this task. Each of the three functions builds exactly the same `Clause` `query.rs`'s matching `ffi_search_*_query_scored` sibling already builds (same wire formats, same norms-map construction, reused via a newly-`pub(crate)` `query::open_field_norms`) and hands it straight to `explain_clause`. **Scope deliberately matches `query.rs`'s existing clause-construction surface, not `explain_clause`'s full ten-variant `Clause` enum**: only `Clause::Term`/`Clause::Phrase`/flat-`Clause::Term`-only `Clause::Boolean` are wrapped, since those are the only three shapes `query.rs` can build from FFI input at all — `DisjunctionMax`/`ConstantScore`/`Boost`/`Wildcard`/`Prefix`/`Fuzzy`/`Regexp`/`Span`/truly-nested-`Boolean` explanations have no wrapper because those clauses can't be *searched* through this ABI either, not a gap this task introduced. **The recursive-tree problem**: `Explanation` is a recursive tree (`details: Vec<Self>`, e.g. a single term explanation is already three levels deep — `weight(...)` → `score(freq=...)` → `idf`/`tfNorm`), unlike every prior FFI result (`facets.rs`/`highlighter.rs` both flat lists). Chosen scheme: depth-first, pre-order flattening into `Vec<registry::ExplainNode>` at construction time — each node keeps its own `value`/`matched`/`description` plus a `Vec<usize>` of *its children's indices into that same flat `Vec`* (a child-index list per node rather than a parent-index-per-node scheme, so "this node's Nth child" is an O(1) lookup, not an O(total nodes) scan); pre-order guarantees the root is always flattened first, so **node index `0` is always the root**. `ffi_explain_results_len`/`ffi_explain_node_value`/`ffi_explain_node_matched` read the fixed-size per-node fields; `ffi_explain_node_description` is a per-node string accessor reusing this crate's existing `buf`/`buf_len`/`out_written`/`BufferTooSmall` contract; `ffi_explain_node_child_count`/`ffi_explain_node_child_at` (the same "length first, then per-index accessor" shape `results_fragments.rs` established for a fragment's matched-terms list, applied here to a node's children) let a caller walk the whole tree starting at node `0`. New `RegistryTag::ExplainResults`/`registry::ExplainResultsHandle` (own registry — an explain node's shape has no correspondence to any existing handle's element). **Verified**: `explain::tests` cross-checks the term/phrase/boolean FFI paths against calling `lucene_search::explain::explain_clause` directly on the same real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture, walking the **entire** flattened tree via the FFI accessors node-by-node (not just the root value) and independently re-deriving every `ffi_explain_node_child_at` link against a from-scratch Rust-side re-flattening of the same `Explanation`, plus a non-matching doc collapsing to a single no-match node, a single-term phrase delegating to the same tree a direct term-explain call produces, a missing-`.pos`-input multi-term phrase surfacing as `FfiStatus::Search`, an empty boolean query as a single no-match node, and unknown-handle/null-pointer/invalid-UTF-8 cases for each of the three functions. `results_explain::tests` covers a full tree round-trip (value/matched/description/child-count/child-at on both an internal and a leaf node), out-of-bounds node/child index on every accessor, buffer-too-small on the description accessor, null-pointer variants, and unknown/double-close handle rejection. `cargo test -p lucene-ffi`: 261 tests pass (up from 221). New-file coverage: `explain.rs` 97.05% lines, `results_explain.rs` 100.00% lines (the handful of missed `explain.rs` lines are `.doc`/`.pos` reopen-decode-error branches identical in shape to `query.rs`'s own already-accepted untested branches, unreachable without hand-corrupting already-validated segment bytes). **Deferred, not a gap introduced by this task**: every clause kind `query.rs` itself doesn't expose (see above) has no explain wrapper either — a follow-up to `query.rs`'s own wire format, not to `explain.rs` (either crate). |
| `search/IndexSearcher.search(Query, Collector)` (single-segment slice, C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/query.rs::{ffi_search_term_query, ffi_search_boolean_query, ffi_search_phrase_query, ffi_search_term_query_scored, ffi_search_boolean_query_scored, ffi_search_phrase_query_scored}` | **new** (unscored); **new, task #30** (scored). Thin `catch_unwind`-guarded wrappers around `lucene_search::{search_term_query, search_boolean_query, search_phrase_query}`, collecting every matching doc ID into a plain `lucene_search::VecCollector` (entirely Rust-side — no callback ever crosses back into the caller) and storing the result under a new results handle. `BooleanQuery`'s `must`/`should`/`must_not` clause lists cross the boundary as four parallel flat arrays per bucket (`*_fields`/`*_field_lens`/`*_terms`/`*_term_lens`, length `*_count`) — a common C-ABI pattern for a variable-length list of fixed-shape records. `live_docs` is always `None` (no `.liv` FFI surface yet, see below). **The `_scored` siblings (task #30)** wrap `lucene_search::{search_term_query_scored, search_boolean_query_scored, search_phrase_query_scored}`, feeding a `lucene_search::TopDocsCollector` (constructed from a caller-given `top_n`) instead of a `VecCollector`, and storing the `(doc_id, score)` hits under a new `ScoredResultsHandle`. Each scored function's segment-handle norms (see the `segment.rs` row above) are looked up per call via a small `open_field_norms` helper (name -> field number -> `NormsEntry` -> `FieldNorms::open`, recomputing `avgFieldLength` every call rather than caching it on `SegmentHandle` — a deliberate simplicity-over-micro-optimization call, documented in that helper's doc comment); `ffi_search_boolean_query_scored` builds one `HashMap<String, FieldNorms>` from every distinct field name across its flat `must`/`should`/`must_not` term-clause arrays. Same deferred-nested-clause-construction limitation as the unscored sibling (flat `Clause::Term` only). |
| — | `lucene-ffi/src/results.rs::{ffi_results_len, ffi_results_copy, ffi_close_results}`, `lucene-ffi/src/results_scored.rs::{ffi_scored_results_len, ffi_scored_results_copy, ffi_close_scored_results}` (task #30), `lucene-ffi/src/results_sorted.rs::{ffi_sorted_results_len, ffi_sorted_results_copy, ffi_close_sorted_results}` (task #40) | **new.** Reads a results handle's collected doc IDs back out via a caller-allocated buffer (`ffi_results_len` sizes it, `ffi_results_copy` bulk-copies — chosen over a per-index accessor since a JNI caller almost always wants the whole array at once, see that module's doc comment), then releases the handle. No Rust-side-allocated memory ever crosses the boundary in this slice — `ffi_results_copy`/`ffi_scored_results_copy`/`ffi_sorted_results_copy` only ever write into a buffer the caller already allocated. **`ffi_scored_results_copy` (task #30)** writes into two caller-allocated *parallel* buffers (`out_doc_ids: *mut i32`, `out_scores: *mut f32`, same `buf_len`) rather than one interleaved buffer — see `results_scored.rs`'s module doc for why; backed by a new `ScoredResultsHandle`/`registry::scored_results()` registry (a separate `RegistryTag`, not a widened `ResultsHandle`) so a results handle from the wrong search flavor is rejected by the handle-tag check rather than misread. **`ffi_sorted_results_copy` (task #40)** is the same parallel-buffers shape again (`out_doc_ids: *mut i32`, `out_values: *mut i64`), backed by yet another separate `SortedResultsHandle`/`registry::sorted_results()` registry — a sort's second element is an arbitrary doc-value, not a BM25 score, so it gets its own handle type rather than being folded into `ScoredResultsHandle`. |
| — | `lucene-ffi/src/error.rs::{FfiStatus, guard, ffi_get_last_error_message}` | **new.** Every exported function's body runs inside `guard`, which wraps `std::panic::catch_unwind` and converts a caught panic into a stable `FfiStatus::Panic` status code plus a thread-local last-error message (readable via `ffi_get_last_error_message`) instead of letting the unwind cross into the JVM. **Notable implementation detail**: the panic message is captured via a process-wide panic hook (installed once, active only while the calling thread is inside `guard`) rather than by downcasting `catch_unwind`'s `Box<dyn Any + Send>` payload to `&str`/`String` — the ordinary downcast approach was tried first and found to intermittently fail to match either type in this environment even though the same payload's type is correctly observable from a hook at panic time; see `error.rs`'s `install_panic_hook` doc comment for the full investigation. Every handle-taking function validates its handle(s) against the relevant `SlotMap` before doing anything else, returning `FfiStatus::InvalidHandle` on a miss (stale/closed/unknown handles never dereference freed state). Every call site locks its registry's `Mutex` via `registry::lock_recovering` (`.lock().unwrap_or_else(|poisoned| poisoned.into_inner())`) rather than a bare `.lock().unwrap()` — a panic caught by `guard` while a registry lock was held would otherwise poison that `Mutex` permanently, making every later `.lock().unwrap()` on it panic again forever (turning one bad call into a permanently broken registry); recovering the poisoned guard is sound here since every `SlotMap` mutation is a single non-panicking sequence with no possibility of a torn write. **Task #30's regression test for the scored path** (`registry_mutex_recovers_from_poisoning_after_a_panic_mid_scored_query`) uses a `thread_local!`-scoped panic-injection switch rather than reusing task #20's process-wide `AtomicBool` one (`PANIC_ON_NEXT_TERM_QUERY`) — `cargo test`'s default parallel execution means a process-wide flag armed by one test can fire inside a different, concurrently-running test's call to the same function, a real (if narrow) flakiness source task #29's review flagged in the pre-existing unscored-path test; the new thread-local flag is immune to that race by construction (arming and firing always happen on the same test's own thread). The pre-existing `PANIC_ON_NEXT_TERM_QUERY` itself was not changed by this task — fixing it is tracked as a separate follow-up. |
| `index/DirectoryReader.open(Directory)` + `IndexSearcher.search` fan-out, sequential and concurrent (C-ABI wrapper) | `lucene-ffi/src/directory_reader.rs::{ffi_open_directory_reader, ffi_close_directory_reader, ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment, ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment, ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent, ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent}` | **new, task #51.** Exposes task #45's `lucene_search::directory_reader::DirectoryReader` and task #41's multi-segment fan-out/merge over the C ABI, following tasks #20/#30/#40's exact FFI pattern (opaque `u64` handles, `catch_unwind`-guarded `extern "C" fn`s via `guard`, `lock_recovering` registry-mutex access, bounds-checked out-buffers). A new `RegistryTag::DirectoryReader`/`registry::directory_readers()` registry backs a `DirectoryReaderHandle`; `ffi_open_directory_reader` takes a filesystem path directly (not an already-open `ffi_open_directory` handle -- a `DirectoryReader` copies every segment's bytes into its own owned buffers at open time and needs the directory for no longer than that one call, unlike `ffi_open_segment`'s directory-handle-reuse case). `ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment`/`ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment` reuse task #30's existing `ScoredResultsHandle`/`ffi_scored_results_len`/`ffi_scored_results_copy`/`ffi_close_scored_results` trio rather than inventing a new results type, since multi-segment search returns the exact same `Vec<ScoreDoc>` shape single-segment scored search already does. Every per-segment norms slot passed to the wrapped `lucene_search` functions is `None` -- task #45's `DirectoryReader` carries no `.nvm`/`.nvd` data, so every multi-segment scored query here falls back to `similarity::UNNORMED_FIELD_LENGTH`, the same documented fallback single-segment scored queries already use for a bare `None`. **Avoiding task #29's flakiness pattern**: the new poison-recovery regression test arms a **thread-local** `Cell<bool>` switch (`PANIC_ON_NEXT_MULTI_SEGMENT_QUERY`), following `query.rs`'s post-task-#29 `PANIC_ON_NEXT_SCORED_TERM_QUERY` precedent rather than task #20's older process-wide `AtomicBool`, since `cargo test`'s parallel thread pool can otherwise let one test's armed flag fire inside a different, concurrently-running test's call to the same function. **Verified**: happy-path multi-segment term and boolean search against the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture; wrong-tag handle rejection in both directions (a `ScoredResultsHandle` id passed as a reader handle, and a `DirectoryReader` handle passed to `ffi_scored_results_len`); null-pointer/unknown-handle/double-close cases for every new entry point; the poison-recovery regression test above. No new Java fixture needed -- this is FFI wiring around already cross-engine-verified `lucene-search` logic (tasks #41/#45), not new correctness surface. Coverage: `directory_reader.rs` 96.04% lines.

**Progress (Concurrent segment search FFI exposure):** `ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent`/`ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent` expose task #68's `search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent` (`lucene-search/src/multi_segment.rs`, the `rayon`-based sibling row above) over the identical wire format, handle validation, and `ScoredResultsHandle` readback the sequential wrappers above already use -- no search/merge logic reimplemented at this layer, only the fan-out function called differs (`_concurrent` instead of the sequential one). **Verified**, including the critical byte-for-byte proof at the FFI boundary itself: `term_query_multi_segment_concurrent_matches_sequential_ffi_wrapper`/`boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent_matches_sequential_ffi_wrapper` each open two independent `DirectoryReader` handles against the same real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture, run the sequential wrapper through one handle and the concurrent wrapper through the other, and assert the read-back `(doc_id, score)` vectors are equal -- confirming the identical-output property already proven for the underlying Rust functions still holds with the FFI marshaling/handle/registry layer in the loop. Plus the same real-fixture-happy-path/unknown-reader-handle/null-out-handle coverage every other entry point in this crate carries. `cargo test -p lucene-ffi`: 269 tests pass (up from 261).
