| `queryparser/classic/QueryParser`, `queryparser/flexible/standard/StandardQueryParser` | `lucene-search/src/query_parser.rs::{parse_query, parse_query_with_analyzer, ParseError}` | **a minimal parser inspired by classic `QueryParser`'s syntax (task #44), not a port of `QueryParser.java`/`StandardQueryParser` themselves.** Both real classes are large grammars (JavaCC-generated in the classic case) covering range queries, configurable boolean-operator precedence, per-field analyzers, fractional fuzzy similarity, and a great deal of escaping-edge-case handling; this module is a from-scratch, hand-written recursive-descent parser (same "small, honestly-scoped hand-built parser" precedent `wildcard.rs`/`regexp.rs`/`fuzzy.rs` already established) turning a deliberately small syntax subset directly into this port's existing `Clause` tree — `parse_query(input: &str, default_field: Option<&str>) -> Result<Clause, ParseError>` reuses every already-ported constructor (`TermQuery`/`PhraseQuery`/`BooleanQuery`/`WildcardQuery`/`PrefixQuery`/`FuzzyQuery`/`RegexpQuery`/`BoostQuery`), adding no new query representation. **Boolean-operator style, a deliberate single-style choice**: real classic `QueryParser` supports *both* `+`/`-` prefixes *and* `AND`/`OR`/`NOT` operators simultaneously, with configurable default-operator precedence — exactly the "half-supported mix" this task's scoping explicitly called out to avoid. This parser supports **only** `+`/`-`/bare-is-SHOULD (`+term` = `Occur::MUST`, `-term` = `Occur::MUST_NOT`, bare = `Occur::SHOULD`, mapped straight onto `BooleanQuery`'s existing `must`/`should`/`must_not` buckets with no translation layer); `AND`/`OR`/`NOT` tokens parse as ordinary bare terms, never as operators — unambiguous to parse (every clause's role comes from its own leading character, never from what's between clauses), so no precedence table is needed at all. **Supported grammar**: `field:term` and bare terms (`default_field: Option<&str>`; `None` plus a bare term is a clean `ParseError::MissingField`, never a silent "search every field" guess), quoted `"phrase terms"` → `PhraseQuery`, `field:term~`/`field:term~N` (`N` in `0..=2`, matching `FuzzyQuery`'s own `LevenshteinAutomata.MAXIMUM_SUPPORTED_DISTANCE` range) → `FuzzyQuery`, `field:prefix*` (a single trailing unescaped `*` and no other wildcard char) → `PrefixQuery` vs. `field:c?t`/any other `*`/`?` combination → `WildcardQuery` (mirroring real `QueryParser`'s own `PrefixQuery`-vs-`WildcardQuery` split), `field:/pattern/` (Lucene's own regexp delimiter convention, `\/` escaping a literal slash without ending the pattern) → `RegexpQuery`, `(...)` grouping recursing to arbitrary depth (not just one level — "one grouping construct" was the scoping ask, not a depth cap), and a `^boost` suffix on any atom (term, phrase, group, wildcard, etc.) → `BoostQuery`. Escaping: inside a bareword, `\` followed by any byte inserts that byte literally, stripped from the resulting term — the same convention `wildcard.rs::WildcardPattern::new` already documents. **Deferred explicitly, rejected with a `ParseError` rather than silently mis-parsed**: range queries (`field:[a TO b]`/`field:{a TO b}`, `ParseError::UnsupportedSyntax`), `AND`/`OR`/`NOT` as real operators with precedence rules (not implemented at all), fractional-similarity fuzzy (`term~0.8`, the `StandardQueryParser` float-similarity convention — only a bare `~` or `~` plus a plain `0..=2` integer is accepted), and any escaping edge case beyond the single `\`-then-any-byte rule (e.g. `\uXXXX` Unicode escapes). **Verification**: no cross-engine Java fixture applies here (there's no "real Lucene bytes" for query-string *syntax* to decode — the correctness question is "does this string parse to the `Clause` a human would expect," per this task's own scoping note) — unit tests in `query_parser.rs` cover every supported grammar construct (single term, `field:term`, phrase, `+`/`-` combination, wildcard, prefix, fuzzy with/without explicit edit distance, regexp with/without escaping, one level and nested parenthesized groups, boost on a term and on a group) plus every malformed-input case (unclosed quote/paren/regexp, including after a trailing escape; unmatched close paren; missing field; invalid/non-finite boost; invalid fuzziness including out-of-range and fractional; unsupported range syntax; empty/whitespace-only input; empty group) confirming a clean `Err`, never a panic. `crates/lucene-search/tests/query_parser_fixtures.rs` is the honest substitute for a Java fixture: it parses queries against the real `IndexWriter`-produced `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` segment `term_query_fixtures.rs`/`boolean_query_fixtures.rs` already validate, executes them via `search_boolean_query`, and confirms the result matches the equivalent hand-built `Clause` (`TermQuery`/`PhraseQuery`/nested `BooleanQuery`) executed the same way — proving the parser's output is not just structurally right but genuinely executes to the same doc set as the already-differentially-verified query layer. **Deferred, same as every other `Clause`-producing task**: no `lucene-ffi` C-ABI entry point accepts a query string yet (the FFI wire format still only builds flat `Clause::Term` clauses); no query-string support for `Clause::DisjunctionMax`/`Clause::ConstantScore` (real classic `QueryParser` has no direct syntax for either anyway — both are Java-API-only constructs). **Analyzer wiring (task #62)**: closes the gap the `lucene-analysis` row above previously flagged (nothing wired an `Analyzer` into this module). `parse_query` is unchanged and now delegates to a new additive entry point, `parse_query_with_analyzer(input, default_field, analyzer: Option<&lucene_analysis::Analyzer>)` — `None` reproduces every prior literal-term behavior exactly (all 41 pre-existing tests pass unmodified, plus a new test directly comparing `parse_query`'s and `parse_query_with_analyzer(.., None)`'s output). When an analyzer is supplied it runs over a bareword's text before `Clause::Term`, and over each whitespace-separated word of a quoted phrase before `Clause::Phrase` (real `QueryParser` analyzes phrase text word-by-word, not as one blob), but **never** over wildcard/prefix/fuzzy/regexp pattern text — matching real classic `QueryParser`, which doesn't analyze pattern syntax either, since tokenizing/lowercasing/stopword-filtering a glob or regex would corrupt it (verified with pattern text containing uppercase letters and a stopword-shaped substring that must survive untouched). Zero/one/multi-token-per-word handling (a deliberately simplified subset of real `QueryParserBase.newFieldQuery`'s fuller handling, which can also build position-aware `SynonymQuery`s — out of scope): one token → `Clause::Term`/one phrase position; zero tokens (the word analyzed away entirely, e.g. it was itself a stopword) → an empty `BooleanQuery` (no `must`/`should`/`must_not`), already this crate's established "matches nothing" shape per `matched_boolean_docs`'s own doc comment, so no new `Clause` variant was needed; more than one token → `Clause::Phrase` in order (bareword) or spliced into the phrase's term list (one phrase word). No new Java fixture — this composes two already independently cross-engine-verified pieces (this row's own parser grammar, the `lucene-analysis` row's analyzer chain); the added zero/one/multi-token control flow is new Rust-level logic covered directly by unit tests, not new byte-format decoding. **Numeric range syntax (`PointRangeQuery`'s classic-`QueryParser` grammar)**: `field:[min TO max]` now parses (inclusive both ends) into a new leaf `crate::query::Clause::PointsRange(PointsRangeQuery)` carrying `field`/`min: i64`/`max: i64`. The `[`/`{`-range syntax that was previously always a `ParseError::UnsupportedSyntax` is now split: `[min TO max]` parses; `{min TO max}` (exclusive) and any mixed `[`/`{` bracket combination still reject with `ParseError::UnsupportedSyntax`, exactly as before — **inclusive-only, exclusive bounds explicitly deferred**. Either bound may be `*` (mapped to `i64::MIN`/`i64::MAX`, real Lucene's own open-end convention) or a plain, optionally-negative decimal integer; a non-numeric bound, a missing/misspelled `TO`, or a missing closing `]` is a new `ParseError::InvalidRangeBound` rather than a panic or a silently-wrong clause. Only `i64` bounds are supported — string/date range queries (non-numeric bounds, real `TermRangeQuery`'s territory) are also `ParseError::InvalidRangeBound`, not a fallback to lexicographic comparison. **Parsing only — execution deliberately NOT wired in this task.** No `resolve_clause_docs`/`clause_scores`/`explain_clause` arm resolves a `Clause::PointsRange` against a real segment: each of those three exhaustive matches gained a `Clause::PointsRange` arm that returns a new `Error::UnexecutablePointsRange(field)` rather than silently matching nothing, since "parsed but not executable" is a real, caller-visible gap, not an empty-result query. The already-existing `crate::points_query::search_points_range` (single-segment `PointsReader`-based BKD range resolver, see that module's own row) is the intended eventual callee — wiring it in requires reconstructing a segment's `PointsReader` alongside the `BlockTreeFields`/`DocInput` every `resolve_clause_docs` caller already opens, plus per-field numeric encoding (packing an `i64` bound into `search_points_range`'s big-endian `min_packed`/`max_packed` convention), neither of which this task added; tracked as a clean, well-scoped follow-on. Covered by new unit tests in `query_parser.rs`: inclusive range with plain bounds, negative bounds, `*` on either/both ends, bare (no `field:`) range using the default field, boosted range, and every malformed shape (non-numeric bound, missing `TO`, lowercase `to`, missing closing `]`, missing bound, exclusive `{}` still rejected) — plus new `lib.rs`/`explain.rs` unit tests pinning the new `Error::UnexecutablePointsRange` path for `search_boolean_query`/`search_boolean_query_scored`/`explain_clause`. |

| `search/IndexSearcher` constructed with an `ExecutorService` (concurrent per-leaf search) | `lucene-search/src/multi_segment.rs::{merge_multi_segment_scored_concurrent, search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent, search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent}` | **ported (task #68), a `rayon`-based parallel sibling of the existing sequential fan-out/merge core — not a port of real `IndexSearcher`'s `Executor`/`LeafSlice` machinery itself.** Real Lucene's `IndexSearcher(IndexReader, Executor)` constructor searches each `LeafReaderContext` (or `LeafSlice` group of leaves) on the supplied `Executor`, then merges the partial `TopDocs` once every leaf finishes. This port has no thread-pool abstraction of its own, and `rayon` is already a workspace dependency used elsewhere in this crate, so `merge_multi_segment_scored_concurrent` uses `rayon::prelude::*`'s `par_iter` over segments in place of an `Executor`: each segment's `TopDocsCollector`, per-segment search call, and doc-base translation run independently inside the parallel closure (no shared mutable state between segments, so no locking needed), producing one `Vec<ScoreDoc>` per segment. Those per-segment vectors are then merged **sequentially**, through the identical `TopDocsCollector` type [`merge_multi_segment_scored`] (the pre-existing sequential core, unchanged by this task) already uses for its own merge step — the same merge logic, not a second implementation of it, and `rayon`'s `.collect()` preserving input order regardless of which worker thread computed which element is what makes the two paths' outputs provably identical rather than merely usually-the-same. `search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent` are thin wrappers mirroring the existing `search_term_query_multi_segment`/`search_boolean_query_multi_segment` exactly, differing only in which core they call. **Additive only**: the pre-existing sequential functions (`merge_multi_segment_scored`, `search_term_query_multi_segment`, `search_boolean_query_multi_segment`) and all of their tests are unchanged. **Verified**: sequential and concurrent results are asserted byte-for-byte identical (same doc IDs, same order, same scores — `assert_eq!`, not an epsilon compare) for the same input across an empty index (zero segments), a single segment, 16 synthetic segments (enough for rayon's global pool to plausibly run more than one in parallel), a `top_n`-truncation case, a case where every segment ties on score at the same local doc ID (exercising the cross-segment tie-break through the concurrent path too), and both real end-to-end query types (term, boolean) against the real `fixtures/data/blocktree_index/` fixture. **Explicitly deferred**: any thread-pool configuration/sizing knob (real Lucene's `Executor` lets a caller supply an arbitrarily sized/shaped pool; this always uses rayon's process-global pool, with no equivalent knob exposed), work-stealing tuning beyond what that global pool already provides out of the box, and any I/O-bound async concern — this is CPU-parallel per-segment scorer evaluation only. ~~No `lucene-ffi` C-ABI entry point exposes the concurrent path yet~~ — closed by the Concurrent segment search FFI exposure task: `lucene-ffi/src/directory_reader.rs::{ffi_search_term_query_multi_segment_concurrent, ffi_search_boolean_query_multi_segment_concurrent}` (see the `directory_reader.rs` row below for that FFI wiring's own details). |

| `search/IndexSearcher.explain(Query, int)` + `search/Explanation` | `lucene-search/src/explain.rs::{Explanation, explain_clause}` | **ported (task #59), introspection only — does not change any scoring behavior.** `Explanation { matched, value, description, details }` mirrors real `Explanation` exactly (`matched` stands in for `isMatch()`; `Explanation::match_(value, description)`/`.with_details(vec)` and `Explanation::no_match(description)` mirror the real `Explanation.match(...)`/`Explanation.noMatch(...)` factory split). `explain_clause(fields, doc_in, pos_in, pay_in, live_docs, clause, doc, norms)` recomputes each node's `value` via the *exact same* `similarity::idf`/`similarity::tf_norm` calls (and the same `term_doc_freqs`/`term_doc_positions`/`phrase_freq_exact`/`matched_boolean_docs`/`resolve_clause_docs` helpers) `search_term_query_scored`/`search_boolean_query_scored`/`search_phrase_query_scored`/`search_disjunction_max_query_scored` already call — its top-level `value` is bit-for-bit identical to those functions' own output for the same doc, verified directly (`assert_eq!`, not an epsilon compare) in this module's own unit tests rather than re-derived independently. **Detailed explanations** (weight → score → idf/tfNorm sub-trees, or the query's own composition formula): `Clause::Term` (idf with `docFreq`/`docCount` leaf details, tfNorm with `freq`/`k1`/`b`/`fieldLength`/`avgFieldLength` leaf details), `Clause::Phrase` (same shape, phrase idf = sum of each term's own idf, tfNorm keyed on phrase frequency), `Clause::Boolean` (sum of matching `must`/`should` sub-clause explanations, `no_match` when a `must` clause fails, `minimum_should_match` isn't met, or the query has no `must`/`should` clauses at all), `Clause::DisjunctionMax` (real `max + tie_breaker * sum(rest)` formula over matching disjuncts' own explanations), `Clause::ConstantScore` (matches iff the wrapped clause matches, always reports the constant, discarding the wrapped clause's own score), `Clause::Boost` (wrapped clause's own explanation value multiplied by `boost`). **Flat explanations** ("1.0 = matches, unscored constant score" or a clean `no_match`, no per-term breakdown): `Clause::Wildcard`/`Clause::Prefix`/`Clause::Fuzzy`/`Clause::Regexp`/`Clause::Span` — same "no single term's frequency/idf to score against" rationale each query type's own `query.rs` doc comment already gives for why they score a flat `1.0`. No new Java fixture generator needed (per the `differential-testing` skill's precedent for presentation-layer logic over already-differentially-verified scoring — there's no "real Lucene bytes" to check a description string against, only the numeric equality this task's tests assert directly against this crate's own already-verified ground truth). Coverage: `lucene-search/src/explain.rs` 97.82% lines (workspace total 97.28% lines, `cargo llvm-cov --fail-under-lines 95` passing). |
